Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
6 min
Timing of Intention for Voluntary and Non-Mu'ayyan Fasts
Explains ruling that intention can be made in first half of day for voluntary fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible timing of intention for voluntary fasts in the Hanafi school and explain why intention after zawal is invalid.

Core Idea
For voluntary fasts, intention can be made up to half the day but not after zawal.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on when intention (niyyah) must be made for fasting. While many assume intention is always required before dawn, the Hanafi school makes a distinction: for voluntary fasts and non-mu'ayyan obligatory fasts, intention can be made in the first half of the day. However, for qada and nazr mu'ayyan, intention must be at night. The reasoning relies on the nature of fasting as a single extended pillar and the legal principle that the majority of the day stands for the whole.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making intention for a fast. For voluntary fasts, the ruling is that intention can be made after dawn but before nisf al-nahar (half the day) or before zawal (zenith). For qada and nazr mu'ayyan, intention must be made the night before.
2
Locate the dalil and reasoning
The proof is based on the nature of fasting as a single extended pillar (rukn wahid mumtadd) and the principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole (al-kathir yattahiku bi al-kull). This is an example of qiyas and istihsan.
The text contrasts fasting with prayer and Hajj, which have multiple discrete pillars requiring intention at the start of each.
3
Analyze the exceptions
Qada and nazr mu'ayyan are exceptions: they require intention at night because those days are not originally prescribed for voluntary fasting; the obligation is already established. Therefore, merely refraining from dawn without prior intention does not create a valid fast.
For voluntary fasts, the day is considered 'empty' of obligation, so intention can be made later.
4
Determine the time limit for voluntary fasts
Intention for voluntary fasts must be made before zawal. After zawal, the majority of the day has passed without intention, so the principle of majority no longer applies, and the fast is invalid.
Some texts say before nisf al-nahar; Al-Hidayah reconciles this by stating that most of the day is before zawal.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that for voluntary fasts, intention can be made before nisf al-nahar, and for qada and nazr mu'ayyan, intention must be at night. This is the view in Zahir al-Riwayah and preferred by Al-Marghinani.
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intention must be at night for all obligatory fasts, including Ramadan.

موقوف ہے پس اگر اس نے آئندہ روزہ کی نیت کر لی اور ابھی دن کا زیادہ حصہ باقی ہے تو کہا جائے گا کہ دن کے اول حصہ کا امساک بھی روزہ ہے اور اگر آئندہ افطار کی نیت کی تو کہا جائے گا کہ ابتداء کا امساک بھی صوم نہیں تھا پس معلوم ہوا کہ ابتداء کا امساک آئندہ کی نیت پر موقوف ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ابتدائے دن کے امساک کا آئندہ کی نیت پر موقوف ہونا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ صوم ایک رکن ہے البتہ دراز ہے اب اس میں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ بدر کنا عادت کے طور پر ہو۔ پس یہ متعین کرنا کہ یہ امساک خالص اللہ کے لئے ہے اور یہ عبادت کی طور پر ہے نہ کہ عادت کے طور پر نیت ہی سے ہوسکتا ہے اس لئے کہا گیا کہ ابتدائے دن کا امساک آئندہ کی نیت پر موقوف ہے اب یہ نیست اگر دن کے اکثر حصہ میں پائی گئی تو چونکہ اکثر کل کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے اس لئے کثرت کی وجہ سے جانب وجود کو جانب عدم پر ترجیح دیکر کہا جائے گا کہ نیت پورے دن میں پائی گئی ہے اور جب پورے دن میں نیت پائی گئی ہے تو روزہ درست ہو گا پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ روزہ کی رات میں نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف نماز اور حج کہ ان دونوں میں ابتداء سے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے ان دونوں کے اندر لاکثر حکم الکل کا قاعدہ جاری نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ ان دونوں کے کئی کئی ارکان ہیں چنانچہ نماز میں قیام، رکوع ، سجدہ، قرات قرآن وغیرہ ارکان ہیں اور حج میں وقوف عرفہ اور طواف ارکان ہیں اب اگر تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت اول نماز کی نیت نہ کی گئی اور احرام کے وقت اول حج میں حج کی نیت نہیں کی گئی تو بعض ارکان بغیر نیت کے رہ جائیں گے اور جوار کان بغیر نیت کے ادا ہوئے باطل ہیں اور بغیر ان ارکان کے نماز اور حج ادا نہ ہوں گے اس لئے ان دونوں کے شروع میں نیست کرنا ضروری ہے بعد میں اگر نیت کی گئی تو وہ معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ بِخِلَافِ الْقَضاءِ .. الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے سوال یہ ہے کہ روزہ اگر رکن واحد ممتد ہے اور زوال سے پہلے پہلے نیت کرنا جائز ہے تو قضاء رمضان میں بھی زوال سے پہلے پہلے نیت جائز ہونی چاہئے تھی حالانکہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ قضاء رمضان میں رات میں نیت کرنا شرط ہے جواب یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے علاوہ اور نذرمعین کے روزہ کے علاوہ تمام ایام نفلی روزہ کے لئے مشروع ہیں سوائے ایام منہی عنہا کے یعنی شریعت نے اس دن کا روزہ اس پر لازم نہیں کیا الا یہ کہ وہ نفلی روزہ رکھے پس رمضان اور نذر معین کے ایام کے علاوہ میں امساک یعنی کھانے پینے اور جماع سے رکنا اسی دن کے روزہ پر موقوف ہوگا اور اس دن کا روزہ نفلی ہے لہذا اس دن کا روز فعلی شمار ہوگا الا یہ کہ شروع دن سے یعنی صبح صادق ہی سے قضاء وغیرہ کے روزہ کی نیت کر لی ہو پس ثابت ہوا کہ قضاء کے روزہ کی نیت رات میں کرنا شرط ہے اگر صبح صادق کے بعد زوال سے پہلے نیت کی گئی تو معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ وَبَخِلافِ مَابَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ ... الخ سے بھی ایک سوال کا جواب ہے سوال یہ ہے کہ جب روزہ رکن واحد متد ہے تو نیت کا قرآن دن کے قلیل اور کثیر دونوں کی ساتھ برابر ہونا چاہئے یعنی نیت دن کے اکثر حصہ میں پائی جائے یا کم حصہ میں پائی جائے بایں طور کہ زوال کے بعد نیت کی ہو تو دونوں صورتوں میں روزہ درست ہونا چاہتے حالانکہ مابعد الزوال نیت کرنے کی صورت میں روزہ جائز نہیں ہوتا جواب : اصل تو یہ تھا کہ نیت دن کے شروع حصہ میں کی جاتی یعنی صبح صادق ہونے کے ساتھ ہی روزہ کی نیت کی جاتی لیکن اگر دن کے اکثر حصہ کے ساتھ نیت کا اقتران پایا گیا بہ ایں طور کہ زوال سے پہلے پہلے نیت کر لی گئی تو لیا کثر حکم الکل کے قاعدہ کی وجہ سے اس اصل کو ہم نے ترک کر دیا ہے اور چونکہ زوال کے بعد نیت کرنے کی صورت میں دن کے اکثر میں نیت نہیں پائی گئی اس لئے اس صورت میں جانب عدم رائج ہوگی اور یوں کہا جائیگا گویا کہ پورے دن نیت نہیں پائی گئی اور روزہ بغیر نیت کے رکھا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ بلانیت روز و معتبر نہیں ہوتا اس لئے ما بعد الزوال نیت کرنے کی صورت میں بھی روزہ معتبر نہ ہوگا۔
The chapter of fasting: The intention depends on the later part and accompanies most of the day, as in voluntary fasting. Therefore, if a person refrains from eating, drinking, and intercourse from dawn, this restraint depends on the later intention. So if he later intends fasting and most of the day remains, it is said that the restraint of the first part is also part of the fast. And if he later intends to break the fast, it is said that the initial restraint was not fasting. Thus the initial restraint depends on the later intention. The author of Hidayah says: The initial restraint's dependence on the later intention is because fasting is a single extended pillar. There is also the possibility that this restraint is out of habit. So specifying that this restraint is purely for Allah and as an act of worship, not out of habit, can only be through intention. Thus it is said that the initial restraint depends on the later intention. So if the intention occurs in most of the day, since the majority stands in place of the whole, we prefer existence over non-existence due to majority, and it is said that intention occurred for the whole day. When intention occurred for the whole day, the fast is valid. Thus it is proven that intention at night is not necessary for fasting. Contrary to prayer and Hajj, where intention at the beginning is necessary; in both, the rule of 'most of the whole' does not apply because both have multiple pillars: in prayer, standing, bowing, prostration, recitation, etc.; in Hajj, staying at Arafah and circumambulation are pillars. If intention is not made at the opening takbir for prayer or at the ihram for Hajj, some pillars would be without intention, and pillars performed without intention are invalid, and without those pillars prayer and Hajj are not fulfilled. Therefore, intention at the beginning of both is necessary; if intention is made later, it is not valid. As for qada (make-up fasts), it is the answer to a question: The question is: if fasting is a single extended pillar and intention before zawal is permissible, then in qada of Ramadan, intention before zawal should also be permissible, but it is not; rather, intention at night is a condition for qada of Ramadan. The answer is: Except for Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan, all days are prescribed for voluntary fasting, except prohibited days. That is, the Law does not impose fasting on that day unless one voluntarily fasts. So apart from Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan, the restraint is dependent on that day's fasting, and that day's fast is voluntary. Hence that day's fast will be considered voluntary unless from the beginning of the day, i.e., from true dawn, one intended qada, etc. So it is proven that for qada fast, intention at night is a condition; if intention is made after true dawn before zawal, it will not be valid. As for after zawal, it is the answer to another question: The question is: since fasting is a single extended pillar, the conjunction of intention with the day should be equal whether in a small or large part; i.e., whether intention is found in most of the day or in a small part, such as after zawal, in both cases the fast should be valid. Yet intention after zawal is not valid. The answer: Originally, intention should be made at the beginning of the day, i.e., simultaneously with true dawn. But if the intention accompanies most of the day, such that it is made before zawal, we deviate from this original rule because of the principle 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole'. And since in the case of intention after zawal, intention is not found in most of the day, in that case the side of non-existence prevails, and it is said that the intention is as if not found for the whole day, and the fast is kept without intention. Obviously, a fast without intention is invalid. Therefore, in the case of intention after zawal, the fast will also be invalid.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the timing of intention for voluntary and non-mu'ayyan fasts. The author begins by stating that intention can be made late, i.e., after the start of the day, and it must accompany most of the day. He illustrates with an example: if someone refrains from eating from dawn, that restraint depends on whether he later intends to fast or break it. This shows that the initial restraint is not inherently a fast; it becomes a fast only through subsequent intention. The reasoning is that fasting is a single extended pillar (rukn wahid mumtadd). Since the act may be due to habit, intention is needed to specify it as worship. If intention occurs in most of the day, the legal principle 'al-kathir yattahiku bi al-kull' (the majority is treated as the whole) applies, so the entire day is considered covered by intention. This principle does not apply to prayer and Hajj because they have multiple pillars; intention must accompany each pillar, so it must be at the start. Next, the passage addresses exceptions: qada (make-up) of Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan require intention at night because those fasts are already obligatory; the day is not originally for voluntary fasting. Therefore, merely refraining from dawn without prior intention is not sufficient. Another exception is intention after zawal: even for voluntary fasts, intention must be made before zawal because after zawal, most of the day has passed without intention, so the rule of the majority no longer applies. The overall ruling is that for voluntary and non-mu'ayyan obligatory fasts, intention can be made in the first half of the day, but not after zawal. For qada and nazr mu'ayyan, intention must be made the night before.

Key Terms
رکن واحد ممتد (rukn wahid mumtadd): A single extended pillar that continues over time, as opposed to discrete acts.
نیت (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on making intention for a voluntary fast after dawn but before zawal?
A) The fast is valid if intention is made before zawal.
B) The fast is valid only if intention is made at night.
C) The fast is valid only if intention is made exactly at dawn.
D) The fast is invalid regardless of when intention is made.

Key Takeaway
For voluntary fasts, intention can be made in the first half of the day, but for qada and nazr mu'ayyan, intention must be the night before.

Sawm — Fasting

The Intention Cutoff: Quduri vs. Jami' al-Saghir
Compares two texts on intention cutoff

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir texts on intention timing and state the mufta bihi cutoff time for Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan according to al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
For fasting, intention must be made before half of the shari day, not before zawal.

This lesson examines a key textual difference within the Hanafi school: the cutoff time for making intention when one failed to intend at night. Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah resolves this by preferring the text of Jami' al-Saghir, introducing the concept of the shari day (nahar shar'i). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Texts
Read the passage and note the two statements: Quduri says intention suffices up to zawal; Jami' al-Saghir says intention must be before half of the day (nisf al-nahar). Identify these as two transmitted positions within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the Shari vs. Customary Day
Grasp the difference: the shari day (nahar shar'i) runs from true dawn to sunset, while the customary day (nahar 'urfi) runs from sunrise to sunset. The half of the shari day occurs earlier than zawal—specifically at the end of forenoon (dahuwa kubra). This is key to why Jami' al-Saghir's text is more correct.
Example given in the passage: on Jan 8, shari day half is at 11:42 AM, while zawal is at 12:25 PM.
3
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Dispute and Preferred View
Note that Imam Zufar holds a stricter view: a traveler must intend at night. Also, the author of al-Hidayah declares Jami' al-Saghir's wording more correct (asahh). The mufta bihi position is that intention must be made before nisf al-nahar of the shari day, not before zawal.
This applies equally to residents and travelers for Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan, according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فِي الْمُختصر سے صاحب ہدایہ نے قدوری اور جامع صغیر کی عبارتوں کے فرق کو بیان فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ قدوری کا متن ہے إِذَا لَمْ يَنُو حَتَّى أَصْبَحَ أَجْزَانَتْهُ النِّيةُ مَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الزَّوَالِ یعنی اگر کسی نے رات میں نیت نہیں کی اور صبح ہوگئی تو وہ زوال یعنی سورج کے ڈھلنے سے پہلے پہلے نیت کرلے اور جامع صغیر کا متن ہے قَبلَ نِصْفِ النَّهارِ یعنی نصف نہار سے پہلے پہلے نیت کر لے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت زیادہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ روزہ میں نہار شرعی معتبر ہے نہ کہ نہار عرفی بنہار شرعی طلوع صبح صادق سے غروب تک ہوتا ہے اور نہار عرفی طلوع آفتاب سے غروب تک ہوتا ہے اور زوال کی ساعت نہار عرفی کا نصف ہوتا ہے نہ کہ نہار شرعی کا کیونکہ نہار شرعی کا نصف چاشت کے آخری وقت تک ہو جاتا ہے مثلا آج ۸ جنوری کو طلوع فجر پانچ بیچ کر اڑتالیس منٹ پر ہے اور غروب آفتاب پانچ بج کر چھتیس منٹ پر ہے اس کا نصف گیارہ بجکر بیالیس منٹ پر ہوگا تو یا جامع صغیر کے مطابق گیارہ بجکر بیالیس منٹ جو چاشت کا آخری وقت ہے جس کو ضحوۃ کبری گہا گیا ہے اس سے پہلے پہلے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ شرعی نہار کے اکثر حصہ میں نیت پائی جائے اور آج ۸ جنوری ۸ کو طلوع آفتاب سات بج کر ستر منٹ پر ہے اور غروب آفتاب پانچ بج کر چھتیس منٹ پر ہے اس کا نصف بارہ بجکر پچیس منٹ میں سکنڈ پر ہوگا گویا کہ قدوری کے مطابق بارہ بجکر چھپیں منٹ جس کو زوال کا وقت کہا گیا ہے اس سے پہلے پہلے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے جامع صغیر کے متن کو ا صبح اس لئے قرار دیا ہے کہ روزہ میں شرعی دن معتبر ہے اور شرعی دن کا نصف زوال کا وقت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ زوال کے وقت سے تقریباً ایک گھنٹہ پہلے ہو جاتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ رمضان اور نذرمعین کے روزہ کی نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے نیت کا معتبر ہونا مسافر اور متقیم دونوں کے حق میں برابر ہے کیونکہ جو دلیل بیان کی گئی ہے اس میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے البتہ امام زفر کے نزدیک مسافر کے لئے رات میں نیت کرنا شرط ہے صبح کے بعد نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے نیت معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ واجب معین کے لئے مطلق نیست کافی ہے
From 'qala fi al-Mukhtasar', the author of Hidayah explains the difference between the texts of Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir. He says: Quduri's text is 'When he did not intend until he rose (dawn), the intention suffices him between that and zawal', meaning if someone did not intend at night and dawn came, then he may intend before zawal, i.e., before the sun declines. And the text of Jami' al-Saghir is 'before half of the day', i.e., he intends before nisf al-nahar. The author of Hidayah says: The wording of Jami' al-Saghir is more correct because in fasting, the shari day is considered, not the customary day. The shari day is from true dawn to sunset, and the customary day is from sunrise to sunset. The hour of zawal is the half of the customary day, not of the shari day, because the half of the shari day occurs by the end of forenoon (chast). For example, on Jan 8, subh sadiq is at 5:48 AM and sunset at 5:36 PM; its half would be at 11:42 AM. So according to Jami' al-Saghir, one must intend before 11:42 AM, which is the end of forenoon (called dahuwa kubra). So that intention occurs in most of the shari day. And on Jan 8, sunrise is at 7:10 AM and sunset at 5:36 PM; its half is at 12:25 PM. So according to Quduri, one must intend before 12:25 PM, which is zawal time. The author of Hidayah preferred the text of Jami' al-Saghir because in fasting, the shari day is considered, and its half is not at zawal but about an hour before zawal. The author of Hidayah said that the validity of intention before nisf al-nahar for Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan is the same for both traveler and resident because the evidence given does not differentiate. However, according to Imam Zufar, for a traveler, intention at night is a condition; intention after dawn before nisf al-nahar is not valid. For a mu'ayyan obligatory fast, a general intention (mutlaq niyyah) is sufficient.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that parses the difference between two authoritative texts of the Hanafi school: the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad. The issue is the cutoff time for making intention for a fast when one did not intend at night. According to Quduri, intention can be made up to zawal (when the sun passes the meridian). According to Jami' al-Saghir, intention must be made before nisf al-nahar (half of the day). The author of Hidayah (al-Marghinani) declares Jami' al-Saghir's wording more correct because the fast is measured by the shari day (from true dawn to sunset), not the customary day (sunrise to sunset). The half of the shari day occurs well before zawal, specifically at the end of the forenoon (dhuha kubra). Therefore, to have intention cover most of the shari day, it must be made before this half, not before zawal. The passage also notes that this timing applies equally to travelers and residents for Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan, according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. However, Imam Zufar holds that a traveler must intend at night, and intention after dawn is not valid. Finally, for a mu'ayyan obligatory fast (like Ramadan), a general intention (mutlaq niyyah) suffices.

Key Terms
نہار شرعی (nahar shar'i): The legal day from true dawn (subh sadiq) to sunset.
ضحوۃ کبری (dahuwa kubra): The end of the forenoon, approximately the midpoint of the shari day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of Hidayah, which text is more correct regarding the cutoff time for intention?
A) The text of al-Quduri, which says before zawal.
B) The text of al-Jami' al-Saghir, which says before nisf al-nahar.
C) Both are equally correct.
D) Neither is correct; intention must be at night.

Key Takeaway
The correct cutoff for intention in Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan is half of the shari day, which occurs before zawal.

Intention for Ramadan: General Intention and the Rule of Laghat al-Jihah
Inter-madhhab dispute on intention with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf for traveler/sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that a general intention, a nafl intention, or another wajib intention suffices for the Ramadan fast, and apply the principle of 'laghati al-jihah' to explain why, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the traveler and sick.

Core Idea
For a specific obligatory fast like Ramadan, the essence of intention suffices; extra specifications drop away.

This passage from the Hidayah engages in a key inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over the validity of a general intention for the Ramadan fast. The Hanafi school holds that the fast is fulfilled even with a general intention or an intention for another fast (nafl or wajib) because the act itself is specified. The passage then explores an intra-Hanafi difference: does the same ruling apply to a traveler or sick person? Understanding these distinctions clarifies the Hanafi methodology of intention and dispensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the opposing position
Read the passage and note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intending nafl invalidates the fast for Ramadan because it shows turning away from the fard. Identify the two parts of the dispute: first, general intention / nafl intention vs. Shafi'i; second, the intra-Hanafi difference on traveler/sick.
Shafi'i has two statements on general intention; the text mentions this but doesn't detail both.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi proof is an analogy (qiyas): just as a person in a house is addressed by his generic name and responds, so the basic intention of fasting ('asl al-sawm') covers the specific Ramadan fast. The extra specification becomes redundant (lagh).
This is a key principle: 'laghati al-jihah' – the additional aspect drops off.
3
Apply the principle to the examples
Consider a person who wakes up on a Ramadan day and intends 'I am fasting a nafl today'. According to Hanafi, the nafl intention drops away, and the fast counts for Ramadan. Similarly, if one intends to fast a missed wajib (qada) on a Ramadan day, it counts for that wajib (according to Abu Hanifa).
4
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on traveler/sick
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the dispensation for travel/sickness is such that if a traveler or sick person undertakes the fast, they are like a resident. So if they intend another wajib (e.g., qada) on a Ramadan day, it counts for that wajib, not Ramadan. Abu Hanifa also holds it counts for the other wajib, but with a different rationale: they prioritized the more important duty. For nafl intention, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
Note the practical difference: for a traveler/sick person, Sahibayn make no distinction between them and resident/healthy; Abu Hanifa has a specific ruling about prioritizing the more important.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical outcome: According to Hanafi, a Muslim who makes a general intention (e.g., 'I am fasting today') during Ramadan has fulfilled the obligation, even if he did not specify Ramadan. He does not need to make up the day. This leniency is based on the principle that the specific duty is automatically intended.
This differs from Shafi'i who requires specification. For traveler/sick, the mufta bihi is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (no difference between them and others).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُذَا الضَّرْبُ مِنَ الصَّوْمِ يَتَادَى بِمُطلَقَ النِّيَّةِ وَبِنِيَّةِ النَّفْلِ وَبِيَّةِ وَاجِب أَخَرَ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِى نِيَّةِ التَّفْل عَابِتُ وَفِي مُطْلَقِهَا لَهُ قَوْلَان لأنَّهُ بِنِيَةِ النَّقْلِ مُعْرِضُ عَنِ الْقَرْضِ فَلَا يَكُونُ لَهُ الْفَرْضُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الفَرضَ مُتَعَينَ فِيهِ فَيُصَابٌ بِأصْلِ النَّبِيَّةِ كَالْمُتَوَحِدِ فِى الدَّارِ يُصَابُ بِاسْمِ جِنْسِهِ وَإِذَا نَوى النَّفْلَ أَوْ وَاحِبًا أَخَرَ فَقَدْ نَوَى أَصْلَ الصَّوْمِ وَ زِيَادَةِ جِهَةٍ وَقَدْ لَغَتِ الْجِهَةُ فَبَقِيَ الْأصْلُ وَهُوَ كافٍ وَلَا فَرقَ بَيْنَ الْمُسَافِرِ وَالْمُقِيمِ وَالصَّحِيح وَ السَّقِيمِ عِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّ الرُّحْصَةَ كَيْلَا تَلْزَمُ الْمَعْدُورَ مُشَقَّةٌ فَإِذَا تَحَمَلَهَا الْتَحَقَ بِغَيْرِ الْمَعْدُورِ وَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ إِذَا صَامَ الْمَرِيضُ وَالْمُسَافِرُ بِنِيَّةِ وَاجِبِ أَخَرَ يَقَعُ عَنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ شَعَلَ الْوَقْتَ بِالْاهُمْ لِتَحقِّقِهِ فِى الْحَالِ وَتَحْتِرِدٍ فِي صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ إِلى إِدْرَابِ العِدَّةِ وَعَنْهُ فِي نِيَّةِ التَّطَوُّعِ رِوَايَتَانِ والفَرَقُ عَلَى أَحَدِهِمَا اللَّهُ مَا صَرَفَ الْوَقْتَ إلى الاهم
And this type of fast is fulfilled by a general intention, by an intention of voluntary (nafl), and by an intention of another obligatory (wajib). Al-Shafi'i said: regarding intention for voluntary, it is [؟] and regarding general intention, he has two statements, because by intending voluntary one turns away from the obligatory, so the obligatory is not achieved. Our (Hanafi) evidence is that the obligatory is specified in it, so it is attained by the basic intention, like a solitary person in a house who is addressed by his generic name. And when he intends voluntary or another wajib, he has intended the essence of fasting (asl al-sawm) and an additional aspect, and the additional aspect becomes redundant (lagh), so the essence remains, which is sufficient. And there is no difference between traveler and resident, healthy and sick according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because the dispensation (rukhsah) is such that hardship does not necessitate it for the excused; if he undertakes it, he joins the non-excused. And according to Abu Hanifa, if a sick person or traveler fasts with the intention of another wajib, it will fall from him (i.e., be valid for the intended wajib) because he occupied the time with the more important due to its actual existence and [؟] in fasting of Ramadan until completion of the number. And from him (Abu Hanifa) regarding intention for voluntary, there are two narrations, and the difference according to one of them is that Allah diverted the time to the more important.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the sufficiency of a general intention for the Ramadan fast. The Hanafi position is that for a mu'ayyan wajib fast like Ramadan, the fast is valid with a general intention (mutlaq niyyah), with an intention of nafl, or even with an intention of another wajib. This is because the fast is essentially a specific duty; the intention of the basic act (asl al-sawm) is sufficient. The additional specification (e.g., nafl) is redundant and drops away, leaving the essence. Al-Shafi'i disagrees: if one intends nafl, he is turning away from the obligatory, so it doesn't count for the fard. He also has two statements on general intention. The Hanafi proof is analogical: just as someone in a house is addressed by his generic name and responds, so the basic intention covers the specific duty. The passage then moves to the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the traveler and sick person. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, when a traveler or sick person intends another wajib (like making up a missed fast), it counts for that wajib and not for the current day's Ramadan; but they hold that there is no difference between them and a resident/healthy person in terms of validity – the fast is valid. According to Abu Hanifa, if a traveler or sick person fasts with the intention of another wajib, it will count for that wajib because he gave priority to the more important duty (the other wajib) over the current one, and he will complete the Ramadan fast later. For intention of voluntary (nafl) by a traveler/sick, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. The passage ends with a reference to one of them: that Allah diverted the time to the more important.

Key Terms
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): A general intention to fast without specifying the type (e.g., intending 'to fast' without naming Ramadan or nafl).
لَغَتِ الْجِهَةُ (laghati al-jihah): The additional aspect of intention (e.g., specifying nafl) becomes redundant and drops off, leaving the basic intention intact.
رخصة (rukhsah): A legal dispensation; in this context, the permission for travelers and sick to not fast during Ramadan and make up later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person intends to fast a voluntary (nafl) fast on a day of Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is for nafl and he must make up the Ramadan day later.
B) The fast counts for the Ramadan obligation.
C) The fast is invalid because he did not specify Ramadan.
D) The fast is valid for both nafl and Ramadan simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Ramadan fast is fulfilled by any basic intention to fast, including general, nafl, or another wajib intention, due to the principle of laghati al-jihah.

Sawm — Fasting

Time of Intention for Ramadan and Fixed Vows
Explains correct intention time before half of shari'i day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct time for intention in Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan fasts according to the Hanafi school, and explain why half of the shari'i day is preferred over zawal.

Core Idea
The intention for an obligatory fixed fast must be made before half the shari'i day, not at zawal.

The timing of niyyah (intention) for Ramadan and fixed vows (nazr mu'ayyan) is a subtle but decisive issue. While many assume that intention is valid up to noon (zawal), the relied-upon Hanafi position sets an earlier limit: half of the shari'i day. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that limit, resolving an apparent textual conflict between two foundational Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual conflict
Al-Quduri states intention suffices until zawal (noon). Al-Jami' al-Saghir states intention must be before half the day. Recognize that these two texts define the day differently.
The difference is not about the rule itself but about the definition of 'day' in shari'ah.
2
Understand the two types of day
The shari'i day (nahar shar'i) runs from true dawn (fajr sadiq) to sunset. The customary day (nahar 'urfi) runs from sunrise to sunset. Their midpoints are different.
Zawal is the midpoint of the customary day, not the shari'i day.
3
Analyze the proof for half of shari'i day
Since intention must be present in most of the day, and the shari'i day is longer than the customary day, its midpoint occurs earlier. Therefore, intention must be made before that midpoint to ensure it covers most of the day.
This is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on the definition of the day.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on the traveler
Imam Zufar holds that a traveler must intend at night; intention after dawn is invalid. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that both resident and traveler may intend until half the day.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows the majority.
5
State the final ruling
For Ramadan and nazr mu'ayyan, intention is valid until half the shari'i day (which occurs before zawal). This applies equally to resident and traveler, though it is best to intend at night.
The Hidayah prefers the view of al-Jami' al-Saghir.

کا نصف چاشت کے آخری وقت تک ہو جاتا ہے مثلا آج ۸ جنوری کو طلوع فجر پانچ بیچ کر اڑتالیس منٹ پر ہے اور غروب آفتاب پانچ بج کر چھتیس منٹ پر ہے اس کا نصف گیارہ بج کر بیالیس منٹ پر ہوگا تو یا جامع صغیر کے مطابق گیارہ بج کر بیالیس منٹ جو چاشت کا آخری وقت ہے جس کو ضحوۃ کبری گہا گیا ہے اس سے پہلے پہلے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ شرعی نہار کے اکثر حصہ میں نیت پائی جائے اور آج ۸ جنوری ۸ کو طلوع آفتاب سات بج کر ہدایہ نے کہا کہ رمضان اور نذرمعین کے روزہ کی نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے نیت کا معتبر ہونا مسافر اور متقیم دونوں کے حق میں برابر ہے کیونکہ جو دلیل بیان کی گئی ہے اس میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے البتہ امام زفر کے نزدیک مسافر کے لئے رات میں نیت کرنا شرط ہے صبح کے بعد نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے نیت معتبر نہ ہوگی۔
It has been left, and since when intention is made after zawal, intention is not found in most of the day, therefore in this case the side of non-existence will prevail, and it will be said that as if intention was not found for the entire day, and he observed the fast without intention. And it is obvious that a fast without intention is not valid. Therefore, even in the case of making intention after zawal, the fast will not be valid. He (author) said: From al-Mukhtasar, the author of Hidayah has explained the difference between the expressions of al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir. He said: The text of al-Quduri is: 'If he did not intend until morning, the intention between him and zawal suffices him.' That is, if someone did not intend at night and morning came, then he may make intention before zawal, i.e., before the sun's decline. The text of al-Jami' al-Saghir is: 'Before half of the day.' That is, he should make intention before half the day. The author of Hidayah says that the expression of al-Jami' al-Saghir is more correct because in fasting, the shari'i day is considered, not the customary day. The shari'i day is from dawn to sunset, and the customary day is from sunrise to sunset. The hour of zawal is the middle of the customary day, not the middle of the shari'i day, because the middle of the shari'i day occurs until the end of the forenoon (chast). For example, today, January 8, dawn is at 5:48 AM and sunset is at 5:36 PM, its mid-point will be at 11:42 AM. So according to al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is necessary to make intention before 11:42 AM, which is the end of the forenoon, called الضحوۃ الكبرى, so that intention is found in most of the shari'i day. And today, January 8, sunrise is at 7:10 AM and sunset is at 5:36 PM, its mid-point will be at 12:25 PM. So according to al-Quduri, it is necessary to make intention before 12:25 PM, which is called the time of zawal. The author of Hidayah considered the text of al-Jami' al-Saghir as correct because in fasting, the shari'i day is considered, and the middle of the shari'i day is not the time of zawal, but rather occurs about one hour before zawal. The author of Hidayah said: The validity of intention before half of the day for the fast of Ramadan and fixed vow is equal for both the traveler and the resident, because the proof that has been cited has no detail. However, according to Imam Zufar, intention at night is a condition for the traveler; intention after morning and before half of the day will not be valid.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time for making intention (niyyah) for an obligatory fixed fast (Ramadan or nazr mu'ayyan). The author of al-Hidayah discusses a textual difference between al-Quduri's text and al-Jami' al-Saghir. Al-Quduri's text allows intention up to zawal (noon), while al-Jami' al-Saghir requires intention before half the day. Al-Marghinani (author of al-Hidayah) prefers the latter because in Shar'i law, the day (nahar) runs from true dawn (fajr sadiq) to sunset, and half of that occurs before zawal, roughly at the end of the forenoon (duha). Therefore, to ensure intention is present in the majority of the day, intention must be made before half the shari'i day. The ruling applies equally to traveler and resident, as the proof does not differentiate. However, Imam Zufar holds that the traveler must intend at night, and intention after dawn does not suffice. The Hanafi mu'tamad (operative ruling) is that both traveler and resident may intend until half the day for Ramadan and fixed vows, but it is better to intend at night.

Key Terms
نہار شرعی (nahar shar'i): The legal day in fasting, from true dawn (fajr sadiq) to sunset.
نہار عرفی (nahar 'urfi): The customary day, from sunrise to sunset.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith (noon).
نصف النہار (nisf al-nahar): Half of the shari'i day; the time before which intention must be made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Until half of the shari'i day
C) Until zawal (noon)
D) Until sunset

Key Takeaway
Intention for Ramadan and fixed vows must be made before half the shari'i day (before zawal), and this applies equally to residents and travelers, though Imam Zufar differs on travelers.

Validity of Alternative Intentions for Ramadan Fast
Inter-madhhab dispute on intention in Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a Ramadan fast is valid with any fasting intention, distinguish the Shafi'i position, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on sickness and travel.

Core Idea
The specificity of Ramadan's time makes any intention to fast sufficient for its fulfillment.

This passage addresses a key point in the fiqh of sawm: what happens if a person intends a supererogatory (nafl) fast or another obligatory fast during the month of Ramadan? The Hanafi school holds that the fast is valid as the Ramadan fast, while the Shafi'i school disagrees. We will explore the proofs, the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and an important nuance regarding fixed vows.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Clearly state that the Ramadan fast is valid with an absolute intention (e.g., 'I will fast tomorrow'), a nafl intention, or any other wajib intention. The root intention of fasting suffices because the day is specific to Ramadan.
This is the madhhab's ruling; the specific type intended becomes void.
2
Identify the Opposing View and Its Proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that intending nafl is a turning away from the obligatory fast, effectively nullifying intention entirely. For absolute intention, he has two opinions. Understand the logic behind his position.
Malik and Ahmad agree with Shafi'i on nafl intention.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi proof: the obligatory fast (Ramadan) is fixed to that time, just as a person alone in a house is identified by his generic name. The root intention of fasting is enough; the additional specification (nafl, qada) is void and does not affect the root.
The analogy with the lone resident is a key reasoning tool.
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
For a traveler or sick person who intends another wajib (e.g., qada), Abu Hanifa holds it counts as that other wajib, because the time can be used for either obligation. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it counts as Ramadan, as the concession for travel/sickness is optional.
Also note two narrations from Abu Hanifa on nafl intention.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi can make a general intention and fulfill Ramadan, while a Shafi'i must specify Ramadan. For a traveler, the mufta bihi is not settled; both views are considered, but caution recommends the Sahibayn's view.
Additionally, a fixed vow (nazr mu'ayyan) does NOT accept intention of another wajib, unlike Ramadan.

وَاجِب مَعِين کے لئے مطلق نیست کافی ہے وَهُذَا الضَّرْبُ مِنَ الصَّوْمِ يَتَادَى بِمُطلَقَ النِّيَّةِ وَبِنِيَّةِ النَّفْلِ وَبِيَّةِ وَاجِب أَخَرَ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِى نِيَّةِ التَّفْل عَابِتُ وَفِي مُطْلَقِهَا لَهُ قَوْلَان لأنَّهُ بِنِيَةِ النَّقْلِ مُعْرِضُ عَنِ الْقَرْضِ فَلَا يَكُونُ لَهُ الْفَرْضُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الفَرضَ مُتَعَينَ فِيهِ فَيُصَابٌ بِأصْلِ النَّبِيَّةِ كَالْمُتَوَحِدِ فِى الدَّارِ يُصَابُ بِاسْمِ جِنْسِهِ وَإِذَا نَوى النَّفْلَ أَوْ وَاحِبًا أَخَرَ فَقَدْ نَوَى أَصْلَ الصَّوْمِ وَ زِيَادَةِ جِهَةٍ وَقَدْ لَغَتِ الْجِهَةُ فَبَقِيَ الْأصْلُ وَهُوَ كافٍ وَلَا فَرقَ بَيْنَ الْمُسَافِرِ وَالْمُقِيمِ وَالصَّحِيح وَ السَّقِيمِ عِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّ الرُّحْصَةَ كَيْلَا تَلْزَمُ الْمَعْدُورَ مُشَقَّةٌ فَإِذَا تَحَمَلَهَا الْتَحَقَ بِغَيْرِ الْمَعْدُورِ وَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ إِذَا صَامَ الْمَرِيضُ وَالْمُسَافِرُ بِنِيَّةِ وَاجِبِ أَخَرَ يَقَعُ عَنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ شَعَلَ الْوَقْتَ بِالْاهُمْ لِتَحقِّقِهِ فِى الْحَالِ وَتَحْتِرِدٍ فِي صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ إِلى إِدْرَابِ العِدَّةِ وَعَنْهُ فِي نِيَّةِ التَّطَوُّعِ رِوَايَتَانِ والفَرَقُ عَلَى أَحَدِهِمَا اللَّهُ مَا صَرَفَ الْوَقْتَ إلى الاهم . تشریح متا ہے کہ روزہ کی یہ قسم یعنی واجب معین مطلق نیست سے بھی ادا ہو جاتا ہے اور نفل کی نیت سے بھی اور واجب آخر کی نیت سے بھی مصنف قدوری کی عبارت میں تھوڑا سا جھول ہے اس طور پر کہ واجب معین میں رمضان کا روزہ اور نذر معین کا روزہ دونوں داخل ہیں تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ جس طرح رمضان کا روزہ مطلق نیست نفل کی نیت اور واجب آخر کی نیت سے ادا ہو جاتا ہے، اسی طرح نذر معین کا روزہ بھی مذکورہ نیتوں سے ادا ہو جائے گا۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں، کیونکہ نذر معین کا روزہ مطلق نیت اور نفل کی نیت سے تو ادا ہو جاتا ہے مگر واجب آخر مثلاً قضاء یا کفار کی نیت سے ادا نہیں ہوتا بلکہ نذرمعین والے دن اگر رات ہی میں کسی واجب آخر کی نیت کر لی تو واجب آخر ادا ہو گا نہ کہ نذر معین کا روزہ بہر حال احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ رمضان کا روزہ مطلق نیت سے بھی ادا ہو جائے گا مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں کل آئندہ روزہ رکھوں گا اور نفل کی نیت سے بھی ادا ہو جائے گا مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں کل آئندہ نفلی روزہ رکھوں گا اور واجب آخر کی نیت سے بھی ادا ہو جائے گا مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں کل آئندہ کفارہ کا یا گذشتہ سال کے رمضان کی قضا کا روزہ رکھوں گا۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ رمضان میں اگر نفلی روزہ کی نیت کی تو نہ رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہوگا اور نہ نفل کا بلکہ اس دن کا امساک فاقہ ہوگا کیونکہ رمضان کے روزہ کی تو نیت نہیں کی ہے۔ اور نفلی روزہ کا وقت نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ کوئی روزہ شمار نہ ہوگا اور اگر رمضان میں مطلقاً روزہ کی نیت کی تو اس میں امام شافعی کے دو قول ہیں ایک یہ کہ مطلق نیت سے رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہو جائے گا دوم یہ کہ روزہ رمضان ادا نہ ہو گا۔ یہی امام مالک اور امام احمد کا قول ہے اس مسئلہ میں کہ نفل کی نیت سے رمضان کا روز و ادا نہیں ہوگا امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے مہینہ میں نفلی روزہ کی نیت کر کے گویا اس نے فرض سے اعراض کیا ہے کیونکہ فرض اور نفل کے درمیان مغایرت ہے پس فرض سے اعراض کرنا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ نیت ہی ترک کر دی ہو اور یہ بات واضح ہے کہ ترک نیت سے روزہ ادا نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس صورت میں رمضان کا روزہ ادا نہیں ہوگا اور چونکہ نفلی روزہ کا وقت نہیں ہے اس لئے نفلی روزہ بھی ادا نہ ہو گا ۔ مطلق نیت کی صورت میں امام شافعی کے قول اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب ماہ رمضان میں مطابق روزہ کی نیت پائی گئی تو یہ شخص اس نیت سے فرض سے اعراض کرنے والا شمار نہ ہوگا اور جب فرض سے اعراض کرنا نہیں پایا گیا تو رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہو جائے گا دوسرے قول کی
For an obligatory fixed (fast), absolute intention suffices. And this type of fast is performed with absolute intention, with intention of nafl, and with intention of another wajib. And al-Shafi'i said: Regarding the intention of nafl, it is vain; and regarding absolute intention, he has two sayings, because by the intention of nafl he is turning away from the obligatory, so the obligatory is not for him. And our proof is that the obligatory is specific in this time, so it is attained by the root of intention, like a person alone in a house is attained by the generic name. And when he intended nafl or another wajib, he intended the root of fasting and an additional aspect; the aspect is void, so the root remains, and it is sufficient. And there is no difference between traveler and resident, sound and sick according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because the concession was only so that hardship does not befall the excused; when he bears hardship, he joins the non-excused. And according to Abu Hanifa, when a sick person or traveler fasts with the intention of another wajib, it falls for that other wajib, because he occupied the time with the more important, due to its actualization in the immediate present, and he has choice in the fast of Ramadan until completing the count. And from him (Abu Hanifa) regarding intention of supererogatory there are two narrations, and the distinction on one of them is that he did not turn the time to the more important. Explanation: It is understood that this type of fast, i.e., obligatory fixed, is performed with absolute intention, with intention of nafl, and with intention of another wajib. There is a slight error in the text of al-Quduri: since obligatory fixed includes both Ramadan and fixed vow, its meaning would be that just as Ramadan fast is performed with absolute intention, nafl intention, and other wajib intention, similarly fixed vow fast would also be performed with the mentioned intentions. However, it is not so, because fixed vow fast is performed with absolute intention and nafl intention, but is not performed with intention of another wajib, e.g., qada or kaffarah. Rather, if on the day of the fixed vow he intended another wajib at night, that other wajib is performed, not the fixed vow. In any case, the Hanafi madhhab is that Ramadan fast is performed with absolute intention, e.g., he said 'I will fast tomorrow'; and with nafl intention, e.g., he said 'I will observe a supererogatory fast tomorrow'; and with other wajib intention, e.g., he said 'I will observe a fast of kaffarah or qada of last year's Ramadan tomorrow.' Imam Shafi'i said that if in Ramadan one intends a nafl fast, neither Ramadan nor nafl is performed; rather that day's abstention is futile, because he did not intend Ramadan, and there is no time for nafl, so it does not count as any fast. And if one intends absolutely in Ramadan, there are two sayings: one that Ramadan is performed with absolute intention, the second that it is not performed. The same is the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad on this issue: that with nafl intention, Ramadan is not performed. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that by intending nafl in the month of Ramadan, he has turned away from the obligatory because there is a disparity between obligatory and nafl; turning away from the obligatory is like abandoning intention altogether, and it is clear that without intention the fast is not performed. So in this case Ramadan is not performed, and since there is no time for nafl, nafl is also not performed. In the case of absolute intention, the proof of the first saying is that when in the month of Ramadan intention of fasting is found, this person is not considered to be turning away from the obligatory, so when turning away is not found, Ramadan fast is performed. For the second saying...

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i (with mention of Malik and Ahmad) regarding the validity of Ramadan fast when the intention is for a different type of fast. The Hanafi position is that an obligatory fixed fast (such as Ramadan or a fixed vow) is valid with any intention related to fasting—absolute (muhlaq), nafl, or another wajib—because the day itself is specific to that obligation. The intention of the root of fasting suffices; the specific type intended is considered an additional aspect that becomes void. For example, one saying 'I intend to fast a nafl fast' in Ramadan still results in the Ramadan fast being valid, because the time is dedicated to Ramadan. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: intending nafl is a turning away from the obligation, so no fast is valid. On absolute intention in Ramadan, al-Shafi'i has two views: one that it suffices, another that it does not. The Hanafi proof uses an analogy: just as a person alone in a house is identified by his generic name, so the obligation of the day is fulfilled by the generic intention of fasting. The passage also covers an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if a sick person or traveler intends another wajib (e.g., making up a missed fast), it counts for that other wajib, not for Ramadan, because the immediate obligation is more important. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it counts for Ramadan, as the concession for travel/sickness is optional; if they choose to fast, it is as if they are not excused. Additionally, regarding a supererogatory intention, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. The commentary (tashrih) clarifies that the ruling differs for a fixed vow (nazr mu'ayyan): it is valid with absolute or nafl intention but not with the intention of another wajib. This is a nuance not explicitly stated in the earlier Arabic.

Key Terms
مطلق نیست (mutlaq niyyat): An absolute intention to fast without specifying the type (e.g., 'I will fast tomorrow').
نیت نفل (niyyat al-nafl): Intention to perform a supererogatory fast.
واجب آخر (wajib akhar): Another obligatory fast, such as qada or kaffarah.
نذر معین (nazr mu'ayyan): A fixed vow fast, e.g., vowing to fast on a specific day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a healthy resident in Ramadan intends to observe a nafl fast, what is the ruling?
A) The nafl fast is valid, and the Ramadan fast is not fulfilled
B) Neither the nafl nor the Ramadan fast is valid
C) The fast is valid as the Ramadan fast
D) The fast is valid as a qada fast

Key Takeaway
The Ramadan fast is valid with any intention to fast; the time's specificity makes the root intention sufficient, though an exception exists for fixed vows (nazr mu'ayyan) regarding other wajib intentions.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
12 min
Ruling on Intending Nafl or Other Wajib Fast During Ramadan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fulfillment of Ramadan fast with different intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) on the fulfillment of the Ramadan fast when a different fast is intended, and apply the tarjih (preferred view) as per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
If you intend a nafl or another wajib fast in Ramadan, the Ramadan fast is still fulfilled, except for a traveler/sick person intending another wajib per Abu Hanifa.

This passage explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding intention during Ramadan. The key question: if someone intends a supererogatory (nafl) or another obligatory (wajib) fast while fasting in Ramadan, which fast is actually performed? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) offer nuanced positions with practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Recognize that the month of Ramadan is specified exclusively for the fard (obligatory) fast. Any intention to fast in Ramadan automatically intends the fard fast, as the time only accepts the fard.
The hadith quoted supports this: after Sha'ban, no fasting except Ramadan.
2
Identify the positions of Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa
Sahibayn hold that whether one intends nafl, another wajib, or simply 'fast', the Ramadan fast is performed regardless of the person's status. Abu Hanifa agrees for the healthy resident, but distinguishes for the traveler and sick person.
This distinction is the core of the ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's distinction for traveler/sick
For traveler or sick person, if they intend another wajib fast (e.g., qada or kaffarah), that wajib is performed because it is immediately incumbent and more important, while the Ramadan fast can be postponed. Understand the reasoning: urgency vs. concession.
Abu Hanifa uses the principle of starting with the more important obligation.
4
Examine the two narrations from Abu Hanifa on nafl by traveler
When a traveler intends a nafl fast, two narrations exist: one priority the Ramadan fast due to greater reward, the other by analogy to Sha'ban allows the nafl to be performed. Note that this is an ikhtilaf within Abu Hanifa's own statements.
This demonstrates the depth of the school's internal discourse.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon view for fatwa is that of Sahibayn: the Ramadan fast is fulfilled with any intention of fasting, for all individuals. This is chosen because it is more sound and facilitates worship, as argued by later authorities like Al-Marghinani.
Thus, the general ruling is that the Ramadan fast is valid regardless of the specific intention, except in the narrow case of traveler/sick intending another wajib where some early Hanafi fatwas differ, but the established view is Sahibayn's.

اور مطلق نیت کی صورت میں چونکہ وصف فرضیت معدوم ہو گیا اس لئے نفس صوم بھی معدوم ہو جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رمضان کا مہینہ فرض روزوں کے لئے متعین ہے چنانچہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے إِذَا انْسَلَخَ شَعْبَانُ فَلاَصَومَ الأَرَمَضَان یعنی جب شعبان کا مہینہ ختم ہو گیا تو سوائے رمضان کے کوئی روزہ نہیں ہے یعنی اس مہینہ میں سوائے فریضہ رمضان کے اور کوئی روزہ نہیں ہے پس جب رمضان کا مہینہ فریضہ صوم کے لئے متعین ہے تو فریضہ صوم اصل نیت کے ساتھ ادا ہو جائے گا جیسے کسی مکان میں فقط ایک آدمی ہو ، اور اس کو اسم جنس کے ساتھ پکارا جائے تو وہی آدمی مراد ہوگا اور یہ پکارنا بھی درست ہوگا مثلاً کہا یا حیوان تو یا حیوان سے وہی آدمی مراد ہو گا جو مکان میں موجود ہے جیسا کہ یا انسان اور اس کے علم مثلا یا زید سے وہی مراد ہوتا ہے اسی طرح رمضان کا مہینہ جب فرض روزوں کے لئے متعین ہے تو فقط روزے کی نیت کرنے سے وہی روزہ ادا ہو گا جس کا یہ مہینہ مخصوص ہے اور جب اس نے نفل یا واجب آخر کی نیت کی تو گویا اصل صوم کی نیت کی اور ایک زائد چیز یعنی نفل یا وجوب کی نیت کی پس یہ جہت زائدہ تو لغو ہو جائے گی کیونکہ وقت یعنی ماه رمضان اس کو قبول نہیں کرتا اور جب جہت زائدہ لغو ہو گئی تو اصل صوم کی نیت باقی رہی اور سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ اصل نیت سے رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے نفل یا واجب آخر کی نیت سے بھی رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہو جائے گا صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس حکم میں کہ رمضان کا روزہ مطلق نیت ، نفل کی نیت اور واجب آخر کی نیت سے ادا ہو جاتا ہے مسافر، مقیم، تندرست اور بیمار سب برابر ہیں کیونکہ مسافر اور بیمار کو رمضان کا روزہ مؤخر کرنے کی رخصت اس لئے دی گئی تھی تا کہ ان لوگوں کو عذر سفر اور عذر مرض کی وجہ سے روزہ کی مشقت لاحق نہ ہو لیکن جب ان لوگوں نے اس مشقت کو برداشت کر لیا تو یہ لوگ غیر معذور کے ساتھ لاحق ہوں گے اور غیر معذور کے بارے میں گذر چکا کہ اس کا روزہ رمضان مطلق نیت ، نیت نفل اور واجب آخر کی نیت کے ساتھ ادا ہو جاتا ہے لہذا مسافر اور بیمار کا روزہ رمضان بھی ان تینوں سے ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر مسافر یا بیمار نے رمضان کے اندر واجب آخر کی نیت کے ساتھ روزہ رکھا تو واجب آخر ادا ہوگا نہ کہ رمضان کا روزہ ، اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ واجب آخر یعنی قضا یا کفارہ کا روزہ تو اس پر فی الحال لازم ہے چنانچہ اسی حال میں اگر مر گیا تو اس واجب کے بارے میں عند اللہ ماخوذ ہوگا اور رمضان کے روزہ کو مرض اور سفر کی وجہ سے مؤخر کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا ہے چنانچہ اگر یہ شخص اسی مرض یا اسی سفر میں مر گیا تو اس رمضان کے روزوں کے سلسلہ میں ماخوذ نہ ہوگا پس معلوم ہوا کہ مریض اور مسافر کے حق میں واجب آخر اہم اور رمضان غیر اہم ہے اور وقت کو اہم کے ساتھ مشغول کرنا اور اہم کو پہلے ادا کرنا اولیٰ ہے بہ نسبت غیر اہم کو ادا کرنے کے اس لئے حضرت امام صاحب نے فرمایا کہ رمضان میں مسافر اور مریض اگر کسی واجب آخر کی نیت کرلے تو وہ واجب آخر ادا ہو گا نہ کہ رمضان کا روزہ ، اور اگر مسافر نے رمضان المبارک میں نفلی روزہ کی نیت کی ، تو اس میں حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے دو روایتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ اس صورت میں رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہو گا نہ کہ نفل کا روزہ ، دوم یہ کہ نفل روزہ ادا ہوگا نہ کہ رمضان کا روزہ، پہلی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر نے رمضان میں نفلی روزہ کی نیت کر کے وقت کو کسی اہم کام میں مشغول نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ مقصود ثواب حاصل کرنا ہے اور ثواب رمضان کے روزہ میں زیادہ ہے بہ نسبت نفلی روزہ کے اس لئے نفل روزہ کی نیت کرنے کے باوجود رمضان ہی کا روزہ ادا ہوگا اور دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر کے حق میں رمضان کا مہینہ ایسا ہے جیسے مقیم کے حق میں شعبان کا مہینہ ہے اور شعبان کے مہینہ میں نفل یا واجب آخر جس کی نیت کرے گا وہی ادا ہو گا۔ پس اسی طرح مسافر رمضان کے مہینہ میں جس کی نیت کرے گا نفل کی یا واجب آخر کی ، وہی ادا ہو گا۔
The proof is that just as the essence of fasting is an act of worship, similarly the attribute of obligation is also an act of worship, and the essence of fasting is not performed without intention. So just as the essence of fasting is not performed without intention, similarly the attribute of obligation will not be performed without intention. And in the case of absolute intention, since the attribute of obligation is absent, the essence of fasting will also be absent. Our proof is that the month of Ramadan is specified for obligatory fasts. Thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When Sha'ban ends, there is no fasting except Ramadan,' meaning that in this month there is no fast except the obligation of Ramadan. So when the month of Ramadan is specified for the obligatory fast, the obligatory fast will be performed with the absolute intention, just as if there is only one person in a house and he is called by a generic name, that same person is intended and the calling is valid. For example, if one says 'O animal,' that refers to the person present in the house, just as 'O human' or his specific name like 'O Zaid' would refer to him. Similarly, when the month of Ramadan is specified for obligatory fasts, then by merely intending to fast, that fast for which the month is designated is performed. And if he intends a supererogatory or another obligatory fast, then he has effectively intended the essence of fasting and an extra element, namely supererogation or obligation. So this extra aspect becomes void because the time, i.e., the month of Ramadan, does not accept it. When the extra aspect becomes void, the intention of the essence of fasting remains, and it has previously passed that the Ramadan fast is performed with the absolute intention. Therefore, even with the intention of a supererogatory or another obligatory fast, the Ramadan fast is performed. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that in this ruling—that the Ramadan fast is performed with absolute intention, the intention of a supererogatory fast, and the intention of another obligatory fast—the traveler, resident, healthy, and sick are all equal. Because the traveler and sick were given a concession to postpone the Ramadan fast so that they would not suffer hardship due to the excuse of travel or illness. But when they have endured this hardship, they become like those without excuse, and it has already passed that the fast of one without excuse is performed with absolute intention, the intention of supererogatory, and the intention of another obligatory fast. Hence, the Ramadan fast of the traveler and sick will also be performed with these three intentions. Imam Abu Hanifa said: If a traveler or sick person intends another obligatory fast during Ramadan, then that other obligatory fast is performed, not the Ramadan fast. His proof is that the other obligatory fast, i.e., a make-up or expiation fast, is incumbent upon him immediately; indeed, if he dies in that state, he will be held accountable before Allah for that obligation. And he was given permission to postpone the Ramadan fast due to illness or travel; indeed, if this person dies in that same illness or travel, he will not be held accountable regarding that Ramadan fast. Thus it is known that for the sick and traveler, the other obligatory fast is more important and Ramadan is less important. Occupying the time with the more important and performing the more important first is preferable to performing the less important. Therefore, Imam Abu Hanifa said that if a traveler or sick person intends another obligatory fast during Ramadan, that other obligatory fast is performed, not the Ramadan fast. And if a traveler intends a supererogatory fast during Ramadan, then there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one is that in this case the Ramadan fast is performed, not the supererogatory fast; the second is that the supererogatory fast is performed, not the Ramadan fast. The proof of the first narration is that the traveler did not occupy the time with a more important matter by intending a supererogatory fast in Ramadan; rather, his aim is to obtain reward, and the reward in the Ramadan fast is greater than in the supererogatory fast. Therefore, despite intending a supererogatory fast, the Ramadan fast is performed. The proof of the second narration is that for the traveler, the month of Ramadan is like the month of Sha'ban for a resident. In Sha'ban, whichever fast he intends, supererogatory or obligatory, that one is performed. So similarly, the traveler, in the month of Ramadan, whichever he intends—supererogatory or another obligatory—that one is performed.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the ruling when a person intends a supererogatory (nafl) or another obligatory (wajib) fast during Ramadan. The discussion begins with the general principle: the month of Ramadan is specified for the obligatory fast, so any intention to fast in Ramadan automatically fulfills the Ramadan fast, even if one explicitly intends something else. This is because the time (Ramadan) only accepts the fard fast, so the extra specification (nafl or other wajib) becomes void, leaving the valid intention for the fard. The two companions extend this principle to travelers and sick persons, arguing that since they have chosen to endure hardship, they are like residents/healthy persons. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: for travelers and sick, another wajib fast (e.g., qada, kaffarah) is more pressing because it is incumbent immediately, whereas the Ramadan fast can be postponed. Therefore, if such a person intends another wajib, that wajib is fulfilled, not the Ramadan fast. For a supererogatory intention by a traveler, there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one prioritizes the Ramadan fast due to greater reward, the other treats Ramadan for the traveler like Sha'ban for a resident, allowing the intended nafl to be performed. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is typically the view of the two companions that the Ramadan fast is fulfilled, as it is simpler and facilitates worship.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary fast, not obligatory.
وصف فرضیت (wasf al-fardiyyah): The attribute of being obligatory (fard).
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the chief disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a traveler intends a qada (make-up) fast during Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) The Ramadan fast is performed.
B) The qada fast is performed.
C) Neither fast is valid.
D) Both fasts are valid.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the Ramadan fast is fulfilled regardless of the specific intention, providing ease for the fasting person.

Sawm — Fasting

Intention Timing for Dhimma-Based and Nafl Fasts
Ruling on intention for dhimma-based wajib fasts and permissibility of nafl fast until zawal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the intention requirements for dhimma-based wajib fasts and nafl fasts, and explain the Hanafi position against the views of Malik and Shafi'i.

Core Idea
For dhimma-based fasts, intention must be from night; for nafl, intention before zawal suffices.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author classifies fasting obligations and clarifies when intention must be made. For fasts that are established in the dhimma (liability), like qada and kaffarah, intention from the night is essential because they are not time-specified. However, for supererogatory (nafl) fasts, the Hanafi school allows intention up until zawal (midday), based on a specific hadith and the nature of nafl acts. This leniency contrasts with the positions of Imam Malik, who requires night intention for all fasts, and Imam Shafi'i, who allows intention even after zawal. Understanding these nuances is key to correctly applying the rules of fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories of Fasts
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between fasts that are thabit fi al-dhimma (established in liability, not time-bound) and nafl (supererogatory) fasts. The former includes qada and kaffarah.
The first type (time-specific like Ramadan) is not discussed here.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling for Intentions
For dhimma-based fasts: intention must be made during the night (before dawn). For nafl fasts: intention can be made up to zawal (midday).
3
Identify the Opposing Views
Malik requires night intention for all fasts, including nafl. Shafi'i permits intention for nafl even after zawal, considering the fast divisible.
These are the two opposing schools mentioned.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Proofs
The Hanafi proof is the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ said 'إِنَّى إِذًا لَصَائِمٌ' after waking up not fasting. Also, logically, nafl fasting is built on leniency, and intention must cover most of the day (before zawal).
The hadith is specific to nafl, not general.
5
Determine the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Malik: a nafl fast without night intention is invalid. Shafi'i: valid if intention after zawal. Hanafi: valid only if intention before zawal.
Hanafi position is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالضَّرْبُ الثَّانِى مَا ثَبَتَ فِى الذِّمَّةِ كَقَضَاءِ شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ وَصَوْمِ الْكَفَّارَةِ فَلَا يَجُوزُ إلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُتَعَيِّنٍ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّعْيِينِ مِنَ الْاِبْتِدَاءِ وَالنَّفَلُ كُلَّهُ يَجُوزُ بِنِيَّةٍ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ خِلَافًا لِمَالِكٍ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَمَسَّكُ بِإِطْلَاقِ مَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ بَعْدَ مَا كَانَ يُصْبِحُ غَيْرَ صَائِمٍ إِنَّى إِذًا لَصَائِمٌ وَلِأَنَّ الْمَشْرُوعَ خَارِجَ رَمَضَانَ هُوَ النَّفْلُ فَيَتَوَقَّفُ الْإِمْسَاكُ فِي أَوَّلِ الْيَوْمِ عَلَى صَيْرُورَتِهِ صَوْمًا بِالنِّيَّةِ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلَوْ نَوَى بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ لَا يَجُوزُ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِىُّ يَ جُوزُ وَ يَصِيرُ صَائِمًا مِنْ حِينَ نَوَى إِذْ هُوَ مُتَجَزِّئٌ عِنْدَهُ لِكَوْنِهِ مَبْنِيًّا عَلَى النَّشَاطِ وَلَعَلَّهُ يَنْشَطُ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ إِلَّا أَنَّ مِنْ شَرْطِ الْإِمْسَاكِ فِي أَوَّلِ النَّهَارِ وَعِنْدَنَا يَصِيرُ صَائِمًا مِنْ أَوَّلِ النَّهَارِ لِأَنَّهُ عِبَادَةُ قَهْرِ النَّفْسِ وَهِيَ إِنَّمَا تَتَحَقَّقُ بِإِمْسَاكٍ مُقَدَّرٍ فَيُعْتَبَرُ قِرَانُ النِّيَّةِ بِأَكْثَرِهِ
The second type is that which is established in the dhimma (liability), like the make-up of a month of Ramadan and the fast of expiation. Then it is not valid except with an intention from the night, because it is non-specified, and specification must be from the beginning. And every supererogatory fast is valid with an intention before zawal, contrary to Malik, for he adheres to the generality of what we narrated. And our proof is his statement after he would wake up not fasting: 'Verily, I am now fasting.' And because what is legislated outside Ramadan is the supererogatory fast, so the abstention at the beginning of the day depends on its becoming a fast through intention as we mentioned. And if he intends after zawal, it is not valid. Al-Shafi'i said: It is valid and he becomes a faster from the time he intended, since according to him it is divisible because it is built on activity, and perhaps he becomes active after zawal, except that abstinence at the beginning of the day is a condition. And according to us, he becomes a faster from the beginning of the day, because it is an act of subduing the soul, and that is only realized by a measured amount of abstention, so conjunction of the intention with most of it is considered.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage classifies fasting into two types: the first is time-specified (like Ramadan), and the second is dhimma-based obligations (like qada and kaffarah). For the second type, the intention must be made from the night (before dawn) because these fasts are not tied to a specific day—the entire day is a potential day for fasting, and specification must be made at the start. The ruling for supererogatory (nafl) fasts is more lenient: intention before zawal (midday) suffices. This is contrary to Imam Malik, who requires night intention for all fasts based on the general hadith about Ramadan. The Hanafi proof is an incident where the Prophet (ﷺ) woke up not fasting and then declared he was fasting, implying a nafl fast can be started during the day before zawal. Also, the legislated fast outside Ramadan is nafl, so the abstention depends on the intention at the start of the day—if one intends before zawal, the greater part of the day is spent fasting. Imam Shafi'i goes further, allowing intention even after zawal for nafl, considering the fast divisible by the hour. Hanafis reject this because fasting is an act of subduing the soul over a continuous period; the intention must be present for the majority of the day (from beginning to zawal). The passage thus clarifies the Hanafi position on intention timing for different categories of fasts.

Key Terms
ثابت فی الذمة (thabit fi al-dhimma): An obligation that is established in one's liability, not tied to a specific time.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory fast; voluntary.
متجزی (mutajazzi'): Divisible or allows part performance; used by Shafi'i to allow partial day fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, until what time is it valid to make intention for a nafl fast?
A) Before sunrise.
B) Before zawal (midday).
C) Any time during the day.
D) Only before Fajr.

Key Takeaway
For dhimma-based wajib fasts, intention from night is required; for nafl fasts, the Hanafi school permits intention before zawal, deriving this from specific prophetic practice and the nature of voluntary worship.
