Intention for Obligatory and Voluntary Fasts: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on niyyah for nafl and ruling on wajib fasts in dhimmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention for wajib fasts thabit fi al-dhimmah and explain why the Hanafi school permits intention for nafl fast only before zawal, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
A wajib fast that is a debt requires intention from the night; a nafl fast can be intended before midday, but not after, because fasting is a continuous act of subduing the soul.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a critical fiqh question: When must you make your intention (niyyah) for fasting? The answer depends on whether the fast is obligatory (wajib) and unspecified (thabit fi al-dhimmah) or voluntary (nafl). Moreover, the Hanafi school differs sharply from the Maliki and Shafi'i schools on the timing of intention for nafl fasts. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly performing both compensatory and voluntary fasts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on wajib fasts in dhimmah
Identify the second type of wajib fast (qada, kaffarah) and note that intention must be made from the night (before fajr) because the fast is unspecified and needs specification from the start.
This ruling is not disputed among the schools; it is a common requirement.
2
State the Hanafi position on nafl fasts
Note that intention for a nafl fast is valid only before zawal (midday). After zawal, the fast is invalid according to the Hanafi school.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Identify the Maliki and Shafi'i positions on nafl intention
Maliki: intention must be from the night, even for nafl. Shafi'i: intention can be made even after zawal, and the fast counts from the moment of intention.
Both schools differ from the Hanafi view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof for nafl intention before zawal
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet (peace be upon him) would decide to fast in the morning when no food was found. This indicates that intention after dawn is allowed. Additionally, the rational proof is that nafl outside Ramadan is a continuous act of subduing the soul, requiring intention for most of the day; after zawal, intention cannot cover most of the day.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni thubut, but sufficient for a wajib ruling? Actually the ruling is on nafl, so it is permissible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If someone intends to fast at 2 PM (after zawal), the Shafi'i school considers it valid from 2 PM to sunset, while the Hanafi school invalidates the entire fast even if nothing was consumed before, because intention must cover most of the day.
The difference is significant in practice, especially for those following a different school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الصوم
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر کے حق میں رمضان کا مہینہ ایسا ہے جیسے مقیم کے حق میں شعبان کا مہینہ ہے اور شعبان کے مہینہ میں نفل یا واجب آخر جس کی نیت کرے گا وہی ادا ہو گا۔ پس اسی طرح مسافر رمضان کے مہینہ میں جس کی نیت کرے گانفل کی یا واجب آخر کی ، وہی ادا ہو گا۔ واجب روزہ کی دوسری قسم اور اس کے لئے نیت کا حکم
وَالضَّرْبُ الثَّانِى مَا ثَبَتَ فِى الدِّمَةِ كَقَضَاءِ شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ وَصَوْمِ الْكَفَّارَةِ فَلَا يَجُوزُ إلَّا بنية من الليل لأنه غير مُتَعَيِّنِ وَلَابُدّ مِنَ التَّعْيِينِ مِنَ الْاِبْتِدَاءِ وَالنَّفَلُ كُلَّهَ يَجُوزُ بِنِيةٍ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ خِلَافًا لِمَالِكِ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَمَسَّكَ بِإِطْلَاقِ مَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَنَا قَولُهُ بَعْدَ مَا كَانَ يُصْبِحُ غَيْرَ صَائِمِ إِنَّى إِذَ لَصَائِمٌ وَلانَّ المَشْرُوعَ خَارِجُ رَمَضَانَ هُوَ النَّفْلُ فَيْتَوَقَّفُ الْإِمْسَاكُ فِي أَوَّلِ الْيَوْمِ عَلى صَيْرُورَتِهِ صَوْمًا بِالنِّيَّةِ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرَنَا وَلَوْ نَوَى بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ لَا يَجُوزُ و قَالَ الشَّافِعَى يَجُوزُ وَ يَصِيرُ صَائِمًا مِنْ حِينَ نَوَى إِذْ هُوَ مُتَجَزْ عِنْدَهُ لِكَوْنِهِ مَنِيًّا عَلَى النِّشَاطِ وَلَعَلَّةَ يَنْشُطُ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ إِلَّا إِنَّ مِنْ شَرطِ الإِمْسَاكَ فِي أَوَّلِ النَّهَارِ وَعِنْدَنَا يَصِيرُ صَائِمًا مِنْ أَوَّلَ النَّهَارِ لِأَنَّهُ عِبَادَةٌ فَهُرِ النَّفْسِ وَهِيَ إِنَّمَا يَتَحَقَّقُ بِإِمْسَاكِ مُقَدر فَيُعْتَبَرُ قِرَانُ النِّيَةِ بِاكَثَرِه
ترجمہ اور دوسری قسم وہ ہے جو آدمی کے ذمہ میں واجب ہو ، جیسے شہر رمضان کی قضاء اور کفارہ کا روزہ ، پس یہ قتم رات ہی میں نیست کرنے کے ساتھ جائز نہوگی کیونکہ یہ روزہ غیر متعین ہے اور ابتداء سے متعین کرنا ضروری ہے اور نفل ہر طرح کا زوال ہے پہلے پہلے نیست کے ساتھ جائز ہے امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس حدیث کے اطلاق سے استدلال کرتے ہیں جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے غیر صائم ہونے کی حالت میں صبح کرنے کے بعد فرمایا کہ میں اب صائم ہوں اور اس لئے مشروع رمضان کے علاوہ میں نفل ہے اس وجہ سے دن کے اول حصہ میں امساک کا صوم ہو جانا نیت پر موقوف ہے اس بناء پر جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور اگر زوال کے بعد نیت کی تو جائز نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جائز ہے اور روزہ دار اس وقت سے ہوگا جس وقت سے نیت کی ہے اس لئے کہ نفلی روزہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک متجری ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ نفلی روزہ نشاط پر بنی ہے اور ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کو زوال کے بعد نشاط ہو مگر اس کی شرط اول نہار میں امساک ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک اول نہار ہی سے روزہ دار ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ یہ نفس کو مغلوب کرنے کی عبادت ہے اور یہ عبادت امساک مقدر سے متحقق ہوگی پس اکثر یوم کے ساتھ نیت کا مقترن ہونا معتبر ہوگا۔
تشریح روزہ کی قسم ثانی جو ثابت فی الذمہ ہوتی ہے اور اس کے لئے کوئی وقت متعین نہیں ہوتا جیسے رمضان کی قضاء کے روزے کفارہ یمین کے روزے، کفارہ ظہار کے روزے، کفارہ قتل کے روزے جزا ، صید کے روزے اور نذر مطلق کے روزے اس قسم کا حکم یہ ہے کہ رات میں یا صبح صادق ہوتے ہی اگر نیت کر لی تو جائز ہے اور اگر طلوع فجر کے بعد نیت کی تو روزہ درست نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس قسم کے روزہ کا کوئی وقت متعین نہیں ہے بلکہ پورے سال میں رمضان اور ایام منہی عنہا کے علاوہ کبھی بھی رکھ سکتا ہے اس لئے شروع ہی دن سے متعین
کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور دن شروع ہوتا ہے طلوع فجر سے اس لئے طلوع فجر سے پہلے نیت کرے یا فجر طلوع ہوتے ہی نیت کرے۔ اور نفلی روزہ کے لئے نصف نہار سے پہلے پہلے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے چنانچہ نہار شرعی نصف حصہ گذر جانے کے بعد اگر نیت کی گئی تو روزہ معتبر نہ ہوگا امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ نفلی روزہ کے لئے بھی رات میں نیت کرنا ضروری ہے طلوع فجر کے بعد اگر نیت کی گئی تو نفل روزہ
بھی معتبر نہ ہوگا امام مالک کی دلی یہ ہے کہ حدیث لاصِيَامَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَنْوِ الصِّيَامَ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ مطلق ہے اس میں صوم فرض اور افضل کی کوالا تفصیل نہیں لہذا ہر روزہ کے لئے رات میں نیت کرنا ضروری ہے۔
ہماری دلیل حضرت عائشہ کی یہ حدیث ہے أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَدْخُلُ عَلَى نِسَائِهِ وَيَقُولُ هَلْ عِنْدَكُنَّ مِنْ عِذَاءٍ فَإِنْ قُلْنَ لَا قَالَ إِنِّى إِذَ الصَّائِم یعنی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنی ازواج کے پاس تشریف لیجاتے اور فرماتے کہ تمہارے. پاس کچھ کھانے کو ہے پس اگر وہ کہتیں کہ کچھ نہیں تو فرماتے کہ اب میں روزہ دار ہوں یعنی صبح ہو جانے کے بعد جب آپ کو کھانے کی کوئی چیز میسر نہ آتی تو آپ روزہ کی نیت . ی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفلی روزہ کی نیت طلوع آفتاب کے بعد کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رمضان المبارک کے علاوہ پورا وقت نفلی روزہ کے لئے مشروع ہے پس دن کے اول حصہ میں امساک یعنی کھانے پینے اور جماع سے رکھنے کا نام روزہ ہونا نیت پر موقوف ہوگا بشرطیکہ نیت دن کے اکثر حصہ میں پائی جائے اور نیت دن کے اکثر حصہ میں اسی وقت متحقق ہو سکتی ہے جبکہ نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے کی گئی ہو۔
اور اگر نفلی روزہ کی نیت زوال کے بعد کی گئی تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے البتہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ لیکن امام شافعی کے نزدیک روزہ دار اس وقت سے شمار ہوگا جب سے اس نے روزہ کی نیت کی ہے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک نفلی روز منجزی اور ٹکڑے ہو سکتا ہے اور دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ نفلی کام کا دارو مدار طبیعت کے نشاط اور فرحت پر مبنی ہے تو بہت ممکن ہے کہ اس کی طبیعت میں زوال کے بعد ہی نشاط پیدا ہوا ہو ۔ پس جب زوال کے بعد نشاط پیدا ہوا تو اسی وقت نیت کر کے روزہ شروع کر دیا تو یہ روزہ اسی وقت نیست سے شمار ہوگا لیکن اس کی شرط یہ ہے کہ امساک اول نہا رہی سے پایا جائے مثلاً اگر کسی نے طلوع فجر سے زوال کے بعد تک کچھ نہیں کھایا پیا اور پھر زوال کے بعد مثلا ۲ بجے سے روزہ کی نیت کر لی تو امام شافعی کے نزدیک ۲ بجے سے غروب تک اس کا نفلی روزہ معتبر ہوگا اور اگر طلوع فجر کے بعد کچھ کھا پی لیا پھر اس کے بعد نفلی روزہ کی نیت کی تو یہ روزہ معتبر نہ ہوگا اور ہمارے نزدیک روزہ چونکہ ٹکڑے نہیں ہوتا اس لئے روزہ کا اعتبار اول نہار ہی سے ہو گا اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ روزہ نفس کو مغلوب کرنے کی ایک عبادت ہے اور یہ عبادت ایک مقدار اور معین امساک کے ساتھ متحقق ہوگی اور وہ مقدار امساک پورے ایک دن کا ہے یعنی طلوع فجر سے غروب تک ہے پس نیت کا اقتران دن کے اکثر حصہ کے ساتھ معتبر ہو گا یعنی اگر دن کے اکثر حصہ میں نیت پائی گئی تو روزہ معتبر ہوگا ورنہ معتبر نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Fasting. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 3. The evidence is that for a traveler, the month of Ramadan is like the month of Sha'ban for a resident, and in Sha'ban, whatever you intend (nafl or other wajib) will be fulfilled. Similarly, a traveler in Ramadan intends whatever (nafl or other wajib) it will be fulfilled. Second type of obligatory fast and the ruling on intention for it. The second type is what is established in the dhimmah, like making up a month of Ramadan and the fast of expiation; it is not valid except with intention from the night because it is not specified, and specification from the beginning is necessary. And every nafl fast is valid with intention before zawal, contrary to Malik because he holds onto the generality of what we narrated. And our proof is his (the Prophet's) saying after he would wake up not fasting: 'Indeed, I am fasting.' And because outside of Ramadan, what is prescribed is nafl, so the abstention at the beginning of the day is dependent on it becoming a fast by intention, as we mentioned. And if he intended after zawal, it is not valid. And al-Shafi'i said it is valid and he becomes fasting from the time he intended, because according to him it is divisible, since it is based on activity, and perhaps he becomes active after zawal. But his condition is abstention at the beginning of the day. And according to us, he becomes fasting from the beginning of the day because it is an act of subduing the soul, and that is only realized by abstention of a measured amount, so the conjunction of intention with most of the day is considered. Translation: And the second type is what is obligatory on a person, like making up Ramadan and expiation fast. So it will not be valid except with intention from the night because this fast is unspecified, and specification from the beginning is necessary. And every type of nafl fast is valid with intention before zawal, contrary to Imam Malik because he argues from the generality of the hadith we narrated. And our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) after being in a state of not fasting in the morning said, 'I am now fasting.' And because outside of Ramadan what is prescribed is nafl, so abstention in the first part of the day depends on it becoming a fast by intention, based on what we mentioned. And if he intended after zawal, it is not valid. And Imam Shafi'i said it is valid and the faster becomes such from the time he intended, because the nafl fast according to him becomes divisible, since the nafl fast is based on activity, and it is possible that he becomes active after zawal. But his condition is abstention at the beginning of the day. And according to us, he becomes a faster from the beginning of the day because this is an act of subduing the soul, and this act is realized by abstention of a measured amount, so the conjunction of intention with most of the day is considered. Commentary: The second type of fast that is established in the dhimmah and has no specified time, such as the fasts of making up Ramadan, expiation of oath, expiation of zihar, expiation of killing, penalty of hunting, and absolute vow. The ruling of this type is that if he intends at night or at the time of true dawn, it is valid. If he intends after fajr, the fast is not correct because this type of fast has no specified time; rather, it can be done anytime throughout the year except Ramadan and the prohibited days. Therefore, it must be specified from the beginning of the day, and the day begins from fajr. So he should intend before fajr or at the time of fajr. For nafl fast, it is necessary to intend before midday. So if he intends after half of the legal day has passed, the fast will not be valid. Imam Malik said that for nafl fast also, intention from the night is necessary; if intended after fajr, the nafl fast will not be valid. Imam Malik's evidence is that the hadith 'No fast for one who does not intend fasting from the night' is general; there is no detail between obligatory and nafl, so for every fast, intention from the night is necessary. Our evidence is the hadith of Aisha that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to enter upon his wives and say, 'Do you have any food?' If they said no, he said, 'Then I am fasting.' So it is understood that intention for nafl fast after sunrise is also valid. And the rational evidence is that outside of Ramadan, the entire time is prescribed for nafl fast, so abstention in the first part of the day (i.e., refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse) becoming a fast is dependent on intention, provided that the intention is found in most of the day. And intention in most of the day can only be realized if it is made before midday. If intention for nafl fast is made after zawal, it is not valid according to us, but according to Imam Shafi'i it is valid. According to Imam Shafi'i, the faster will be counted from the time he intended, because according to him the nafl fast can be divided and fragmented, and its evidence is that voluntary actions depend on the activity and pleasure of the nature; it is very possible that activity arises after zawal. So when activity arises after zawal, he intends and starts fasting, then this fast will be counted from that time. But its condition is that abstention is present from the beginning of the day. For example, if someone did not eat or drink from fajr until after zawal, and then intended the fast at 2 o'clock, then according to Imam Shafi'i his nafl fast from 2 until sunset is valid. And if he ate or drank after fajr, then intended the nafl fast, this fast would not be valid. According to us, since the fast does not divide, the fast is considered from the beginning of the day, and the reason is that fasting is an act of subduing the soul, and this act is realized by a measured amount of abstention, and that amount is a whole day from fajr to sunset. So the conjunction of intention with most of the day is considered; i.e., if intention is found in most of the day, the fast is valid; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the timing of intention (niyyah) for voluntary (nafl) fasts and a ruling on obligatory fasts that are established as a debt (thabit fi al-dhimmah). The author first states the Hanafi position: obligatory fasts of the second type (qada, kaffarah, etc.) require intention from the night (before fajr) because they are unspecified and need specification from the start. Nafl fasts can be intended before zawal (midday), but not after, according to the Hanafi school. Imam Malik disagrees, holding that even nafl requires night intention, based on the general hadith 'No fast for one who does not intend from the night.' The Hanafi response uses two proofs: (1) the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would decide to fast in the morning after finding no food, indicating permissibility of intention after dawn for nafl; (2) rational: since outside Ramadan the prescribed act is nafl, the fast becomes valid by intention in the first part of the day, provided the intention covers most of the day (i.e., before zawal). Then Imam Shafi'i is mentioned: he allows intention after zawal for nafl, arguing the fast is divisible and based on personal activity. The Hanafi rebuttal is that fasting is a single continuous act of subduing the soul, requiring abstention for the whole day, so intention must be present for most of the day; after zawal, intention cannot cover most of the day, hence invalid. The commentary then elaborates: for the second type of wajib fast, intention at night or at fajr is valid; after fajr it is not. For nafl, intention before midday is necessary; after midday it is invalid. The detailed example illustrates the Shafi'i position and why Hanafi rejects it.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; the mental resolve to perform a specific act of worship. For fasting, it is required to distinguish the specific fast (e.g., nafl vs. wajib).
ثابت فی الذمہ (thabit fi al-dhimmah): Established as a debt; an obligation that is owed by the person, not tied to a specific time, like qada and kaffarah fasts.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory act; here specifically a voluntary fast outside Ramadan.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith (midday); the beginning of the time for zuhr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the latest time one can make intention for a nafl fast?
A) At any time during the day
B) Before zawal (midday)
C) After zawal but before sunset
D) Only from the night before

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires intention from the night for wajib fasts established as a debt (thabit fi al-dhimmah), and for nafl fasts, intention must be made before zawal; after zawal, the fast is invalid.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner
8 min
Seeking the Crescent Moon and Starting Ramadan
Ruling on seeking the crescent moon with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking the crescent moon on the 29th of Sha'ban and explain the obligation to complete 30 days if the moon is not sighted.

Core Idea
Ramadan starts with sighting or completing 30 days — calculation cannot replace it.

Determining the start of Ramadan is a practical issue every Muslim community faces. The Hanafi school, based on the explicit command of the Prophet (peace be upon him), teaches that we must rely on actual sighting of the crescent moon or, if it is obscured, we complete the month of Sha'ban as 30 days. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence from the classical text of Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What does the text say about the 29th of Sha'ban? It says 'yanbaghi' (it is appropriate) to seek the crescent — this is recommended (mustahabb). But the command to complete 30 days if not seen is obligatory (wajib). Distinguish these two levels.
The word 'yanbaghi' does not indicate obligation; the obligation comes from the hadith command 'akmilu'.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the Prophetic hadith: 'Fast upon sighting it... complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' Identify this as the primary evidence.
This hadith is transmitted by Bukhari and Muslim (ahad but widely accepted).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The imperative 'akmilu' (complete) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The condition 'if it is cloudy' triggers the command to complete 30 days, not to calculate.
The word 'ghumm' covers all obstructions, not just clouds.
4
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
This ruling is muttafaq alayh — all four schools agree that if the moon is not sighted, Sha'ban is completed as 30 days. However, some schools allow calculation in subsidiary matters, but the basic principle is unanimous.
The Hanafi school strictly rejects calculation for ibadah.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
Apply to a modern scenario: If a Muslim community on the 29th of Sha'ban does not see the moon due to smog, they must complete 30 days of Sha'ban and fast the following day. They cannot rely on astronomical data.
The original principle (asl) is the continuation of Sha'ban until proven otherwise.

قَالَ وَيَنبَغِي لِلنَّاسِ أنْ يَلتَمِسُوا الهِلَالَ فِي الْيَوْمِ التَّاسِعَ وَالْعِشْرِينَ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ فَإِنْ رَأَوْهُ صَامُوا وَإِنْ غُمَّ عَلَيْهِمْ أكْمِلُوا عِدَّةَ شَعْبَانَ ثَلَاثِينَ يَوْمًا ثُمَّ صَامُوا لِقَوْلِهِ صَوْمُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ وَافَطِرُوا لِرُؤيَتِهِ فَإِنْ غُمَّ عَلَيْكُمُ الْهِلَالَ فَاكْمِلُوا عِدَّةَ شَعْبَانَ ثَلَاثِينَ يَوْمًا وَلِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ بَقَاءُ الشَّهْرِ فَلاَ يَنْتَقِلُ عَنْهُ إِلَّا بِدَلِيل وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ

Ruling on seeking the crescent moon. He said: It is appropriate for people to seek the crescent on the twenty-ninth day of Sha'ban. If they see it, they fast; if it is cloudy (unclear) to them, they complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days, then fast. Because of his saying: Fast upon sighting it and break fast upon sighting it; if the crescent is cloudy to you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days. And because the original principle is the continuation of the month; one does not depart from it except with evidence, and none is found. Translation: He said that it is appropriate for people to seek the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban. If they see it, they should fast; if the moon is confused to them, they should complete thirty days of Sha'ban, then fast. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Fast upon sighting it (Ramadan) and break fast upon sighting it (Eid); if the crescent is cloudy to you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days. And because the original principle is the continuity of the month; one does not depart from it without evidence, and none is found.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) concerning the method of determining the start of Ramadan. The matn (from al-Hidayah) states that people should seek the crescent moon on the 29th of Sha'ban. If they see it, they begin fasting. If it is cloudy (ghumm, i.e., the sky is overcast or the moon is not visible), they should complete Sha'ban as thirty days and then start fasting. The proof is the Prophetic hadith: 'Fast upon sighting it (the crescent of Ramadan) and break fast upon sighting it (the crescent of Shawwal); if the crescent is cloudy to you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' The commentary adds that the underlying principle (asl) is that the month of Sha'ban is considered to continue (i.e., the 30th day is assumed to be still Sha'ban) until there is evidence to the contrary (i.e., confirmed sighting of the Ramadan moon). This is a straightforward ruling based on explicit Sunnah.

Key Terms
ہلال (hilal): The crescent moon at the beginning of a lunar month; specifically the first sighting of the new moon.
غُمَّ (ghumma): The moon is obscured by clouds, dust, or any obstruction making it invisible; the sky is unclear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Complete 30 days of Sha'ban and then fast
C) Fast the next day and then make up if needed
D) Wait until the moon is seen, even if it takes more than 30 days

Key Takeaway
The beginning of Ramadan is determined by actual sighting of the crescent or, if not sighted, by completing 30 days of Sha'ban; calculation is not a valid substitute.

Sawm — Fasting

Intention for Voluntary Fasts During the Day
Explains permissibility of niyyah for nafl sawm after dawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the timing of intention for voluntary fasts, distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, and evaluate the textual and rational proofs presented.

Core Idea
Intention for nafl fasts can be made up to midday, not after—a ruling based on the indivisibility of fasting as a single-day act of worship.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the permissibility of making intention (niyyah) for a voluntary (nafl) fast after dawn. The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith of Aisha and rational reasoning, permits intention for nafl fasts only before zawal (midday). Imam al-Shafi'i allows it even after zawal, provided the person has not eaten or drunk. Understanding this dispute reveals deeper principles about the nature of fasting and the role of intention in voluntary acts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact Hanafi ruling: intention for a voluntary fast must be made before zawal (midday). If made after, the fast is invalid.
This is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intention for a voluntary fast is valid even after zawal, provided the person has not already broken the fast by eating or drinking earlier in the day.
The Shafi'i view considers voluntary acts divisible based on personal inclination.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Aisha (RA) where the Prophet (SAW) made intention after dawn. Additionally, a rational proof: fasting is an indivisible act requiring intention to cover the majority of the day, which is only possible if intention is made before zawal.
The dalil is the hadith and qiyas (reasoning).
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof also uses the hadith of Aisha but interprets it to allow intention at any time before the end of the day, based on the principle that voluntary acts follow one's motivation and can be piecemeal.
They also argue that the hadith 'No fast without intention from the night' applies only to obligatory fasts.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a person makes intention after zawal, the Hanafi school deems the fast invalid, while the Shafi'i school considers it valid from the time of intention onward. This difference affects whether qada (make-up) is required if it later turns out to be a Ramadan fast.
The Hanafi ruling is stricter to preserve the integrity of the fast as a continuous act.

The book of fasting. Also it will not be valid. Imam Malik's proof is that the hadith 'Whoever does not make intention for fasting from the night' is absolute; it does not differentiate between obligatory and voluntary fasts, so intention at night is required for every fast. Our proof is the hadith of Aisha: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, used to enter upon his wives and say, "Do you have any food?" If they said no, he would say, "Then I am fasting."' This shows that it is permissible to make intention for a voluntary fast after dawn. The rational proof is that all time besides Ramadan is prescribed for voluntary fasting; thus, refraining (imsak) from eating, drinking, and marital relations in the first part of the day is called fasting contingent upon intention, provided that intention occurs in the majority of the day, and intention can be realized in the majority of the day only if made before midday. If intention is made after zawal, it is not valid in our view, but Imam Shafi'i allows it. According to him, the fast counts from the time of intention because voluntary acts can be divisible and piecemeal; his proof is that voluntary acts depend on one's motivation and joy, which may arise after zawal. The condition is that refraining from the beginning of the day is observed: if one ate nothing from dawn until after zawal and then intended fasting at, for example, 2 PM, then according to Shafi'i, his voluntary fast is valid from 2 PM to sunset. If one ate or drank after dawn and then intended fasting, the fast is not valid. In our view, since a fast cannot be divided, the fast is considered from the beginning of the day, because fasting is an act of subduing the soul, and this act is realized with a specific quantity of refraining, which is a full day from dawn to sunset. Thus, the intention must be coupled with the majority of the day; if intention is found in the majority of the day, the fast is valid, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding the time for making intention (niyyah) for voluntary (nafl) fasts. It opens with Imam Malik's position that intention must be made at night for all fasts based on a general hadith. The Hanafi response begins by citing the hadith of Aisha (RA) where the Prophet (SAW) stated he was fasting after learning there was no food, after dawn. This establishes that intention for voluntary fasts can be made during the day. The Hanafis then provide a rational proof: voluntary fasting is prescribed for all times except Ramadan, so the act of refraining (imsak) in the first part of the day becomes fasting only with intention, and that intention must occur in the majority of the day (i.e., before zawal). The passage then contrasts the Shafi'i view, which allows intention even after zawal, provided the person has not already broken the fast, because the Shafi'is consider voluntary acts divisible based on one's inclination. The Hanafi response emphasizes the indivisibility of fasting as a single act of worship requiring a continuous block of time from dawn to sunset, so intention after zawal does not cover the first part of the day. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that intention for a voluntary fast must be made before zawal; if made after, the fast is invalid.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship; for fasting, it distinguishes which fast one is observing.
نفلی روزہ (nafl sawm): A voluntary fast that is not obligatory or wajib, observed for extra reward.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes the meridian (midday), just before the time for zuhr prayer begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Before zawal (midday)
C) At any time during the day, even after late afternoon
D) Only before Fajr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits intention for voluntary fasts up to zawal (midday), but not after, because fasting is an indivisible whole-day act of worship.

Fasting on the Day of Doubt: The First Form and Its Ruling
Explains the ruling for the first form of fasting on the day of doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for fasting on yawm al-shakk with the intention of Ramadan, explain why it is makruh, not haram, and cite the hadith along with the Hanafi response to the objection.

Core Idea
Fasting on the day of doubt with Ramadan intention is makruh, not haram — the fast is valid if it coincides with Ramadan.

In this lesson, we examine the first of five forms of fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk). The text from al-Hidayah explains the ruling, the hadith proof, and addresses an important objection about the implication of the negation in the hadith. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the Hanafi approach to textual interpretation and the distinction between makruh tanzihi and haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting on yawm al-shakk with the specific intention of Ramadan. According to the Hanafi school, this is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
The ruling applies to the first of five forms; the subsequent forms are not covered in this passage.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith cited is: 'لا يُصَامُ الْيَوْمُ الَّذِي يُشَكُ فِيهِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ إِلَّا تَطَوُّعًا' — the day that is doubted to be from Ramadan should not be fasted except as a voluntary fast.
The hadith is a single narration (zanni al-thubut).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The negation 'لا يُصَامُ' appears to prohibit fasting on that day. However, the Hanafi school interprets this negation as a prohibition of obligation, not a prohibition of validity. The exception 'إِلَّا تَطَوُّعًا' shows that voluntary fasting is allowed, proving the prohibition is not absolute.
This interpretation distinguishes between makruh (negation of merit) and haram (prohibition of the act itself).
4
Note the objection
An objection is raised: the negation form (لَا يُصَامُ) normally indicates complete prohibition (tahrim), so fasting with Ramadan intention should be haram, not merely makruh.
This objection is based on the apparent meaning of the negation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the negation here conveys a prohibition that negates merit (thawab) but does not make the act invalid. Thus, the act is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
The response relies on the existence of the exception for voluntary fasting, which shows that the prohibition is not categorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یوم الشک کے روزہ کا حکم
وَلاَ يَصُومُونَ يَوْمَ الشَّكِ إِلا تَطُوعًا لِقَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَا يُصَامُ الْيَوْمُ الَّذِى يُشَكُ فِيهِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ إِلَّا تَطَوُّعًا وَهُذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَة عَلَى وُجُوهِ إِحْدُهَا أَنْ يَنوَى صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ وَهُوَ مَكْرُوهُ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلأنَّه تَشَبهُ بِأَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ لِأَنَّهُمْ زَادُوا فِي مُدَّةٍ صَوْمِهِمْ ثُمَّ إِنْ ظَهَرَ أَنَّ الْيَوْمَ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ يُجْزِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ شَهِدَ الشَّهْرَ وَ صَامَهُ وَإِنْ ظَهَرَ أَنَّهُ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ كَانَ تَطَرُّعًا وَإِنْ اَفْطَرَ لَمْ يَقْضِهِ لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَعْنَى الْمَظْنُّونِ
ترجمہ اور شک کے دن روز نہ رکھیں مگر نفلی کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ وہ دن جس میں رمضان ہونے کا شک ہو اس میں روزہ نہ رکھا جائے مگر نفل کا اور یہ مسئلہ چند صورتوں پر ہے ان میں سے ایک یہ کہ رمضان کے روزہ کی نیت کرے اور یہ مکروہ ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ۔ اور اس لئے یہ اہل کتاب کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے کیونکہ ان لوگوں نے اپنے روزہ کی تعداد میں اضافہ کر لیا تھا پھر اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ واقعی یہ دن رمضان کا تھا تو اس کو یہ روزہ رمضان سے کافی ہو گیا کیونکہ اس نے شہر رمضان کو پالیا اور روزہ رکھ لیا ہے اور اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ یہ دن شعبان کا تھا تو روزہ فضل ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس نے یہ روزہ توڑ ڈالا تو اس کی قضا نہ کرے کیونکہ یہ مظنون کے معنی میں ہے۔ تشریح یوم شک سے مراد شعبان کا آخری دن ہے جس کے بارے میں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ وہ رمضان کا پہلا دن ہو اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ شعبان کا آخری دن یعنی شعبان کی تیس تاریخ ہو۔ لیکن یہ واضح رہے کہ شعبان کا آخری دن یعنی تیسویں شعبان یوم الشک اس صورت میں ہو گا جبکہ انتیس شعبان کو مطلع صاف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے چاند کے ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں شک ہو۔ اور اگر مطلع صاف ہو تو اگلا دن یوم الشک نہیں کہلائے گا بہر حال یوم شک میں نفلی روزہ کے علاوہ روزہ نہ رکھا جائے اور دلیل یہ حدیث ہے لَا يُصَامُ اليَومُ الَّذِي يُشَكَ فِيهِ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ مصنف ہدایہ نے اس مسئلہ کی پانچ صورتیں ذکر کی ہیں (۱) یہ کہ کسی نے یوم شک میں رمضان کے روزے کی نیت کی ہو، یہ صورت مکروہ ہے اور دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو دو سطر اوپر مذکور ہے اس پر ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ حدیث میں لا یصام نفی کا صیغہ ہے اور نفی عدم جواز پر دلالت کرتی ہے تو اس سے یوم شک میں رمضان کے روزے کی نیت سے روزہ رکھنا نا جائز ثابت ہوا نہ کہ مکروہ۔ جواب حدیث میں نفی نہی کے معنی میں ہے اور نہی تقاضا کرتی ہے مشروعیت کا پس ثابت ہوا کہ یوم شک میں رمضان کی نیت
Ruling on fasting on the day of doubt. They should not fast on the day of doubt except voluntarily, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The day in which there is doubt whether it is from Ramadan should not be fasted except voluntarily.' This matter has several aspects; one of them is that one intends the fast of Ramadan, and it is disliked (makruh) due to what we have narrated, and because it is imitating the People of the Book, as they increased the period of their fasting. Then, if it becomes apparent that the day was from Ramadan, it suffices for him, because he encountered the month and fasted it; if it becomes apparent that it was from Sha'ban, then it is voluntary; and if he broke the fast, he does not make it up, because it is in the sense of a presumed day. Translation: And they should not fast on the day of doubt except voluntarily, because the Prophet said: 'The day in which there is doubt whether it is from Ramadan should not be fasted except voluntarily.' This matter has several forms; one of them is that one intends the fast of Ramadan, and this is disliked, due to the hadith we narrated, and because it is imitation of the People of the Book, as they increased the period of their fasting. Then, if it appears that the day was actually from Ramadan, this fast suffices for him, because he encountered the month and fasted it; if it appears that it was from Sha'ban, then the fast becomes voluntary; and if he broke the fast, he does not make it up, because it is in the sense of a presumed day. Commentary: The day of doubt refers to the last day of Sha'ban regarding which there is a possibility that it is the first day of Ramadan and also a possibility that it is the last day of Sha'ban, i.e., the 30th of Sha'ban. But it is clear that the last day of Sha'ban, i.e., the 30th of Sha'ban, is the day of doubt only when the sky was not clear on the 29th of Sha'ban, causing doubt about the existence of the moon. If the sky is clear, the next day is not called the day of doubt. In any case, only voluntary fasting is allowed on the day of doubt; the proof is the hadith: 'The day in which there is doubt whether it is from Ramadan should not be fasted except voluntarily.' The author of Hidayah mentions five forms of this issue: (1) that one intends the fast of Ramadan on the day of doubt; this form is disliked (makruh), and the proof is the hadith mentioned two lines above. There is an objection: the hadith uses a negation form 'la yusamu' which indicates prohibition, so fasting with the intention of Ramadan on the day of doubt would be impermissible, not merely disliked. Answer: In the hadith, the negation is in the sense of prohibition (nahy), and prohibition necessitates the lack of legislated merit, so it is established that intending Ramadan on the day of doubt is ...
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage addresses the fiqh of the 'day of doubt' (yawm al-shakk) — the 30th of Sha'ban when the month of Ramadan is uncertain. It begins by stating the basic ruling: only voluntary (nafl) fasting is permitted on this day, based on the hadith that prohibits fasting on a day of doubt except as a voluntary act. The text then outlines the first of five forms: if someone intends the fast of Ramadan on this day, it is makruh (disliked). The reason given is that it imitates the People of the Book who added to their fasts. The practical consequences are explained: if the day later turns out to be Ramadan, the fast is valid and counts; if it turns out to be from Sha'ban, it is considered a voluntary fast; if the person breaks the fast, no qada is required. The commentary then discusses a potential objection: the hadith uses a negation (la yusamu) which normally indicates prohibition (tahrim). The response is that the negation here is interpreted as a nahy (prohibition of a lesser degree), meaning it is makruh tanzihi, not haram. The text is incomplete at the end, but it establishes that the Hanafi position is that fasting with the intention of Ramadan on yawm al-shakk is makruh, not haram, and is valid if it coincides with Ramadan.

Key Terms
یوم الشک (yawm al-shakk): The day of doubt: the 30th of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether it is the last day of Sha'ban or the first day of Ramadan, due to lack of sighting on the 29th.
مکروہ (makruh): In this context, makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited). Fasting with Ramadan intention on yawm al-shakk is makruh due to imitation of ahl al-kitab and the hadith's negation.
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary acts of worship, including supererogatory fasting (nafl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if someone fasts on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan and it later turns out to be Sha'ban, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is invalid and must be made up.
B) The fast counts as a voluntary (nafl) fast.
C) The fast counts as a makeup for a missed Ramadan day.
D) The fast is haram and must be broken immediately.

Key Takeaway
Fasting on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan is disliked (makruh) but valid; it is not prohibited (haram) and becomes a voluntary fast if it is not Ramadan.

Obligation of Sighting the Crescent for Ramadan
Explains the obligation of moon sighting and completion of Sha'ban

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that sighting the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban is wajib kifayah and apply the rational proof of istishab to determine when to complete 30 days.

Core Idea
Sighting the crescent is a communal obligation; if not seen, complete 30 days of Sha'ban because certainty is not removed by doubt.

In this passage, the commentator explains the Hanafi ruling on beginning Ramadan. The key point is that the month of Sha'ban is established with certainty, so you cannot move to Ramadan without evidence. This lesson will help you understand the legal obligation of moon sighting and the role of istishab in determining the start of Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sighting the crescent of Ramadan on the 29th of Sha'ban. The ruling is that it is wajib kifayah (communal obligation).
Wajib kifayah means if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved of sin.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Fast upon its sighting, break fast upon its sighting, and if the crescent is obscured, complete the count of Sha'ban as 30 days.'
This hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'صُومُوا' (fast) indicates obligation. The phrase 'فَاكْمِلُوا' (complete) commands completing 30 days when the moon is not seen, reinforcing that sighting is the basis.
Imperative form implies wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the rational proof
The rational proof is based on istishab: the month of Sha'ban is established with certainty from the previous month. Without evidence (i.e., clear sighting), the original state continues.
Certainty is not removed by doubt (al-yaqeen la yazulu bi al-shakk).
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that it is wajib kifayah to sight, and if not seen, 30 days of Sha'ban are completed. This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is mentioned in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم ۱۸۹ کتاب الصوم (مہینہ ) کا باقی ہونا ہے پس اس سے بغیر دلیل کے منتقل نہ ہوگا اور دلیل پائی نہیں گئی۔ تشریح علامہ ابن الہمام نے فتح القدیر میں تحریر کیا ہے کہ انتیس ۲۹ شعبان کو رمضان المبارک کا چاند دیکھنا واجب علی الکفایہ ہے کیونکہ ۲۹ کا ہوتا ہے اور بھی ۳۰ کا ہوتا ہے پس ۲۹ شعبان کو اگر چاند نظر آ گیا تو روزہ رکھ لیا جائے اور اگر چاند نظر نہ آیا تو شعبان کے تمھیں دن پورے کر کے اگلے دن کا روزہ رکھیں دلیل رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول صُومُوا الرُّؤْيَتِهِ وَافَطِرُ وَالرُّؤْيَتِهِ فَإِنَّ غُمَّ عَلَيْكُمُ الْهِلَالَ فَاكْمِلُوا عِدَّةَ شَعْبَانَ ثَلَاثِينَ يَوماً بے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصل یہی ہے کہ شعبان کا مہینہ باقی ہو کیونکہ شعبان کا مہینہ گذشتہ سے بالیقین چلا آ رہا ہے لہذا ابغیر دلیل کے اس سے رمضان کے مہینہ کی طرف انتقال نہیں ہوگا اور یہاں دلیل کوئی پائی نہیں گئی ہے اس لئے کہ ۲۹ شعبان کو بالیقین چاند نظر نہیں آیا بلکہ ابر و وغیرہ کی وجہ سے شک ہے اور شک کی وجہ سے یقین زائل نہیں ہوتا پس ۲۹ شعبان کو چاند کے شبہ کی صورت میں شعبان کا مہینہ ختم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ ۳۰ تاریخ تک شعبان کا مہینہ باقی رہے گا۔
The month remains as it is, so it will not shift without evidence, and evidence is not found. Explanation: Allamah Ibn al-Humam wrote in Fath al-Qadir that sighting the crescent of Ramadan on the 29th of Sha'ban is wajib kifayah because the month can be 29 or 30 days. So if the crescent is seen on the 29th of Sha'ban, then fast is kept, and if the crescent is not seen, then complete 30 days of Sha'ban and fast the next day. The proof is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Fast upon its sighting, and break fast upon its sighting, and if the crescent is obscured for you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as 30 days.' The rational proof is that the original state is that the month of Sha'ban remains, because the month of Sha'ban has been coming with certainty from the previous month. Therefore, without evidence, one cannot transfer from it to the month of Ramadan, and no evidence is found here because on the 29th of Sha'ban the crescent is not certainly seen, rather there is doubt due to clouds and other reasons, and certainty is not removed by doubt. So in case of doubt about the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban, the month of Sha'ban does not end; rather, the month of Sha'ban remains until the 30th.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation of sighting the crescent for Ramadan. The source text is a commentary (sharh) on al-Hidayah. It begins by stating the principle that the month of Sha'ban remains in its current state unless evidence necessitates a change. The author then cites Allamah Ibn al-Humam's explanation that it is wajib kifayah (communal obligation) to sight the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban because the month may be 29 or 30 days. If the crescent is seen, fasting begins; if not, thirty days of Sha'ban are completed. The proof is the well-known hadith commanding fasting and breaking fast based on sighting, and completing thirty days if the crescent is obscured. The rational proof is based on istishab (continuity of certainty): Sha'ban is established with certainty, so it cannot be replaced by Ramadan without evidence. Since the crescent sighting is uncertain (due to clouds), the original certainty of Sha'ban remains. This establishes that the 30th day is still Sha'ban, not Ramadan.

Key Terms
واجب علی الکفایہ (wajib ala al-kifayah): A communal obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved of sin.
یقین (yaqeen): Certainty, as opposed to doubt (shakk). Certainty about the continuation of Sha'ban is established by previous knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on sighting the crescent of Ramadan on the 29th of Sha'ban according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard ayn on every Muslim
B) Wajib kifayah on the community
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Sighting the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban is a communal obligation; if not seen, complete 30 days due to the principle that certainty is not removed by doubt.

Sawm — Fasting

Ruling on Fasting on the Day of Doubt (Yawm al-Shakk) with Different Intentions
Rules and cases of fasting on the day of doubt with proof and detailed analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting on yawm al-shakk with the intention of Ramadan or another wajib, explain the proof from hadith, and apply the concept of mamnu' li ghayrihi to distinguish between makruh tanzihi and impermissibility.

Core Idea
Fasting on the day of doubt with obligatory intention is makruh but valid; the prohibition is external, not inherent.

On the 30th of Sha'ban, when the moon is hidden, uncertainty arises about the start of Ramadan. The Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed us not to fast on this 'day of doubt' except as supererogatory. But what if one intends an obligatory fast? The Hanafi school details two main cases: intending Ramadan and intending another wajib. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, the objection, and the Hanafi resolution using the principle of 'mamnu' li ghayrihi'.

Guided Path
1
Define yawm al-shakk and the general rule
Yawm al-shakk is the 30th of Sha'ban when the moon was not sighted on the 29th due to cloudiness. The general rule: only supererogatory (nafl) fasting is permitted. This is based on the hadith: 'The day which is doubted to be from Ramadan is not to be fasted except as supererogatory.'
If the sky is clear, the next day is not called yawm al-shakk.
2
Analyse the first case: intending Ramadan fast
If someone fasts on yawm al-shakk with the intention of the Ramadan fast, it is makruh tanzihi (disliked). The proof is the hadith. An objection arises: the hadith uses negation (la yusam) which implies absolute impermissibility. The Hanafi response: the negation is interpreted as prohibition (nahy), but the prohibition is due to an external factor (resembling Ahl al-Kitab), not intrinsic to the act itself. This is called mamnu' li ghayrihi, and such a prohibition does not invalidate the act; it only renders it makruh.
The rational proof: resembling Ahl al-Kitab who added to their fasts.
3
Analyse the second case: intending another wajib fast
If someone fasts on yawm al-shakk intending a wajib fast other than Ramadan (e.g., qada, nadhr), it is also makruh, but less so than the first case. The proof is the same hadith. There is a difference of opinion on whether this fast fulfills the intended wajib if the day turns out to be Sha'ban. One view says it becomes nafl because it is prohibited (manhiyy 'anhu). The other view, which is the most correct (al-ashah), says it suffices for the intended wajib because the prohibition of advancing before Ramadan is not universal, unlike the prohibition of fasting on Eid.
The author says 'wa huwa al-ashah' for the second view.
4
Study the consequences
For both cases: if the day turns out to be Ramadan, the fast counts as the Ramadan fast (or the intended wajib). If it turns out to be Sha'ban, the fast becomes a supererogatory (nafl) fast. If the fast is broken midway and it is confirmed to be Sha'ban, no qada is required because the obligation was only presumed (maznun).
Analogy: a person who prayed Zuhr then forgot and started another Zuhr – if he breaks it, no qada.
5
Apply the teachings to scenarios
Given a scenario, identify the intention, apply the ruling, and determine the outcome. For example, if Zayd fasts on yawm al-shakk with intention of Ramadan and it turns out to be Sha'ban, the fast is nafl and valid though makruh.
Practice with different facts to solidify understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یوم الشک کے روزہ کا حکم وَلاَ يَصُومُونَ يَوْمَ الشَّكِ إِلا تَطُوعًا لِقَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَا يُصَامُ الْيَوْمُ الَّذِى يُشَكُ فِيهِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ إِلَّا تَطَوُّعًا وَهُذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَة عَلَى وُجُوهِ إِحْدُهَا أَنْ يَنوَى صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ وَهُوَ مَكْرُوهُ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلأنَّه تَشَبهُ بِأَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ لِأَنَّهُمْ زَادُوا فِي مُدَّةٍ صَوْمِهِمْ ثُمَّ إِنْ ظَهَرَ ترجمہ اور شک کے دن روز نہ رکھیں مگر نفلی کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ وہ دن جس میں رمضان ہونے کا شک ہو اس میں روزہ نہ رکھا جائے مگر نفل کا اور یہ مسئلہ چند صورتوں پر ہے ان میں سے ایک یہ کہ رمضان کے روزہ کی نیت کرے اور یہ مکروہ ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ۔ اور اس لئے یہ اہل کتاب کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے کیونکہ ان لوگوں نے اپنے روزہ کی تعداد میں اضافہ کر لیا تھا پھر اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ واقعی یہ دن رمضان کا تھا تو اس کو یہ روزہ رمضان سے کافی ہو گیا کیونکہ اس نے شہر رمضان کو پالیا اور روزہ رکھ لیا ہے اور اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ یہ دن شعبان کا تھا تو روزہ فضل ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس نے یہ روزہ توڑ ڈالا تو اس کی قضا نہ کرے کیونکہ یہ مظنون کے معنی میں ہے۔ تشریح یوم شک سے مراد شعبان کا آخری دن ہے جس کے بارے میں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ وہ رمضان کا پہلا دن ہو اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ شعبان کا آخری دن یعنی شعبان کی تمیں تاریخ ہو۔ لیکن یہ واضح رہے کہ شعبان کا آخری دن یعنی تیسویں شعبان یوم االشک اس صورت میں ہو گا جبکہ انتیس شعبان کو مطلع صاف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے چاند کے ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں شک ہو۔ اور اگر مطلع صاف ہو تو اگلا دن یوم الشک نہیں کہلائے گا بہر حال یوم شک میں نفلی روزہ کے علاوہ روزہ نہ رکھا جائے اور دلیل یہ حدیث ہے لَا يُصَامُ اليَومُ الَّذِي يُشَكَ فِيهِ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ مصنف ہدایہ نے اس مسئلہ کی پانچ صورتیں ذکر کی ہیں (۱) یہ کہ کسی نے یوم شک میں رمضان کے روزے کی نیت کی ہو، یہ صورت مکروہ ہے اور دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو دو سطر او پر مذکور ہے اس پر ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ حدیث میں لا یصام نفی کا صیغہ ہے اور نفی عدم جواز پر دلالت کرتی ہے تو اس سے یوم شک میں رمضان کے روزے کی نیت سے روزہ رکھنا نا جائز ثابت ہوا نہ کہ مکروہ۔ جواب حدیث میں نفی نہی کے معنی میں ہے اور نہی تقاضا کرتی ہے مشروعیت کا پس ثابت ہوا کہ یوم شک میں رمضان کی نیت سے روزہ رکھنافی نفسہ تو مشروع ہے مگر نہی کی وجہ سے ممنوع لغیرہ ہے۔ اور ممنوع لغیرہ کا دوسرا نام مکروہ ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کہا گیا کہ اس دن میں رمضان کی نیت سے روزہ رکھنا جائز تو ہے مگر مکروہ ہے۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یوم شک میں رمضان کی نیت سے روزہ رکھنے میں یہود و نصاری کے ساتھ مشابہت لازم آتی ہے اس طور پر کہ وہ اپنے روزوں کی تعداد میں اضافہ کر دیا کرتے تھے اور اضافہ کی وجہ یہ تھی کہ اگر کبھی روزے گرمی کے زمانہ میں پڑتے تو ان کے علماء ان کو سردی کے زمانہ میں کر دیا کرتے تھے۔ اور اس تغیر کی وجہ سے کچھ روزوں کا اضافہ کر دیا کرتے ۔ پس چونکہ یوم شک کے اندر رمضان کا روزہ رکھنے میں یہ مشابہت ہے اس وجہ سے اس دن کا روزہ بنیت رمضان مکروہ قرار دیا گیا۔ بہر حال یوم شک میں بنیت رمضان روزہ رکھنا مکروہ ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود اگر کسی نے رکھ لیا اور پھر بعدم میں معلوم ہوا کہ واقعی یہ رمضان کا دن تھا تو اس کا یہ روزہ رمضان کا روزہ شمار ہوگا اور اس پر اس دن کے روزہ کی قضاء لازم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہ شخص شہر رمضان میں موجود ہے اور روزہ رکھ چکا ہے تو یہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول فَمَنْ شَهِدَ مِنْكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمُهُ (البقرۃ: ۱۸۵) پر عامل ہو گیا ہے اور اگر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ وہ شعبان کا دن تھا تو یہ نفلی روزہ شمار ہوگا اور مع الکراہت جائز ہوگا اور اگر اس نے روزہ توڑ ڈالا اور یہ تحقیق ہو چکا کہ یہ دن شعبان کا دن ہے تو اس پر اس کی قضا لازم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ شیخص مظنون کے حکم میں ہے یعنی اس نے اس گمان کے ساتھ روزہ شروع کیا کہ مجھ پر واجب ہے حالانکہ واجب نہ تھا اور مظنون پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی مثلاً ایک آدمی ظہر کی نماز پڑھ چکا پھر یاد نہ رہا اس نے دوبارہ ظہر کی فرض نماز شروع کر دی پھر یاد آیا کہ ظہر تو پڑھ چکا ہے اب اگر اس نے اس کو پورا کر لیا تو نفل ہو جائے گا اور اگر درمیان میں تو ڑ دیا تو اس نفل کی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی پس اسی طرح جب کسی نے یوم شک میں رمضان کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا اور پھر معلوم ہوا کہ آج رمضان نہیں شروع ہوا تو اگر اس نے اس روز ہ کو پورا کر لیا تو بس ہو جائے گا اور اگر درمیان میں تو ڑ دیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔ یوم الشک میں دوسرے واجب کی نیت بھی مکروہ ہے وَالثَّانِى أَنْ يَنْوِيَ عَنْ وَاجِبِ اخَرَ وَهُوَ مَكْرُوهُ أَيْضًا لِمَا رَوَيْنَا إِلَّا أَنَّ هَذَا دُونَ الأوَّلِ فِى الْكَرَاهَةِ ثُمَّ إِنْ ظَهَرَ أَنَّهُ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ يُجْزِيهِ الوُجُودِ أصْلِ البَيَةِ وَإِنْ ظَهَرَ أَنَّهُ مِنْ شَعْبَان فَقَدْ قِيلَ يَكُونُ تَطَوُّعًا لأنَّهُ مَنْهِيٌّ عَنْهُ فَلا يَتَأذَى بهِ الْوَاجِبُ وَقِيلَ يُجْزِيهِ عَنِ الَّذِى نَواهُ وَهُوَ الْأصْحُ لأنَّ المَنْهَى عَنهُ وَهُوَ التَقَدُّمُ عَلَى رَمَضَانَ بصَوه رَمَضَانَ لَا يَقَوْمُ بِكُلِّ صَوْمٍ بِخَلافِ يَوْمُ الْعِيدِ لأنَّ الْمَنْهِيِّ عَنْهُ وَهُوَ تَرَكَ الْإِجَابَةِ يُلازِمُ كُلَّ صَوْمِ وَالْكَرَاهَةُ هُنَا بِصُورَةِ النهى ترجمہ اور دوسری صورت یہ کہ واجب آخر کی نیت کرے اور یہ بھی مکروہ ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے مگر ہ صورت کراہت میں اول سے کمتر ہے پھر اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ یہ دن رمضان کا تھا تو اس کو کافی ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اصل نیت پائی گئی اور اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ یہ دن شعبان کا تھا تو کہا گیا کہ یہ روزہ افضل ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس روزہ سے منع کیا گیا ہے تو اس سے واجب ادا نہ ہوگا اور کہا گیا کہ اس واجب روزہ سے کافی ہو جائے گا جس کی نیت کی ہے اور یہی قول زیادہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ ممنوع ہونا یعنی رمضان پر رمضان کے روزے کو مقد کرنا ہر روزہ کی وجہ سے قائم نہ ہوگا بر خلاف یوم عید کے، اس لئے کہ جس چیز سے ممانعت کی گئی ہے اور وہ دعوت کو چھوڑنا ہے ہر روزہ کے ساتھ
Ruling on the day of doubt: They do not fast on the day of doubt except as supererogatory, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The day which is doubted to be from Ramadan is not to be fasted except as supererogatory.' This issue has several forms. One of them is that one intends the fast of Ramadan, and it is makruh due to what we narrated, and because it resembles the People of the Book, for they added to the duration of their fast. Then if it becomes apparent that the day was from Ramadan, it suffices him because he witnessed the month and fasted it. And if it becomes apparent that it was from Sha'ban, it becomes supererogatory. And if he breaks it, he does not have to make it up because it is in the meaning of a presumed thing (maznun). Translation: And they do not fast on the day of doubt except as supererogatory, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The day in which there is doubt about being from Ramadan, do not fast except supererogatory.' And this issue has several forms. One of them is that he intends the fast of Ramadan, and it is makruh due to this hadith, and because it is resemblance to the People of the Book, as they increased the number of their fasts. Then if it appears that the day was truly from Ramadan, this fast suffices for Ramadan because he reached the month and fasted it. And if it appears that it was from Sha'ban, then the fast is supererogatory. And if he breaks it, he does not have to make it up because it is in the meaning of a presumed thing. Commentary: The day of doubt refers to the last day of Sha'ban which could be the first day of Ramadan or the last day of Sha'ban (the 30th). But it should be clear that the last day of Sha'ban (the 30th) is the day of doubt only when on the 29th of Sha'ban the sky is not clear and there is doubt about the moon's existence. If the sky is clear, the next day is not called the day of doubt. In any case, on the day of doubt, no fast is kept except supererogatory, and the proof is this hadith. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned five forms of this issue: (1) One intends the fast of Ramadan on the day of doubt, this form is makruh, and the proof is the hadith mentioned two lines above. There is an objection: in the hadith, 'la yusam' is a form of negation, and negation indicates impermissibility, so fasting on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan would be impermissible, not makruh. The answer: In the hadith, negation is in the sense of prohibition, and prohibition demands that it is not legislated. So it is established that fasting on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan is in itself legislated, but due to the prohibition it is prohibited for something else (mamnu' li ghayrihi). And the other name of 'mamnu' li ghayrihi' is makruh. For this reason, it is said that fasting on this day with the intention of Ramadan is permissible but makruh. The rational proof is that fasting on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan entails resemblance to the Jews and Christians, in that they used to increase the number of their fasts. The reason for increase was that if the fasts fell in summer, their scholars would shift them to winter, and due to this change they would add some fasts. So, since fasting on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan has this resemblance, it was declared makruh. In any case, fasting on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan is makruh, but despite this, if someone did it and then it turned out that it was indeed Ramadan, this fast counts as the Ramadan fast, and he does not have to make it up, because this person was present in the month of Ramadan and has fasted, so he has acted upon the saying of Allah: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Al-Baqara 185). And if it later turned out that it was a day of Sha'ban, then it will be counted as a supererogatory fast, and it is permissible with karahah. And if he broke the fast and it was confirmed that it was a day of Sha'ban, then making it up is not necessary, because this person is in the ruling of 'maznun', i.e., he started fasting with the assumption that it was obligatory upon him, while it was not, and making up is not obligatory for a presumed thing. For example, a person has prayed Zuhr, then forgot and started another Zuhr fard prayer, then remembered that he had already prayed Zuhr. Now if he completes it, it becomes supererogatory, and if he breaks it midway, making up this supererogatory prayer is not obligatory. Similarly, when someone fasts on the day of doubt with the intention of Ramadan, and then it becomes known that Ramadan has not started, if he completed the fast, it suffices, and if he broke it midway, making it up is not obligatory. Also, intending another wajib fast on the day of doubt is makruh: The second form is that he intends another wajib fast, and this is also makruh due to what we narrated, except that this is less in karahah than the first. Then if it appears that it was from Ramadan, it suffices him due to the existence of the original intention. And if it appears that it was from Sha'ban, it has been said that it becomes supererogatory because it is prohibited and so the wajib is not fulfilled by it. And it has been said that it suffices for what he intended, and this is the most correct, because the prohibition (i.e., advancing before Ramadan with the fast of Ramadan) is not established for every fast, unlike the day of Eid, because the prohibition (i.e., leaving the invitation) is inseparable from every fast. And the karahah here is in the form of prohibition.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk). The original Arabic text (matn) from al-Hidayah states the general rule: only supererogatory fasting is permissible. The commentator (sharh) then lists five cases, of which two are fully explained here. The first case: intending Ramadan on the day of doubt is makruh. The proof is the hadith and the rational reasoning of resembling Ahl al-Kitab. An objection arises: the hadith uses negation, which seems to imply total prohibition. The answer is that the prohibition is for an external reason (mamnu' li ghayrihi), making the act valid but disliked. The second case: intending another wajib fast (e.g., a missed Ramadan day or a vow) is also makruh, but less so. The text then discusses the consequence: if the day turns out to be Ramadan, the fast suffices; if Sha'ban, there is a difference of opinion: some say it becomes voluntary, others say it fulfills the intended wajib. The author prefers the latter, reasoning that the prohibition of advancing before Ramadan is not universal, unlike the prohibition of fasting on Eid which is absolutely prohibited. The commentary also clarifies that the day of doubt is only when the sky is not clear on the 29th.

Key Terms
یوم الشک (yawm al-shakk): The 30th of Sha'ban when there is doubt (due to cloudiness) whether it is actually Ramadan or not.
ممنوع لغیرہ (mamnu' li ghayrihi): An act that is itself permissible but is prohibited due to an external factor or consequence. Here, fasting on the day of doubt is valid in itself (as supererogatory), but when intending Ramadan, it becomes makruh because of resemblance to Ahl al-Kitab.
منهی عنه (manhiyy 'anhu): That which is prohibited. In this context, it refers to the act of fasting on yawm al-shakk with the intention of Ramadan, which is prohibited in the sense of being makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if someone fasts on yawm al-shakk with the intention of Ramadan and it later turns out to be Sha'ban, what is the ruling on the fast?
A) The fast is invalid and must be made up as qada.
B) The fast counts as a supererogatory (nafl) fast.
C) The fast is considered an obligatory fast for Sha'ban.
D) The fast is considered a missed Ramadan fast and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Fasting on yawm al-shakk with obligatory intention is makruh tanzihi but valid; if it turns out to be Ramadan it counts, otherwise it becomes nafl or may fulfill the intended wajib per the preferred view.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
6 min
Fasting on the Day of Doubt (Yawm al-Shakk) with Intention of Ramadan
Ruling on fasting the Day of Doubt with intention of Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting Yawm al-Shakk with intention of Ramadan, explain why it is makruh, and apply the consequences if it turns out to be Ramadan or Sha'ban.

Core Idea
Fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with Ramadan intention is valid but makruh due to resemblance to non-Muslims.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a common dilemma: fasting on the 30th of Sha'ban when the start of Ramadan is uncertain. The Hanafi school rules that such a fast is permissible but disliked (makruh). The commentary explains the reasoning behind this dislike and the legal consequences if the day later turns out to be Ramadan or Sha'ban. Understanding this ruling helps you navigate the fiqh of indeterminate days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with the intention of Ramadan. The ruling is makruh (disliked) but the fast is valid (sahih).
The dislike is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Locate the proof
The text gives a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) of resemblance to Jews and Christians who added days to their fasts. It also quotes Quran 2:185 to show the fast counts if it indeed is Ramadan.
The Quranic evidence is used to validate the fast, not to establish the dislike.
3
Understand the makruh classification
The act is legislated in itself (mashru') but prohibited due to an external factor (mamnu' li-ghayrihi), i.e., the resemblance to non-Muslims. This makes it makruh.
This is a classic Hanafi distinction: something valid but disliked due to an external cause.
4
Trace the consequences
If the day turns out to be Ramadan, the fast counts as the Ramadan obligation. If it is Sha'ban, the fast becomes a voluntary fast (nafl). If broken and confirmed as Sha'ban, no make-up is required.
The person acted based on presumption (maznun), so qada' is not obligatory.
5
Apply the principle of maznun
The example of Zuhr prayer illustrates that if one prays a second Zuhr based on forgetting, it becomes nafl, and if broken, no qada' is due. Similarly, if one fasts on Yawm al-Shakk intending Ramadan and it turns out not to be Ramadan, the fast is nafl and no qada' is owed.
This principle is important in similar cases of doubtful obligation.

Source Text

كتاب الصوم
19.
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
سے روزہ رکھنافی نفسہ تو مشروع ہے مگر نہی کی وجہ سے ممنوع لغیرہ ہے۔ اور ممنوع لغیرہ کا دوسرا نام مکروہ ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کہا گیا کہ اس دن میں رمضان کی نیت سے روزہ رکھنا جائز تو ہے مگر مکروہ ہے۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یوم شک میں رمضان کی نیت سے روزہ رکھنے میں یہود و نصاری کے ساتھ مشابہت لازم آتی ہے اس طور پر کہ وہ اپنے روزوں کی تعداد میں اضافہ کر دیا کرتے تھے اور اضافہ کی وجہ یہ تھی کہ اگر کبھی روزے گرمی کے زمانہ میں پڑتے تو ان کے علماء ان کو سردی کے زمانہ میں کر دیا کرتے تھے۔ اور اس تغیر کی وجہ سے کچھ روزوں کا اضافہ کر دیا کرتے ۔ پس چونکہ یوم شک کے اندر رمضان کا روزہ رکھنے میں یہ مشابہت ہے اس وجہ سے اس دن کا روزہ بنیت رمضان مکروہ قرار دیا گیا۔
بہر حال یوم شک میں بنیت رمضان روزہ رکھنا مکروہ ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود اگر کسی نے رکھ لیا اور پھر بعدم میں معلوم ہوا کہ واقعی یہ رمضان کا دن تھا تو اس کا یہ روزہ رمضان کا روزہ شمار ہوگا اور اس پر اس دن کے روزہ کی قضاء لازم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہ شخص شہر رمضان میں موجود ہے اور روزہ رکھ چکا ہے تو یہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول فَمَنْ شَهِدَ مِنْكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمُهُ (البقرۃ: ۱۸۵) پر عامل ہو گیا ہے اور اگر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ وہ شعبان کا دن تھا تو یہ نفلی روزہ شمار ہوگا اور مع الکراہت جائز ہوگا اور اگر اس نے روزہ توڑ ڈالا اور یہ تحقیق ہو چکا کہ یہ دن شعبان کا دن ہے تو اس پر اس کی قضا لازم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ شیخص مظنون کے حکم میں ہے یعنی اس نے اس گمان کے ساتھ روزہ شروع کیا کہ مجھ پر واجب ہے حالانکہ واجب نہ تھا اور مظنون پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی مثلاً ایک آدمی ظہر کی نماز پڑھ چکا پھر یاد نہ رہا اس نے دوبارہ ظہر کی فرض نماز شروع کر دی پھر یاد آیا کہ ظہر تو پڑھ چکا ہے اب اگر اس نے اس کو پورا کر لیا تو نفل ہو جائے گا اور اگر درمیان میں تو ڑ دیا تو اس نفل کی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی پس اسی طرح جب کسی نے یوم شک میں رمضان کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا اور پھر معلوم ہوا کہ آج رمضان نہیں شروع ہوا تو اگر اس نے اس روز ہ کو پورا کر لیا تو بس ہو جائے گا اور اگر درمیان میں تو ڑ دیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔
Book of Fasting. 19. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 3. Fasting in itself is legislated but due to the prohibition it is prohibited for something external. And the prohibited for something external is called makruh. For this reason it was said that on this day fasting with the intention of Ramadan is permissible but makruh. The rational proof is that fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with intention of Ramadan entails resemblance to Jews and Christians in that they used to increase the number of their fasts, and the reason for increase was that if sometimes the fasts fell in summer, their scholars would move them to winter and due to this change they would add some fasts. So since fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with intention of Ramadan has this resemblance, it was deemed makruh. Nevertheless, fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with the intention of Ramadan is makruh. But despite this, if someone fasted and later it became known that it was indeed the day of Ramadan, then his fast will count as the fast of Ramadan and he will not have to make it up because he was present in the month of Ramadan and has fasted, so he has acted upon the saying of Allah (Quran 2:185). And if it later becomes known that it was a day of Sha'ban, then it will count as a voluntary fast and is permissible with dislike. And if he broke the fast and it was established that it was a day of Sha'ban, then he does not have to make it up because the person is under the ruling of presumption (maznun), i.e., he started the fast with the presumption that it was obligatory upon him, whereas it was not, and qada' is not obligatory upon presumption. For example, a person prayed Zuhr, then forgot and started the Zuhr fard prayer again, then remembered that he had already prayed Zuhr. Now if he completes it, it becomes nafl, and if he breaks it in the middle, qada' of that nafl is not obligatory. Similarly, if someone fasted on Yawm al-Shakk with intention of Ramadan and then found that Ramadan had not started, then if he completes the fast, it is just that, and if he breaks it in the middle, qada' is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school on fasting on the Day of Doubt (Yawm al-Shakk) with the intention of Ramadan. The author explains that fasting itself is a legislated act (mashru'), but when done on this day with the intention of Ramadan, it becomes prohibited due to an external factor (mamnu' li-ghayrihi), which is termed makruh. The ruling is that it is permissible but makruh. The author provides a rational proof (dalil 'aqli): it resembles the practice of Jews and Christians who would adjust the timing of their fasts, leading to an increase in days. Since fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with Ramadan intention has this resemblance, it is considered makruh. The passage then addresses the consequence: if it later becomes known that the day was indeed Ramadan, the fast counts as the Ramadan fast, based on the verse (2:185). If it was Sha'ban, the fast becomes voluntary (nafl) and is valid with dislike. If the fast was broken and it was Sha'ban, no make-up is required because the person acted on a presumption (maznun). An analogy with Zuhr prayer is provided to illustrate that qada' is not obligatory upon a mistaken presumption. The ruling clearly distinguishes between the objective obligation and the subjective presumption.

Key Terms
یوم الشک (Yawm al-Shakk): The day of doubt, i.e., the 30th of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether Ramadan has begun due to cloudy weather.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked but not prohibited; the act is valid but entails sin if done without valid reason.
مظنون (maznun): Presumed; a situation where one acts based on a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) rather than certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person fasts on Yawm al-Shakk with the intention of Ramadan and later discovers it was Sha'ban, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is invalid and must be made up.
B) The fast counts as a voluntary fast and no make-up is required.
C) The fast counts as the missed Ramadan fast.
D) The fast is obligatory to complete.

Key Takeaway
Fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with Ramadan intention is valid but makruh; if it later becomes Ramadan it fulfills the obligation, otherwise it is nafl with no qada'.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with Intention of Another Wajib
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting Yawm al-Shakk with intention of another wajib, identify the two opinions if it turns out to be Sha'ban, and explain why the mufta bihi is that it suffices.

Core Idea
Fasting Yawm al-Shakk for another wajib is valid but disliked — the prohibition only applies to anticipating Ramadan with Ramadan intention.

On the Day of Doubt, if one intends an obligatory fast other than Ramadan—such as qada' or kaffarah—the Hanafi school considers it valid but makruh tanzih. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and the preferred view (asahh) among two positions within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Recognize that the passage addresses a second scenario: fasting on Yawm al-Shakk with an intention for a wajib other than Ramadan. The initial ruling is that it is also makruh, but less so than the first scenario (intending Ramadan itself).
The first scenario (intending Ramadan) is discussed earlier, but here the focus is on a different intention.
2
Examine the dalil and its delimitation
The proof is the same hadith prohibiting fasting on the day of doubt. However, the Hanafi interpretation limits the prohibition to fasting with the intention of Ramadan, not all fasts. Understand the wording 'la tataqaddamu ala Ramadana bi sawmi yawm' as specifically targeting Ramadan intention.
The hadith is ahad, so it yields zanni thubut and zanni dalalah according to Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish two outcomes: if day is Ramadan vs Sha'ban
If the day later proves to be Ramadan, the fast suffices because the original intention of being in Ramadan is subsumed. If it proves to be Sha'ban, there is disagreement on the status.
This distinction is crucial for practical application.
4
Analyze the two Hanafi opinions for the Sha'ban case
Opinion 1: The fast becomes nafl because the day is prohibited for fasting, so the wajib is not fulfilled. Opinion 2 (the asahh): The fast fulfills the intended wajib because the prohibition is specific to anticipating Ramadan with Ramadan intention, not to all fasts.
The first opinion draws an analogy with Eid, but the text distinguishes the illa.
5
Understand why the second opinion is preferred and contrast with Eid
The second opinion is preferred because the hadith's prohibition is restricted to Ramadan intention; it does not cover other wajib fasts. In contrast, on Eid the prohibition is absolute because the illa (abandoning Allah's invitation) is present in every fast, regardless of intention.
This contrast highlights the role of illa in Hanafi reasoning.
