Main Ruling: Lone Moon Sighting Obligates Fasting without Kaffarah
Presents the main Hanafi ruling on lone moon sighting with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a lone moon sighting, identify the evidence from hadith, and explain why breaking the fast requires qada but not kaffarah.

Core Idea
A lone sighting obligates fasting individually; breaking requires qada, no kaffarah due to doubt.

This lesson focuses on the core Hanafi ruling when an individual alone sights the Ramadan crescent and the imam rejects his testimony. The passage establishes that the person must fast based on the Prophet's command, and if he breaks his fast, he only needs to make up the day (qada), without any expiation (kaffarah). We will dissect the evidence and the rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The scenario: a person sees the Ramadan crescent alone. The ruling: he must fast (صام) even if the imam does not accept his testimony.
This is the core hukm for the individual.
2
Extract the dalil (evidence)
The passage cites the hadith: 'Fast upon its sighting and break your fast upon its sighting.' This is the proof that personal sighting is sufficient for obligation.
The hadith is a dalil naqli.
3
Analyze the consequence of breaking the fast
If he breaks his fast (e.g., by intercourse), the ruling is: upon him is qada but no kaffarah. This is the Hanafi position.
Kaffarah is dropped due to shubhah (doubt) created by the imam's rejection.
4
Understand the principle behind dropping kaffarah
The imam's rejection is based on a legal evidence (suspicion of error), which creates a doubt. The principle 'al-hudud wa al-kaffarat tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' applies.
This is a key usul principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ رَأَى هِلَالَ رَمَضَانَ وَحْدَهُ صَامَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْبَلِ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَتَهُ لِقَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم صُومُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ وَافْطِرُوا لِرُؤيَتِهِ وَقَدْ رَأَى ظَاهِراً وَإِنْ أَفْطَرَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَةِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ عَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ إِنْ أَفْطَرَ بِالْوِقَاعِ لِأَنَّهُ أَفْطَرَ فِي رَمَضَانَ حَقِيْقَةً بِيَقِينِهِ وَحُكْمًا لِوُجُوبِ الصَّوْمِ عَلَيْهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْقَاضِي رَدَّ شَهَادَتَهُ بِدَلِيلٍ شَرْعِيٍّ وَهُوَ تُهْمَةُ الْغَلَطِ فَأَوْرَثَ شُبْهَةً وَهَذِهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ تُدْرَأُ بِالشُّبُهَاتِ وَلَوْ أَفْطَرَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَرُدَّ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَتَهُ اخْتَلَفَ الْمَشَايِخُ فِيهِ وَلَوْ أَكْمَلَ هَذَا الرَّجُلُ ثَلَاثِينَ يَوْمًا لَمْ يُفْطِرْ إِلَّا مَعَ الْإِمَامِ إِنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عَلَيْهِ لِلْإِحْتِيَاطِ وَالْإِحْتِيَاطُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فِي تَأْخِيرِ الْإِفْطَارِ وَلَوْ أَفْطَرَ لَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ اعْتِبَارًا لِلْحَقِيقَةِ الَّتِي عِنْدَهُ
And whoever sees the crescent of Ramadan alone must fast, even if the imam does not accept his testimony, due to his (PBUH) saying: 'Fast upon its sighting and break your fast upon its sighting.' And he has indeed seen it apparently. And if he breaks his fast, then upon him is qada without kaffarah. Al-Shafi'i said: 'Upon him is kaffarah if he breaks his fast by intercourse, because he has broken it in Ramadan, in reality due to his certainty, and in ruling due to the obligation of fasting upon him.' Our proof: The judge rejected his testimony by a legal evidence, which is the suspicion of error, so it caused a doubt, and this kaffarah is repelled by doubts. And if he broke his fast before the imam rejected his testimony, the scholars differed concerning this. And if this man completed thirty days, he should not break his fast except with the imam; indeed, the obligation upon him was for precaution, and precaution after that lies in delaying the breaking of the fast. And if he broke his fast, no kaffarah is upon him, considering the reality that is with him.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling: If a single person sees the Ramadan crescent (moon) and the imam does not accept his testimony (perhaps due to lack of witnesses or suspicion of error), that person is still obligated to fast individually. The evidence is the Prophet's hadith commanding fasting based on sighting, and this person has indeed sighted it. If he breaks his fast (e.g., by eating or intercourse), he must make up the day (qada) but does not have to pay kaffarah (expiation). This is the Hanafi position. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that if he breaks it by intercourse, kaffarah is also required because in reality he is certain it is Ramadan, and by ruling the fast is obligatory on him. The Hanafi response: The imam's rejection of his testimony is based on a valid legal reason (suspicion of error), which creates a doubt (shubhah) in the certainty of Ramadan. Kaffarah is a penal expiation that is dropped by doubts (a legal maxim: 'al-hudud wa al-kaffarat tudra'u bi al-shubuhat'). Therefore, no kaffarah. The passage then addresses two subsidiary issues: 1) If he breaks his fast before the imam rejects his testimony, there is disagreement among Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) about the ruling. 2) If he completes 30 days of fasting (to be safe), he should not break his fast (for Eid) except with the imam, because his obligation was based on precaution; after completing 30 days, caution is to delay breaking until the imam does. If he breaks it, no kaffarah because he considered his own reality. The passage thus clarifies the delicate balance between individual certainty and communal authority, and the role of shubhah in dropping obligatory expiations.

Key Terms
رؤية الهلال (ru'yat al-hilal): Sighting of the new moon crescent to determine the start of Ramadan or Shawwal.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast by intercourse, which in the Hanafi school is freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor.
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity in the legal status of an act that prevents the application of penal or expiatory measures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person who alone sights the Ramadan crescent breaks his fast by intercourse after the imam rejects his testimony?
A) He must pay both qada and kaffarah.
B) He must only pay qada.
C) He is not required to do anything because his fast was never valid.
D) He must pay kaffarah but no qada.

Key Takeaway
A lone moon sighting obligates the individual to fast; breaking requires qada but no kaffarah due to the principle of dropping penalties by doubts.

Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Kaffarah for Lone Moon Sighting
Presents the inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on kaffarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i view on kaffarah for lone moon sighting and the Hanafi response, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah) of the difference.

Core Idea
Shafi'i requires kaffarah for breaking lone-sighted fast by intercourse; Hanafi drops it due to shubhah.

This lesson delves into the dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over whether a person who alone sights the Ramadan crescent and breaks his fast by intercourse must pay kaffarah. We examine each school's evidence, the Hanafi rebuttal, and the practical impact of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Hanafi: only qada, no kaffarah. The imam's rejection creates a doubt that drops kaffarah.
The principle: 'al-hudud wa al-kaffarat tudra'u bi al-shubuhat'.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that kaffarah is required because the person broke his fast in Ramadan with certainty and by ruling fasting was obligatory.
Shafi'i relies on the individual's certainty and the external ruling of obligation.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Their dalil: he broke his fast in Ramadan 'in reality due to his certainty' (bi yaqīnihi) and 'by ruling' (ḥukman) due to the obligation of fasting upon him.
Thus, both reality and ruling confirm it was Ramadan.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The imam's rejection is based on a legal evidence (suspicion of error), which creates a shubhah. Kaffarah, like hudud, is repelled by doubts.
The individual's certainty is overridden by the judicial rejection's legal effect.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi says only qada; Shafi'i says qada + kaffarah.
This affects the person's financial/ritual obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ رَأَى هِلَالَ رَمَضَانَ وَحْدَهُ صَامَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْبَلِ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَتَهُ لِقَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم صُومُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ وَافْطِرُوا لِرُؤيَتِهِ وَقَدْ رَأَى ظَاهِراً وَإِنْ أَفْطَرَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَةِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ عَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ إِنْ أَفْطَرَ بِالْوِقَاعِ لِأَنَّهُ أَفْطَرَ فِي رَمَضَانَ حَقِيْقَةً بِيَقِينِهِ وَحُكْمًا لِوُجُوبِ الصَّوْمِ عَلَيْهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْقَاضِي رَدَّ شَهَادَتَهُ بِدَلِيلٍ شَرْعِيٍّ وَهُوَ تُهْمَةُ الْغَلَطِ فَأَوْرَثَ شُبْهَةً وَهَذِهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ تُدْرَأُ بِالشُّبُهَاتِ وَلَوْ أَفْطَرَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَرُدَّ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَتَهُ اخْتَلَفَ الْمَشَايِخُ فِيهِ وَلَوْ أَكْمَلَ هَذَا الرَّجُلُ ثَلَاثِينَ يَوْمًا لَمْ يُفْطِرْ إِلَّا مَعَ الْإِمَامِ إِنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عَلَيْهِ لِلْإِحْتِيَاطِ وَالْإِحْتِيَاطُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فِي تَأْخِيرِ الْإِفْطَارِ وَلَوْ أَفْطَرَ لَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ اعْتِبَارًا لِلْحَقِيقَةِ الَّتِي عِنْدَهُ
And whoever sees the crescent of Ramadan alone must fast, even if the imam does not accept his testimony, due to his (PBUH) saying: 'Fast upon its sighting and break your fast upon its sighting.' And he has indeed seen it apparently. And if he breaks his fast, then upon him is qada without kaffarah. Al-Shafi'i said: 'Upon him is kaffarah if he breaks his fast by intercourse, because he has broken it in Ramadan, in reality due to his certainty, and in ruling due to the obligation of fasting upon him.' Our proof: The judge rejected his testimony by a legal evidence, which is the suspicion of error, so it caused a doubt, and this kaffarah is repelled by doubts. And if he broke his fast before the imam rejected his testimony, the scholars differed concerning this. And if this man completed thirty days, he should not break his fast except with the imam; indeed, the obligation upon him was for precaution, and precaution after that lies in delaying the breaking of the fast. And if he broke his fast, no kaffarah is upon him, considering the reality that is with him.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling: If a single person sees the Ramadan crescent (moon) and the imam does not accept his testimony (perhaps due to lack of witnesses or suspicion of error), that person is still obligated to fast individually. The evidence is the Prophet's hadith commanding fasting based on sighting, and this person has indeed sighted it. If he breaks his fast (e.g., by eating or intercourse), he must make up the day (qada) but does not have to pay kaffarah (expiation). This is the Hanafi position. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that if he breaks it by intercourse, kaffarah is also required because in reality he is certain it is Ramadan, and by ruling the fast is obligatory on him. The Hanafi response: The imam's rejection of his testimony is based on a valid legal reason (suspicion of error), which creates a doubt (shubhah) in the certainty of Ramadan. Kaffarah is a penal expiation that is dropped by doubts (a legal maxim: 'al-hudud wa al-kaffarat tudra'u bi al-shubuhat'). Therefore, no kaffarah. The passage then addresses two subsidiary issues: 1) If he breaks his fast before the imam rejects his testimony, there is disagreement among Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) about the ruling. 2) If he completes 30 days of fasting (to be safe), he should not break his fast (for Eid) except with the imam, because his obligation was based on precaution; after completing 30 days, caution is to delay breaking until the imam does. If he breaks it, no kaffarah because he considered his own reality. The passage thus clarifies the delicate balance between individual certainty and communal authority, and the role of shubhah in dropping obligatory expiations.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt that prevents the application of penalties or expiations.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for intentional break of Ramadan fast by intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi school's response to the Shafi'i argument that kaffarah is due for lone moon sighting?
A) The person is not required to fast at all.
B) The imam's rejection creates a doubt that drops kaffarah.
C) The person must pay kaffarah but no qada.
D) The person must repeat the fast without any compensation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school drops kaffarah for lone moon sighting due to the legal doubt created by the imam's rejection, applying the principle that penalties are repelled by doubts.

Subsidiary Issues: Timing of Breaking Fast and Consensus with Imam
Presents subsidiary rulings on timing of breaking fast and consensus with imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on two subsidiary scenarios: (1) breaking the fast before the imam rejects testimony, and (2) completing 30 days and breaking only with the imam.

Core Idea
If fast is broken before imam's rejection, scholars differ; after 30 days, break only with imam but no kaffarah if broken alone.

After establishing the main ruling and the kaffarah dispute, the passage addresses two additional situations: a person who breaks his fast before the imam rejects his testimony, and a person who completes 30 days of fasting out of precaution. This lesson examines the Hanafi guidance on these scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first subsidiary issue
If a person breaks his fast before the imam rejects his testimony, the passage says 'the scholars (mashayikh) differed concerning this.'
This indicates an intra-Hanafi difference not fully detailed here.
2
Understand the second subsidiary issue
If the person completes 30 days of fasting (to be sure), he should not break his fast for Eid except with the imam (i.e., when the community declares Shawwal).
His original obligation was precautionary; now caution is to delay breaking.
3
Note the ruling if he breaks alone after 30 days
If he breaks his fast (by himself, not with the imam), no kaffarah is due, considering the reality that is with him (his own certainty that Ramadan ended).
This aligns with the principle that his own certainty is respected, and the doubt from imam's rejection is no longer present because 30 days have passed.

And whoever sees the crescent of Ramadan alone must fast, even if the imam does not accept his testimony, due to his (PBUH) saying: 'Fast upon its sighting and break your fast upon its sighting.' And he has indeed seen it apparently. And if he breaks his fast, then upon him is qada without kaffarah. Ruling on Solitary Witness of Ramadan Crescent and Kaffarah
Solitary witness of Ramadan crescent with inter-madhhab dispute on kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for a solitary witness who breaks his fast by intercourse, explain the shubhah rationale, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A solitary witness of Ramadan must fast even if rejected, but kaffarah is averted by the doubt arising from his testimony being rejected.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the expiation (kaffarah) required when a person who alone sees the Ramadan crescent intentionally breaks his fast. The key point is whether the certainty of the individual overrides the communal rejection of his testimony. The Hanafi position relies on the principle that penal sanctions are averted by doubts (shubuhat), a fundamental maxim in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic Hanafi ruling
Determine what the Hanafi school rules for a person who alone sees the Ramadan crescent, and what the obligation is if his testimony is rejected by the Imam.
The person must fast based on his own sighting, as per the hadith 'Fast upon seeing it' and Quran 2:183.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since the person is certain it is Ramadan and the Shariah obliges fasting upon him, breaking the fast requires both qada and kaffarah if by intercourse.
The dispute centres on whether kaffarah is averted by doubt.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response based on shubhah
The Hanafi school argues that the Imam's rejection, based on a legal evidence (accusation of error), creates a doubt (shubhah). Since kaffarah is akin to a hadd penalty, it is repelled by doubts.
Also the hadith 'The fast is the day you fast' indicates that communal practice affects obligation.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on a sub-case
If the person breaks the fast before the Imam rejects his testimony, some Mashayikh said kaffarah is due, but the correct (sahih) view is that even then kaffarah is not due because doubt already exists from the community not fasting.
The hadith 'al-sawmu yawma tasumoon' is cited to show communal fast defines obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference is that the Hanafi school spares the individual from the heavy expiation. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is no kaffarah in either case.
The text declares the latter view as 'sahih qawl'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے اکیلے رمضان کا چاند دیکھا اور امام نے اسکی گواہی قبول نہیں کی اس کے لئے روزہ رکھنے کا حکم وَمَنْ رَأَى هِلَالَ رَمَضَانَ وَحْدَهُ صَامَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْبَلِ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَتَهُ لِقَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم صُومُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ وَافْطِرُوا لِرُؤيَتِهِ وَ قَدْ رأى ظَاهِراً وَإِنْ اَفْطَرَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَةِ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ عَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ إِنْ أَفْطَرَ بِالْوِقَاعِ لِأَنَّهُ أَفْطَرَ فِي رَمَضَانَ حَقِيْقَةً لِيَقْبِهِ بِهِ وَ حُكْمًا لِوُجُوبِ الصَّوْمِ عَلَيْهِ وَلَنَا اَنَّ الْقَاضِي رَدَّ شَهَادَتَهُ بِدَلِيل شَرْعِي وَهُوَ تُهُمَةٌ الْغَلَطِ فَاوْرَثَ شُبْهَةٌ وَهَذِهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ تُندَرِئُ بِالشَّبُهَاتِ وَلَوْ اَفْطَرَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَرُدَّ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَتَهُ اخْتَلَفَ الْمَشَائِحُ فِيهِ وَلَوْ اكْمَلَ هَذَا الرَّجُلُ ثَلَاثِينَ يَوْمًا لَمْ يُقْطَرُ إِلَّا مَعَ الْإِمَامِ إِنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عَلَيْهِ لِلْإِحْتِيَاطِ وَالْإِحْتِيَاطُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فِي تَاخِيرِ الْإِفْطَارِ وَلَوْ اَفْطَرَ لَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ اعتبارا لِلْحَقِيقَةِ الَّتِي عِندَهُ ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے رمضان کا چاند تنہا دیکھا تو یہ شخص خود روزہ رکھے اگر چہ امام نے اس کی گواہی قبول نہ کی ہو کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ روزہ رکھو چاند دیکھ کر اور افطار کرو چاند دیکھ کر اور حال یہ کہ اس شخص نے ظاہر دیکھ لیا۔ اور اگر اس نے افطار کیا تو اس پر قضا واجب ہوگی نہ کہ کفارہ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر کفارہ بھی واجب ہے اگر اس نے جماع کے ساتھ افطار کیا ہو کیونکہ اس نے رمضان میں افطار کر لیا ہے حقیقتہ بھی اس لئے کہ اس کو رمضان کا یقین ہے اور حکما بھی اس لئے کہ اس پر روزہ واجب ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی نے اس کی شہادت کو دلیل شرعی سے رد کر دیا ہے اور دلیل شرعی غلطی کی تہمت ہے پس اس نے ایک طرح کا شبہ پیدا کر دیا اور یہ کفارہ شہبات کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور اگر افطار کیا امام کے اس کی شہادت کو رد کرنے سے پہلے تو اسمیں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے اور اگر اس آدمی نے تمیں روزے پورے کئے تو افطار نہ کرے مگر امام کے ساتھ کیونکہ اس پر پہلے روزہ کا وجوب احتیاط کی وجہ سے تھا اور اس کے بعد احتیاط تاخیر افطار میں ہے اور اگر افطار کیا تو اس پر کفارہ نہیں ہو گا اس حقیقت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے جو اسکے نزدیک ثابت ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے تنہا چاند دیکھا مطلع صاف تھا اور بیداری کی حالت میں ظاہر دیکھا نہ کہ خواب میں تو یہ شخص خود روزہ رکھے اگر چہ امام نے اس کی گواہی کسی وجہ سے قبول نہ کی ہو ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے صوموا لرؤيته وافطر والرؤيته پس جب اس کے حق میں رؤیت ہلال پائی گئی تو اس پر روزہ واجب ہو گیا نیز جب اس نے بیداری کی حالت میں ظاہر اچاند دیکھ لیا تو اس کے حق میں شہود شہر پایا گیا یعنی اس کے حق میں رمضان موجود ہو گیا اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا فَمَنْ شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمُهُ ( البقرة ۱۸۳) كم جس کے حق میں رمضان موجود ہو اس پر روزہ رمضان فرض ہو گیا پس آیت اور روایت دونوں اس کے بق میں وجوب صوم رمضان پر دلالت کرتے ہیں اور اگر اس شخص نے اس دن میں روزہ رکھ کر تو ڑ دیا اگر چہ جماع سے تو ڑا ہو تو اس پر اس روزہ کی قضاء واجب ہوگی نہ کہ کفارہ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر جماع سے اس روزہ کو تو ڑا ہے تو اس پر قضاء کے ساتھ کفارہ صوم بھی واجب ہوگا اور اگر کھانے پینے سے تو ڑا ہے تو اس پر کفارہ صوم واجب نہ ہوگا یہی قول امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص کے حق میں رمضان حقیقت بھی پایا گیا اور حکما بھی حقیقتا تو اس لئے کہ چاند دیکھنے کی وجہ سے اس کو رمضان کی آمد کا یقین ہو گیا اور حکماً اس لئے کہ شریعت نے اس پر روزہ واجب ہونے کا حکم کر دیا پس جب اس کے حق میں رمضان حقیقتا بھی موجود ہے اور حکما بھی موجود ہے تو گویا اس نے رمضان میں روزہ رکھ کر عدا توڑ ڈالا ۔ اور رمضان کے روزہ کو عمد اتو ڑنے کی وجہ سے قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے اس شخص پر قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوں گے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی نے جب اس کی شہادت کو رد کر دیا تو یہ شخص شرعاً مکذب ( تکذیب کیا ہوا) ہو گیا اور قاضی نے اس کی شہادت کو ر د بھی شرعی دلیل سے کیا ہے اور شرعی دلیل غلطی کی تہمت ہے کیونکہ مطلع صاف ہونے کے باوجود صرف اس کو چاند نظر آیا ہے اور کسی کو نظر نہیں آیا حالانکہ اس دن مسلمانوں کا ہجوم ہوتا ہے اور سب ہی چاند دیکھنے کی کوشش کرتے ہیں پس تنہا اس کو چاند کا نظر آنا اور دوسرے کسی کو نظر نہ آنا اس نے چاند نظر آنے میں ایک طرح کا شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور کفارہ شہادت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے لہذا اس صورت میں بھی اس شخص پر روزہ توڑنے کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر امام نے ابھی تک اس کی گواہی کو رد نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ اس شخص نے اس سے پہلے ہی روز چتوڑ ڈالا تو وجوب کفارہ کے سلسلہ میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے بعض نے کہا کہ اس صورت میں کفارہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ شبہ پیدا کرنے والا قاضی کا اسکی شہادت کو رد کرنا تھا اور قاضی کی طرف سے روشہادت پایا نہیں گیا اس لئے شبہ بھی پیدا نہیں ہوا اور جب ثبوت رمضان میں کوئی شبہ نہیں رہا تو رمضان میں روزہ توڑنے کی وجہ سے اس پر قضاء کے ساتھ کفارہ بھی واجب ہو گا لیکن صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شہادت کے رد ہونے سے پہلے بھی شبہ موجود ہے کیونکہ امام ترمزگی اور امام ابو داؤد نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے روایت کی ہے أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسَّلَامَ قَالَ الصَّوْمُ يَوْمَ تَصُومُونَ وَالْفِطْرُ يَوْمَ تُفْطِرُونَ یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس دن تم روزہ رکھو گے وہ دن روزہ کا ہے اور جس دن تم افطار کرو گے وہ دن افطار کا ہے حاصل یہ کہ جس دن عام لوگ روزہ رکھیں وہ صوم مفروض کا دن ہے اور جس دن عام لوگ افطار کریں وہ افطار مفروض کا دن ہے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرض روزہ تب ہی شمار ہوگا جبکہ عام لوگ اس دن روزہ رکھیں ۔ اور مذکورہ صورت میں عام لوگوں نے روزہ رکھا نہیں۔ اس لئے فرض روزہ بھی شمار نہ ہو گا۔ پس اس روزہ کے فرض ہونے میں شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور چونکہ شبہات کفارہ کو دفع کر دیتے ہیں اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی روزہ توڑنے کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
And the person who sees the crescent of Ramadan alone, he should fast even if the Imam does not accept his testimony, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Fast upon seeing it and break fast upon seeing it,' and he has seen it clearly. If he breaks the fast, then qada is obligatory upon him, not kaffarah. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Kaffarah is obligatory upon him if he breaks it by intercourse, because he has broken the fast in Ramadan both in reality, since he is certain of it, and legally, since fasting is obligatory upon him. Our evidence is that the Qadi rejected his testimony by a legal evidence, which is the accusation of error, so it creates a doubt, and this kaffarah is repelled by doubts. If he breaks the fast before the Imam rejects his testimony, the Mashayikh differed. If this person completes thirty days, he should not break his fast except with the Imam, because the obligation upon him was for caution, and caution after that is to delay breaking the fast. If he breaks it, there is no kaffarah upon him, considering the reality that is established according to him. Explanation of the issue: If someone sees the moon alone, the sky is clear, and he sees it clearly while awake, not in a dream, then this person should fast even if the Imam did not accept his testimony for whatever reason. The evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Fast upon seeing it and break fast upon seeing it.' So when sighting of the crescent is found in his case, fasting becomes obligatory upon him. Also, when he saw the moon clearly while awake, then the witnessing of the month is found in his case, i.e., Ramadan is present for him. Allah Almighty said: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Al-Baqarah 2:183). So for one who witnesses Ramadan, fasting Ramadan becomes fard upon him. So both the verse and the hadith indicate the obligation of fasting Ramadan for him. If this person fasted on that day and then broke it, even if he broke it by intercourse, then qada of that fast is obligatory upon him, not kaffarah. Imam al-Shafi'i said: If he broke it by intercourse, then kaffarah of fasting is also obligatory along with qada. But if he broke it by eating or drinking, then kaffarah of fasting is not obligatory. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that in his case, Ramadan is found both in reality and legally. In reality, because of seeing the moon, he becomes certain of the arrival of Ramadan; legally, because the Shariah has ruled that fasting is obligatory upon him. So when Ramadan is present for him both in reality and legally, it is as if he broke a fast in Ramadan. And for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory. Therefore, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory upon him. Our evidence is that when the Qadi rejected his testimony, this person becomes legally considered as having been accused of falsehood, and the Qadi rejected his testimony with a legal evidence, and the legal evidence is an accusation of error. Because even though the sky is clear, only he saw the moon, and no one else saw it, even though on that day there is a crowd of Muslims and all try to see the moon. So the fact that only he saw the moon and no one else saw it creates a kind of doubt in the sighting. And kaffarah is repelled by doubts. Therefore, in this case also, kaffarah is not obligatory upon him for breaking the fast. And if the Imam has not yet rejected his testimony, but this person broke the fast before that, then regarding the obligation of kaffarah, the Mashayikh differ. Some said that in this case kaffarah is obligatory because the doubt was created by the rejection of his testimony by the Qadi, and since the Qadi's rejection has not occurred, no doubt has been created. When there is no doubt in the confirmation of Ramadan, then for breaking the fast in Ramadan, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory upon him. But the correct saying is that in this case kaffarah is not obligatory because even before the rejection of testimony, there is doubt. Because Imam al-Tirmidhi and Imam Abu Dawud narrated from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The fast is the day you fast, and the breaking of the fast is the day you break the fast.' That is, the day the common people fast is the day of the prescribed fast, and the day the common people break the fast is the day of the prescribed breaking of the fast. This hadith indicates that a fard fast is only counted when the common people fast on that day. And in the mentioned case, the common people did not fast. Therefore, the fard fast is not counted. So doubt arises in the obligation of this fast. And since doubts repel kaffarah, therefore in this case also, kaffarah is not obligatory for breaking the fast.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling for a person who alone sees the Ramadan crescent (hilal) and whose testimony is rejected by the Imam (ruler or judge). The passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i, with additional intra-Hanafi discussion among later scholars (Mashayikh) on a related sub-case. The text begins by stating the default ruling: such a person must still fast, based on the hadith 'Fast upon seeing it and break fast upon seeing it' and the Quranic verse commanding fasting for those who witness the month. The obligation is individual and definite for him. However, if he breaks the fast (even by intercourse), he only owes qada (make-up) and not kaffarah (expiation). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if intercourse was the means of breaking, kaffarah is also wajib because the person has full certainty that it is Ramadan both in reality and legally. The Hanafi response is that the Imam's rejection of his testimony, based on a legal evidence (accusation of error), creates a shubhah (doubt). Since kaffarah is a hadd-like penalty, it is averted by doubts. The text then examines a sub-case: if the person breaks the fast before the Imam has rejected his testimony. Some scholars said kaffarah becomes wajib because no explicit shubhah exists yet. But the correct (sahih) view is that even then, no kaffarah is due because the fact that the general public is not fasting creates a shubhah about the month's confirmation, as indicated by the hadith 'The fast is the day you fast.' In summary, the Hanafi position is consistent: any shubhah removes kaffarah, which is based on the principle that hadd penalties (including kaffarah of Ramadan) are averted by doubts.

Key Terms
رؤية (ru'yah): Physical sighting of the new moon crescent with the naked eye.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt or uncertainty that arises from circumstantial evidence or procedural factors, sufficient to avert hadd and kaffarah penalties.
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory penalty for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast by intercourse, consisting of freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor.
صوم مظنون (sawm maznun): A fast kept under presumptive or uncertain conditions, such as on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk), where the obligation is not fully confirmed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, if a person sees the Ramadan crescent alone and his testimony is rejected by the Imam, what is required if he intentionally breaks his fast by intercourse?
A) Qada only, no kaffarah
B) Qada and kaffarah
C) Neither qada nor kaffarah
D) Only kaffarah, no qada

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that kaffarah for breaking a Ramadan fast is averted by any doubt (shubhah), such as the Imam's rejection of a solitary witness's testimony.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Solitary Moon Sighting and the Kaffarah Dispute
Explains ruling for solitary moon sighting and kaffarah dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a person who alone sights the moon, explain why kaffarah is dropped due to shubha, and compare the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is dropped by doubt: the imam’s rejection and the community’s non-sighting create shubha that prevents expiation.

Imagine you are the only person who sees the Ramadan crescent on a clear night. The imam does not accept your testimony. Do you still have to fast? And if you break that fast, do you owe expiation? This passage from al-Hidayah addresses these precise questions, revealing a key Hanafi principle: shubha (doubt) averts severe penalties like kaffarah. We will examine the ruling, the proofs, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Consider the case: a person sees the Ramadan moon alone while awake in a clear sky. The imam rejects his testimony for a valid reason. The person then fasts on that day but later breaks it intentionally.
The sky is clear and he is awake, so it is not a dream or cloudy confusion.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling on Fasting
The Hanafi school holds that this person must fast, even if his testimony is rejected. The proof is the hadith 'Fast upon seeing it' and the Quranic verse 'whoever witnesses the month, let him fast it.'
The obligation is wajib, not fard, because the community's testimony is lacking.
3
Analyse the Kaffarah Dispute
If he breaks the fast, does he owe qada only or both qada and kaffarah? The Hanafi school says only qada, due to shubha. Imam Shafi'i says kaffarah is required if broken by intercourse. Understand each side's proof.
The dispute centres on whether the doubt (shubha) is sufficient to drop kaffarah.
4
Examine the Hanafi Proof for Dropping Kaffarah
The Hanafi proof is twofold: (1) The imam's rejection of testimony creates legal doubt. (2) The hadith 'The fast is the day you fast' indicates that the obligatory fast is tied to the community. Since the community did not fast that day, there is shubha.
Shubha in the obligation of the fast repels kaffarah, as per the principle that penalties are averted by doubts.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i Proof and Response
Shafi'i argues that Ramadan is established both in reality (by his sighting) and legally (by the obligation to fast). Therefore it is a certain Ramadan fast, and breaking it intentionally requires kaffarah. The Hanafi response: the imam's rejection creates a legal obstacle (mani') that introduces doubt, and the community's non-participation further weakens certainty.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Hanafi – no kaffarah; Shafi'i – kaffarah if intercourse.
6
Apply to the Scenario Before Rejection
What if the person breaks the fast before the imam rejects his testimony? Some scholars said kaffarah is obligatory, but the correct Hanafi view is that it is still not obligatory, because even before rejection, the hadith about fasting with the community creates inherent doubt.
The sahih qawl (correct position) is no kaffarah in either scenario.

چاند دیکھنے کی کوشش کرتے ہیں پس تنہا اس کو چاند کا نظر آنا اور دوسرے کسی کو نظر نہ آنا اس نے چاند نظر آنے میں ایک طرح کا شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور کفارہ شہادت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے لہذا اس صورت میں بھی اس شخص پر روزہ توڑنے کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
اور اگر امام نے ابھی تک اس کی گواہی کو رد نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ اس شخص نے اس سے پہلے ہی روز چتوڑ ڈالا تو وجوب کفارہ کے سلسلہ میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے بعض نے کہا کہ اس صورت میں کفارہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ شبہ پیدا کرنے والا قاضی کا اسکی شہادت کو رد کرنا تھا اور قاضی کی طرف سے روشہادت پایا نہیں گیا اس لئے شبہ بھی پیدا نہیں ہوا اور جب ثبوت رمضان میں کوئی شبہ نہیں رہا تو رمضان میں روزہ توڑنے کی وجہ سے اس پر قضاء کے ساتھ کفارہ بھی واجب ہو گا لیکن صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شہادت کے رد ہونے سے پہلے بھی شبہ موجود ہے کیونکہ امام ترمزگی اور امام ابو داؤد نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے روایت کی ہے أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسَّلَامَ قَالَ الصَّوْمُ يَوْمَ تَصُومُونَ وَالْفِطْرُ يَوْمَ تُفْطِرُونَ یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس دن تم روزہ رکھو گے وہ دن روزہ کا ہے اور جس دن تم افطار کرو گے وہ دن افطار کا ہے حاصل یہ کہ جس دن عام لوگ روزہ رکھیں وہ صوم مفروض کا دن ہے اور جس دن عام لوگ افطار کریں وہ افطار مفروض کا دن ہے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرض روزہ تب ہی شمار ہوگا جبکہ عام لوگ اس دن روزہ رکھیں ۔ اور مذکورہ صورت میں عام لوگوں نے روزہ رکھا نہیں۔ اس لئے فرض روزہ بھی شمار نہ ہو گا۔ پس اس روزہ کے فرض ہونے میں شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور چونکہ شبہات کفارہ کو دفع کر دیتے ہیں اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی روزہ توڑنے کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
اب اگر اس شخص نے تمیں روزے پورے کر لئے اور امام اور عام مسلمانوں کے انتیس ہوئے ہیں اور انتیس رمضان کو عید کا چاند نظر نہیں آیا تو یہ شخص بھی یہ سمجھ کر کہ میرے تمیں روزے پورے ہو گئے ہیں افطار نہ کرے بلکہ امام کے ساتھ افطار کرے اور امام کے ساتھ اگلے دن کا روزہ رکھے۔ کیونکہ رمضان کا چاند اس کے تنہاء دیکھنے کی وجہ سے اس پر احتیاطاً روزہ واجب کیا گیا تھا نہ کہ قطعی فرض رمضان کا روزہ سمجھ کر واجب کیا گیا تھا اور یہاں افطار کی تاخیر میں احتیاط ہے کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ رمضان کے چاند میں اس کو دھوکا ہو گیا ہو یعنی پہلا روزہ جس کو اس نے رمضان کا روزہ سمجھ کر رکھا ہے وہ رمضان کا نہ ہو، بلکہ شعبان کا ہو تو اس کے بھی رمضان کے روزے انتیس ہوں گے لہذا احتیا طایہ شخص بھی امام وقت کے ساتھ افطار کرے۔ لیکن اس کے باوجود اگر اس نے اپنے تمیں روزے پورے کر کے نئے تنہا افطار کرلیا تو اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ میں روزے پورے کر کے اس شخص کو اپنے طور پر یقین ہے کہ آج عید کا دن ہے لہذ اشبہ عید کی وجہ سے اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Explanation of the issue: If someone alone saw the moon, the sky was clear, and he saw it clearly while awake, not in a dream, then this person should fast himself, even if the imam did not accept his testimony for some reason. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Fast upon seeing it and break fast upon seeing it.' So when sighting of the crescent is established for him, fasting becomes obligatory upon him. Also, when he saw the moon clearly while awake, then the witnessing of the month is established for him, meaning Ramadan is present for him. And Allah the Exalted said: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Al-Baqarah 185). For whomever Ramadan is present, fasting Ramadan becomes obligatory. So both the verse and the narration indicate the obligation of fasting Ramadan upon him. And if this person broke the fast on that day, even if by intercourse, then only qada (make-up) is obligatory upon him, not kaffarah. Imam Shafi'i said that if he broke it by intercourse, then both qada and kaffarah are obligatory; if by eating or drinking, then only qada. This is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that in his case, Ramadan is established both in reality and legally: in reality because by seeing the moon he became certain of Ramadan's arrival, and legally because the Shariah ruled that fasting is obligatory upon him. So when Ramadan is present both in reality and legally, it is as if he broke the fast during Ramadan intentionally, and for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory. Therefore, both are obligatory upon him. Our proof is that when the judge rejected his testimony, this person becomes legally rejected (mukadhdhab), and the judge rejected his testimony based on a legal evidence, and legal evidence creates a suspicion of error, because despite the clear sky, only he saw the moon and no one else, even though on that day there is a crowd of Muslims and all are looking for the moon. So his seeing the moon alone while others did not creates a kind of doubt (shubha) in the sighting, and kaffarah is dropped due to shubha. Therefore, in this case too, kaffarah is not obligatory upon him for breaking the fast. And if the imam has not yet rejected his testimony, but the person broke the fast before that, then regarding the obligation of kaffarah, there is a difference among the mashayikh. Some said that in this case kaffarah is obligatory, because the shubha was caused by the judge's rejection of his testimony, and since the rejection has not occurred, there is no shubha, and when there is no doubt about Ramadan being established, then breaking the fast in Ramadan requires both qada and kaffarah. But the correct view is that kaffarah is not obligatory in this case either, because even before the rejection of testimony, there is shubha. This is because Imam Tirmidhi and Imam Abu Dawud narrated from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The fast is the day you fast, and the breaking of fast is the day you break fast.' The meaning is that the day the general public fast is the day of obligatory fast, and the day they break fast is the day of obligatory breaking of fast. This hadith indicates that the obligatory fast is only considered when the general public fast. In the mentioned scenario, the general public did not fast, so the obligatory fast is not considered. Therefore, there is shubha in it being an obligatory fast, and since shubha repels kaffarah, kaffarah is not obligatory in this case either. Now, if this person completed thirty fasts and the imam and the general public had twenty-nine, and the moon for Eid was not sighted on the twenty-ninth, then this person should not break fast thinking his thirty are complete, but should break with the imam and fast the next day with the imam. Because fasting was made obligatory upon him out of caution due to his seeing the moon alone, not as an absolute obligatory Ramadan fast. And here delaying the breaking of fast is cautious, because it is possible he was deceived regarding the Ramadan moon, i.e., the first fast he thought was Ramadan might actually be from Sha'ban, so his Ramadan fasts would still be twenty-nine. Therefore, out of caution, this person should break with the imam. But if despite that, he broke fast alone after completing his thirty, no kaffarah is obligatory upon him, because after completing thirty fasts, this person is certain in his own view that today is Eid, so it resembles Eid, and due to that, kaffarah is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding a person who alone sights the crescent of Ramadan in a clear sky while awake. The ruling is stated with proof from Quran and Sunnah. The author first presents the Hanafi position: such a person must fast, even if the imam rejects his testimony. If he breaks the fast, he owes only qada (make-up), not kaffarah, due to the presence of shubha (doubt) because the imam's rejection based on legal evidence creates suspicion. Imam Shafi'i, along with Malik and Ahmad, holds that if he breaks by intercourse, both qada and kaffarah are required, since in his view Ramadan is established both in reality and legally. The Hanafi response argues that the rejection of testimony creates shubha, and kaffarah is dropped by shubha. The passage then discusses a scenario where the imam has not yet rejected the testimony: some scholars say kaffarah is obligatory, but the correct view (sahih qawl) is that it is not, because even before rejection, there is shubha from the hadith that the fast is with the general public. The author then addresses the case where the person completes thirty fasts while the public has twenty-nine: he should not break alone but follow the imam, because his fast was precautionary. If he breaks alone, no kaffarah because he genuinely believes it is Eid. The entire discussion emphasizes the Hanafi principle that shubuhat (doubts) prevent the application of kaffarah.

Key Terms
شبہ (shubha): A doubt or uncertainty that prevents the application of severe penalties like kaffarah.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast without valid excuse, typically fasting 60 days or feeding 60 poor.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or broken obligatory fast by fasting another day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person sees the Ramadan moon alone in a clear sky, the imam rejects his testimony, and he breaks the fast by intercourse, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He must perform qada only, no kaffarah.
B) He must perform both qada and kaffarah.
C) He must perform qada and kaffarah only if he ate, not if he had intercourse.
D) He does not need to do anything because his testimony was rejected.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school drops kaffarah for a person who alone sights the moon due to shubha, while the Shafi'i school requires it if broken by intercourse.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
12 min
Accepting One Witness for Moon Sighting in Cloudy Weather
States ruling on one witness for moon sighting with cloudy sky.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting a single witness for moon sighting when the sky is cloudy, explain the conditions of adalat and mastur al-hal, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
One just witness suffices for moon sighting when the sky is cloudy because it is a religious report like hadith.

The sighting of the crescent moon to begin Ramadan can be hindered by clouds or dust. The Hanafi school permits the imam to accept the testimony of a single upright person under such conditions, based on the precedent of the Prophet (peace be upon him). This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and an important intra-Hanafi debate on whether the fast is broken after 30 days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its basis
State the Hanafi position: the imam may accept one just witness (man or woman, free or slave) when the sky is obstructed. Understand the analogy to narrating hadith (riwayat al-akhbar).
2
Examine the required conditions
Determine that adalat (uprightness) is required; a fasiq's statement is not accepted. Note the nuance: mastur al-hal (concealed character) suffices per Imam Tahawi.
The text clarifies that 'illah' includes clouds, dust, and similar obstructions.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on qadhf
Contrast Zahir al-Riwayah (accepts testimony of a repentant qadhf criminal as khabar) with Abu Hanifa's narration (rejects as shahadah).
This shows how the classification as khabar vs. shahadah affects acceptance.
4
Evaluate the Shafi'i dispute
Understand Shafi'i's requirement of two witnesses and the Hanafi rebuttal using the authentic hadith of the Prophet accepting one witness.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi accepts one witness; Shafi'i requires two in one opinion.
5
Apply the ruling to the post-30-day fast dilemma
Consider the difference between Hasan's narration from Abu Hanifa (do not break fast out of caution) and Muhammad's view (break fast by analogy to inheritance). Understand the principle: establishment of Ramadan by one witness does not automatically establish its end.
This demonstrates how caution (ihtiyat) operates in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلع ابر آلود ہو اور امام رمضان کے چاند میں ایک عادل کو گواہی قبول کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں
وَإِذَا كَانَ بِالسَّمَاءِ عِلَّةٌ قَبلَ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَةَ الْوَاحِدِ الْعَدْلِ فِى رُؤيَةِ الْهَلَالِ رَجُلا كَانَ أَوِ امْرَأَةً حُرًّا كَانَ أَوْ عَبْدًا لأنَّهُ أَمْرٌ دِينِيٌّ فَاشْبَهَ رِوَايَةَ الْأَخْبَارِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يُخْتَصُّ بِلَفْظِ الشَّهَادَةِ وَتُشْتَرَطُ الْعَدَالَةُ لِأَنَّ قَوْلَ الْفَاسِقِ فِي الدِّيَانَاتِ غَيْرُ مَقْبُولِ وَتَاوِيلُ قَوْلِ الطَّحَاوِي عَدْلًا كَانَ أَوْ غَيْرَ عَدْلٍ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَسْتُورًا وَالْعِلَّةُ غَيْمٌ أَوْ غُبَارٌ وَنَحْوَهُ فِي إِطْلَاقِ جَوَابِ الْكِتَابِ يَدْخُلُ الْمَحْدُودُ فِى الْقَذَفِ بَعْدَمَا تَابَ وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ الرِّوَايَةِ لِأَنَّهُ خَبَرٌ وَعَنْ أبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهَا لَا تُقْبَلُ لَا نَّهَا شَهَادَةً مِنْ وَجْهِ وَكَانَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِي اَحَدٍ قَوْلَيْهِ يَشْتَرِطُ الْمَثْنَى وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرُنَا وَ قَدْ صَحٌ أَنَّ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَبِلَ شَهَادَةَ الْوَاحِدِ فِى رُؤْيَةِ هِلَالِ رَمَضَانَ ثُمَّ إِذَا قَبِلَ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَةَ الْوَاحِدِ وَ صَامُوا ثَلاثِينَ يَوْمًا لَا يُفْطِرُوْنَ فِيْمَا رَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِلِاحْتِيَاطِ وَلانَّ الْفِطْرَ لَا يَثْبُتُ بشَهَادَةِ الْوَاحِدِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُمْ يُفْطِرُونَ وَيَثْبُتُ الْفِطْرُ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ ثُبُوتَ الرَّمْضَانِيَّةِ بِشَهَادَةِ الْوَاحِدِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يَثْبُتُ لَهَا ابْتِدَاءً كَاسْتِحْقَاقِ الْإِرْثِ بِنَاءً عَلَى النَّسَب الثَّابِتِ بِشَهَادَةِ الْقَابلَةِ
ترجمہ اور جب آسمان پر کوئی علت ( بادل، غبار یا دھواں ) ہو تو مسلمین چاند دیکھنے کے بارے میں ایک عادل آدمی کی گواہی قبولے خواہ وہ مرد ہو یا عورت آزاد ہو یا مملوک کیونکہ یہ دینی معاملہ ہے لہذا روایت حدیث کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور اسی وجہ سے رؤیت ہلال کی گواہی لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے اور عادل ہونا شرط ہے کیونکہ دینی باتوں میں فاسق کا قول معتبر نہیں ہوتا اور امام طحاوی کے قول عدلاً كَانَ أَوْ غَيْرَ عَدْلٍ کی مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ مستور الحال ہو اور علت ابر ہے یا غبار یا اس کے مانند اور حکم کتاب کے اطلاق میں تو بہ کر لینے کے بعد محدود فی القذف بھی داخل ہو جاتا ہے اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے کیونکہ یہ خبر ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ محدود فی القذف کی شہادت قبول نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہ من وجہ شہادت ہے اور امام شافعی اپنے دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول میں دو کی شرط لگاتے تھے اور ان کے خلاف حجت وہ دلیل ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی اور یہ ثابت ہے کہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے رمضان کی رویت ہلال میں ایک آدمی کی شہادت قبول فرمائی ہے پھر جب امام نے ایک آدمی کی گواہی قبول کی، اور لوگوں نے تمیں روزے رکھ لئے تو وہ افطار نہ کریں، اس روایت کے مطابق جوحسن بن زیاد نے امام ابو حنیفہ سے کی ہے (اس روایت کا مبنی) احتیاط پر ہے اور اس لئے کہ افطار ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے اور امام محمد
When the sky has an obstruction (cloud, dust, etc.): the imam may accept the testimony of a single just person for sighting the crescent, whether the person is a man or woman, free or slave, because it is a religious matter, so it resembles the narration of hadith. For this reason, it is not restricted to the wording of shahadah, and uprightness (adalat) is required because the statement of a sinner is not accepted in religious matters. The interpretation of Imam Tahawi's statement 'whether just or not just' is that the person should be of concealed character (mastur al-hal). The obstruction (illah) includes clouds, dust, and the like. In the general application of the ruling of the book, the person who was punished for qadhf (false accusation of adultery) after repenting is included, and this is Zahir al-Riwayah because it is a khabar (report). From Abu Hanifa it is narrated that it is not accepted because it is a shahadah from one aspect. Imam Shafi'i in one of his two opinions stipulates two witnesses, and the proof against him is what we mentioned. It is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of a single individual for sighting the hilal of Ramadan. Then, when the imam accepts the testimony of a single person and they fast thirty days, they do not break the fast according to what Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, for caution and because breaking the fast is not established by the testimony of a single person. And from Muhammad, they break the fast, and the breaking is established based on the fact that the establishment of Ramadan is by the testimony of one, even if it is not established initially, like the entitlement to inheritance based on lineage established by the testimony of a midwife. Translation: And when there is an obstruction (cloud, dust, or smoke) in the sky, then the imam accepts the testimony of one just person regarding the sighting of the moon, whether that person is a man or woman, free or slave, because it is a religious matter, so it resembles the narration of hadith. For this reason, the testimony for moon sighting is not restricted to the wording of shahadah, and uprightness is a condition because the statement of a sinner is not acceptable in religious matters. The meaning of Imam Tahawi's statement 'whether just or not just' is that the person is of concealed character. The obstruction is clouds, dust, or the like. In the general application of the ruling of the book, a person who was punished for qadhf after repenting is also included, and this is Zahir al-Riwayah because it is a khabar. From Imam Abu Hanifa it is narrated that his testimony is not accepted because it is a shahadah from one aspect. Imam Shafi'i in one of his two opinions stipulates two witnesses, and the proof against him is what we mentioned. It is established that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of one person for the sighting of the hilal of Ramadan. Then, when the imam accepts the testimony of one person, and the people fast thirty days, they do not break the fast according to the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa, based on caution and because breaking the fast is not established by the testimony of one. And from Muhammad, they break the fast, and the breaking is established based on the fact that the establishment of Ramadan is by the testimony of one, even if it is not established initially, like the entitlement to inheritance based on lineage established by the testimony of a midwife.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when the sky is cloudy (or dusty, etc.) for moon sighting. It states that the imam can accept the testimony of one just person, regardless of gender or status, because this is a religious matter analogous to narrating hadith. Thus, the technical wording of 'shahadah' is not required; a simple report suffices. The condition of 'adalat (uprightness) is necessary because a fasiq's word is not trusted in religious matters. The passage explains Imam Tahawi's view that 'just or not just' means the person should be 'mastur al-hal' (of concealed character), i.e., not known for sin. It then addresses the issue of a person who was punished for qadhf (false accusation of adultery) after repenting: according to Zahir al-Riwayah, his testimony is accepted because it is considered a report (khabar). But Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration that it is not accepted because it is a shahadah from one aspect. The text also mentions Imam Shafi'i's opinion requiring two witnesses, and rebuts it with the hadith that the Prophet accepted one witness. The passage concludes with an intra-Hanafi difference: after accepting one witness and fasting 30 days, should they break fast? According to Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration from Abu Hanifa, they do not break out of caution because fast-breaking is not established by a single witness. Imam Muhammad holds that they do break, analogizing to inheritance established by a midwife's testimony.

Key Terms
علت (illah): An obstruction in the sky such as clouds, dust, or smoke that hinders moon sighting.
عدالت (adalat): Uprightness or righteousness of a person; necessary for testimony to be accepted.
مستور الحال (mastur al-hal): A person whose internal state is concealed, i.e., not outwardly sinful; acceptable in religious reports.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on accepting a single witness for moon sighting when the sky is cloudy?
A) Not accepted under any circumstances.
B) Accepted only if the witness is a free male.
C) Accepted provided the witness is just (or mastur al-hal) and the obstruction is present.
D) Accepted only if two witnesses are available.

Key Takeaway
When the sky is cloudy, the Hanafi school accepts a single upright witness for Ramadan moon sighting because it is a religious report analogous to hadith narration.

Sawm — Fasting

Following the Imam for Eid When Personal Count Differs
Ruling on obligation to follow imam for Eid if personal count differs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who sighted the Ramadan crescent alone when the public has 29 days, and explain why no kaffarah is due if he breaks fast alone.

Core Idea
Solitary crescent sighting creates a precautionary obligation – follow the imam for Eid.

Imagine a reliable person sighted the Ramadan crescent alone and started fasting accordingly. After completing 30 fasts, the imam and the public have only 29 days and no Eid crescent is seen. Does he celebrate Eid alone? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling that balances personal certainty with communal practice, rooted in the principle of ihtiyat (precaution).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the conflict
Note the key facts: a solitary sighting leads to an obligation to fast; the person completes 30 fasts; the imam and public have 29 days with no Eid crescent. The conflict is between the person’s count and the public’s count.
The person’s count could be erroneous if his initial sighting was of Shaban, not Ramadan.
2
Understand the nature of the obligation (wajib ihtiyatan)
Hanafi fiqh holds that the fasting obligation from a solitary sighting is wajib ihtiyatan (precautionary), not fard qat'i (definitive). This means it is not the absolute fard of Ramadan but a duty imposed to avoid missing Ramadan. Hence, it can be overridden by precaution in case of doubt.
This distinction is crucial: a qat'i obligation cannot be overridden, but a zanni one can.
3
Apply the precautionary principle
Since the public count is 29 and no Eid crescent is sighted, there is a possibility that the person’s initial sighting was mistaken. To avoid breaking Ramadan incorrectly, he must break fast with the imam and fast the next day with the public. This is ihtiyat – delaying iftar to ensure the fast is not broken prematurely.
The text says ‘it is possible he was mistaken’ – thus following the imam is the safe path.
4
Examine the consequence if he acts on his own certainty
If the person breaks fast alone after completing his 30 days, thinking it is definitely Eid, no kaffarah (expiation) is due. Because he acted based on personal certainty (yaqin), it resembles the situation of someone who mistakenly believes it is Eid – in that analogy, no expiation.
This is a concession: the protection from kaffarah is due to his sincere certainty, even though he should have followed the imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اب اگر اس شخص نے تمیں روزے پورے کر لئے اور امام اور عام مسلمانوں کے انتیس ہوئے ہیں اور انتیس رمضان کو عید کا چاند نظر نہیں آیا تو یہ شخص بھی یہ سمجھ کر کہ میرے تمیں روزے پورے ہو گئے ہیں افطار نہ کرے بلکہ امام کے ساتھ افطار کرے اور امام کے ساتھ اگلے دن کا روزہ رکھے۔ کیونکہ رمضان کا چاند اس کے تنہاء دیکھنے کی وجہ سے اس پر احتیاطاً روزہ واجب کیا گیا تھا نہ کہ قطعی فرض رمضان کا روزہ سمجھ کر واجب کیا گیا تھا اور یہاں افطار کی تاخیر میں احتیاط ہے کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ رمضان کے چاند میں اس کو دھوکا ہو گیا ہو یعنی پہلا روزہ جس کو اس نے رمضان کا روزہ سمجھ کر رکھا ہے وہ رمضان کا نہ ہو، بلکہ شعبان کا ہو تو اس کے بھی رمضان کے روزے انتیس ہوں گے لہذا احتیاطا یہ شخص بھی امام وقت کے ساتھ افطار کرے۔ لیکن اس کے باوجود اگر اس نے اپنے تمیں روزے پورے کر کے نئے تنہا افطار کرلیا تو اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ میں روزے پورے کر کے اس شخص کو اپنے طور پر یقین ہے کہ آج عید کا دن ہے لہذا اشبہ عید کی وجہ سے اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Now if this person has completed his thirty days, and the imam and the general Muslims have twenty-nine days, and on the twenty-ninth of Ramadan the Eid crescent is not sighted, then this person, even thinking that his days are complete, should not break the fast, but should break with the imam and fast the next day with the imam. Because the Ramadan crescent was made obligatory upon him as a precaution due to his solitary sighting, not as an absolute fard of Ramadan. And here delaying iftar is precautionary because it is possible he was mistaken about the Ramadan crescent, i.e., the first fast he kept thinking it was Ramadan might not be Ramadan but Shaban, so his Ramadan fasts would also be twenty-nine. Therefore, as a precaution, this person should break fast with the imam of the time. However, if despite this he breaks fast alone after completing his days, no kaffarah is obligatory upon him, because he has certainty in his own mind that today is Eid, so it resembles Eid, and therefore kaffarah is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah expounds a ruling about a person who sighted the Ramadan crescent alone. Such a person is obliged to fast based on his solitary sighting, but this obligation is precautionary (wajib ihtiyatan) rather than a definitive fard (fard qat'i) of Ramadan. If the imam and the general public have only twenty-nine days and no Eid crescent is seen, this person must still break his fast with the imam and fast the next day. The reasoning is precaution: his initial sighting might have been mistaken; perhaps what he thought was the Ramadan crescent was actually Shaban's, so his fasts would actually be twenty-nine. Therefore, he must follow the imam to avoid error. However, if he breaks fast alone based on his own count, no expiation (kaffarah) is due, because he acted on personal certainty, resembling the case of someone who mistakenly believes it is Eid, for whom no kaffarah is imposed.

Key Terms
احتیاطاً (ihtiyāṭan): As a precaution; the obligation is precautionary, not absolute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a person who sighted the Ramadan crescent alone, completed 30 fasts, while the imam and public have 29 days with no Eid crescent?
A) He must break fast alone because his count is complete.
B) He must break fast with the imam and fast the next day; if he breaks alone, no kaffarah.
C) He must break fast alone and perform kaffarah for breaking Ramadan.
D) He must continue fasting until the imam confirms Eid.

Key Takeaway
A solitary crescent sighting creates a precautionary obligation that yields to communal practice; if one acts alone out of certainty, no expiation is imposed.

Accepting a Single Witness for Crescent Sighting in Cloudy Weather
Ruling with proof on accepting one witness for crescent sighting when sky cloudy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of witnesses required for crescent sighting when the sky is cloudy and explain the proof from hadith and analogy to hadith narration.

Core Idea
Crescent sighting is a religious report, not a formal testimony, so one just witness suffices.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah expands on a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding crescent sighting when the sky is obstructed. It clarifies that crescent sighting is treated as a religious matter (amr dīnī) akin to narrating hadith, not as formal testimony (shahādah). Therefore, the strict conditions of testimony—such as number, freedom, and gender—are relaxed, but justice (ʿadālah) remains required. The text also addresses inter-madhhab disputes with the Shafiʿi school and intra-Hanafi differences regarding the acceptance of a repentant slanderer and whether to break fast after 30 days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (the imam's acceptance of a witness for crescent sighting) and the hukm level (permissible/recommended).
The text begins with 'When the sky has an obstruction, the imam accepts the testimony of one just person.'
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepting a single witness for Ramadan crescent.
The dalil is a sunnah ahad but its meaning is decisive (qatʿī al-dalālah) for the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
Explain how the proof leads to the ruling: the Prophet's acceptance shows that one just person suffices; sighting is analogous to hadith narration, so it is a religious report not a testimony.
The text also argues by analogy: 'because it is a religious matter, so it resembles the narration of reports.'
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Identify the opposing view (Shafiʿi requires two witnesses) and the intra-Hanafi dispute about the repentant slanderer and breaking fast after 30 days.
The text mentions Ibn al-Qāsim's narration from Mālik and one opinion of al-Shāfiʿī requiring two witnesses.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
Determine which position is relied upon: the Hanafi position is accepted because of the hadith and the analogy to narration; the precautionary view for breaking fast is preferred.
The apparent narration (ẓāhir al-riwāyah) includes the repentant slanderer, though Abu Hanifa has a dissenting view.

مردود ہے یعنی لفظ غیر مقبول کی جگہ مردود کا لفظ کیوں استعمال نہیں فرمایا۔ جواب: اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فاسق کا قول مطلقا مر دود نہیں ہوتا بلکہ موقوف رہتا ہے کہ اگر تحقیق کے بعد اس کے قول کا صادق ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو مقبول ہوگا اور اگر کا ذب ہونا ثابت ہوا تو رد کر دیا جائے گا چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے يَايُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِن جَاءَكُمْ فَاسِقٌ بِنَا فَتَبَيَّنُوا (الحجرات : 4 ) یعنی اے ایمان والو! اگر آئے تمہارے پاس کوئی گنہگار خبر لے کر تو تحقیق کر لو۔ بہر حال ہلال رمضان کے سلسلہ میں فاسق کا قول قبول نہ ہو گا اس پر ائمہ اور علماء کا اتفاق ہے لیکن امام طحاوی سے روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ ہلال رمضان میں ایک آدمی کا قول قبول ہے خواہ وہ عادل ہو یا غیر عادل ہو اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امام طحاوی کے نزدیک غیر عادل یعنی فاسق کا قول قبول کر لیا جائے گا حالانکہ امام طحاوی کے نزدیک بھی فاسق کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جاتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام طحاوی کے اس قول کی تاویل بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ امام طحاوی کے قول عادل سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس کا عادل اور پرہیز گار ہونا لوگوں میں معروف و مشہور ہو۔ اور غیر عادل سے یہ مراد ہے کہ لوگوں میں معروف نہ ہو ۔ بلکہ اس کا حال مستور اور پوشیدہ ہو پس غیر عادل سے مستور الحال مراد ہے فاسق مراد نہیں ہے اب حاصل یہ ہوا کہ امام طحاوی کے نزدیک روایت ہلال میں اس شخص کا قول بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا جس کی عدالت لوگوں میں معروف ومشہور ہو اور اس کا قول بھی قبول ہوگا جس کی عدالت مستور اور پوشیدہ ہو لیکن جس کا فاسق ہونا لوگوں میں مشتہر ہو اس کا قول حضرت امام طحاورتی کے نزدیک بھی قبول نہ ہوگا ۔ علت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ آسمان پر ابر دیا غبار ہو یا دھواں وغیرہ ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کی عبادت قَبلَ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَةَ الْوَاحِدِ الْعَدْلِ كا مطلقا ہونا اس بات کی نشاندہی کرتا ہے کہ
Subheading: When the sky is cloudy, can the imam accept the testimony of one just person for the crescent of Ramadan?
And when the sky has an obstruction, the imam accepts the testimony of one just person concerning the sighting of the crescent, whether it be a man or a woman, free or slave, because it is a religious matter, so it resembles the narration of reports. For this reason, it is not restricted to the word 'shahadah'. Justice (adalah) is required because the word of a sinner in religious matters is not accepted. The interpretation of Imam al-Tahawi's statement 'whether just or not just' is that he is maskur (concealed status). And the obstruction is cloud, dust, or the like. In the absolute ruling of the book, the one hadd-punished for slander after repentance enters [into acceptance], and this is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) because it is a khabar. And from Abu Hanifa that it is not accepted because it is a testimony in one respect. And al-Shafi'i in one of his two opinions stipulates two witnesses. The proof against him is what we mentioned. And it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of one person concerning sighting of the crescent of Ramadan. Then when the imam accepts the testimony of one and they fast thirty days, they do not break fast according to what Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, as a precaution and because breaking fast is not established by the testimony of one. And from Muhammad that they break fast and breaking fast is established based on the establishment of Ramadan by one witness, even though it is not established initially, like entitlement to inheritance based on lineage established by the testimony of a midwife.
Then the Urdu commentary provides detail: When there is a cloud or dust or smoke, the imam can accept the testimony of one just person, male or female, free or slave. The condition of justice is required. The interpretation of Tahawi's statement is that 'just' means well-known for justice, and 'not just' means maskur al-hal (concealed), not a known sinner. The obstruction means cloud, dust, or similar. The absolute form in the text includes the one punished for slander after repentance in the apparent narration. There is a dispute: Abu Hanifa does not accept it because it is partly a testimony. Al-Shafi'i in one opinion requires two. The proof is the hadith. Then there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, if they fasted 30 days based on one witness, they do not break fast as precaution. According to Muhammad, they break fast based on the establishment of Ramadan by one witness. The commentary then explains the reasoning, discusses the meaning of 'non-accepted' versus 'rejected' for a sinner, cites Quran 49:6, and concludes that the statement of a sinner is not absolutely rejected but suspended until verification. It also clarifies Tahawi's interpretation that 'non-just' means maskur, not a known sinner. Finally, the author of Hidayah says that the absolute wording of Quduri's 'the imam accepts the testimony of one just person' indicates... (cut off).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion of a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the acceptance of a single witness for crescent sighting when the sky is cloudy. The text begins with the Arabic matn stating that the imam accepts the testimony of one just person, male or female, free or slave, because it is a religious matter (amr dini) analogous to hadith narration. Therefore, the strict conditions for testimony in worldly matters (such as the word 'shahadah', number, freedom, and masculinity) are not required. However, justice (adalah) is required because a sinner's word is not accepted in religious matters. The commentary then addresses several points: (1) The interpretation of Imam al-Tahawi's statement that 'whether just or not just' refers to a maskur al-hal (one whose justice is not publicly known) not a known sinner. (2) The inclusion of a person who was hadd-punished for slander after repentance is accepted in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) because it is a khabar (report), though Abu Hanifa reportedly does not accept it because it is partly a testimony. (3) The dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i who in one of his two opinions requires two witnesses. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepting the testimony of one person for Ramadan crescent. (4) An intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration from Abu Hanifa, if the imam accepted one witness and they fasted 30 days, they do not break fast because breaking fast is not established by a single witness. According to Imam Muhammad, they do break fast because Ramadan is established by one witness, and breaking fast follows from that, analogous to inheritance based on lineage established by a midwife's testimony. (5) The commentary also clarifies why the text uses 'non-accepted' (ghayr maqbul) rather than 'rejected' (mardud) for a sinner's statement: it is not absolutely rejected but suspended until verification, citing Quran 49:6. (6) The absolute wording of al-Quduri's matn indicates that the ruling applies even without specifying the presence of obstruction, but the passage ends abruptly.

Key Terms
عدالت (ʿadālah): Justice; the quality of being upright and avoiding major sins, required for acceptance in religious matters.
مستور الحال (mastūr al-ḥāl): One whose state of justice is concealed; i.e., not publicly known as just or sinful.
علت (ʿillah): Obstruction in the sky such as cloud, dust, or smoke that prevents clear sighting of the crescent.
خبر (khabar): Report; crescent sighting is considered a report (khabar) not a formal testimony (shahādah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school accept the testimony of one person for Ramadan crescent sighting when the sky is cloudy?
A) Because it is a worldly matter and one witness suffices in emergencies.
B) Because it is a religious matter analogous to hadith narration, and the Prophet accepted one witness.
C) Because the Quran explicitly states one witness is enough.
D) Because there is no alternative, everyone must rely on a single witness.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, crescent sighting is a religious report (khabar), so one just witness suffices when the sky is cloudy, unlike formal testimony requiring two witnesses.

Principle: Fitr Proven Subordinately by One Witness for Ramadan
Ruling statement on subordinate proof of Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the day of Eid al-Fitr is proven subordinately when Ramadan was established by a single witness, and explain the analogy to inheritance.

Core Idea
Eid is proven subordinately by the same witness who proved Ramadan — just as lineage is proven by a midwife's testimony.

This short but powerful passage encapsulates a key Hanafi principle in the chapter of fasting: the day of Eid al-Fitr (fitr) does not need independent proof if it follows a Ramadan that was established by the testimony of a single witness. The ruling draws an elegant analogy to inheritance law, where lineage can be established through the testimony of a single midwife. Understanding this principle helps you see how Hanafi fiqh applies subordinate proof (thubut dhimnan) in multiple areas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the determination of the day of Eid al-Fitr. The ruling is that it is proven as subordinate to Ramadan's proof.
The passage states: 'the proof of Fitr will be established on the basis of the proof of Ramadan by the testimony of one person.'
2
Note the condition
This applies only when Ramadan was proven by a single witness (khabar wahid). Fitr is not proven initially by one witness.
The text says: 'although initially the proof of Fitr is not established by the testimony of one person.'
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The passage compares this to inheritance: the right to inherit is based on lineage, which can be proven by a single midwife's testimony.
The analogy shows that subordinate proof is valid in Hanafi law for certain derivative rights.
4
Derive the underlying principle
Subordinate proof (thubut al-shay' bi al-taba') is valid in Hanafi law for certain rights even when the same evidence would not suffice for initial establishment.
This principle is later expanded in discussions about completing 30 days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مروی ہے کہ لوگ افطار کریں اور ایک آدمی کی شہادت سے رمضان کے ثبوت کی بنیاد پر فطر کا ثبوت ہو جائے گا اگر چہ ابتداء ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے فطر کا ثبوت نہیں ہوتا جیسے وراثت کا استحقاق منی ہے اس نسب پر جو دایہ کہ شہادت سے ثابت ہے۔
It is narrated that people break the fast and the proof of Fitr (Eid) will be established on the basis of the proof of Ramadan by the testimony of one person, although initially the proof of Fitr is not established by the testimony of one person, just as the entitlement to inheritance is from that lineage which is established by the testimony of a midwife?
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This is a short ruling statement summarizing a key Hanafi principle for the case where Ramadan was started on the testimony of one witness. The ruling states that the people break the fast (perform Eid) based on that same one witness, even though initially the day of Fitr cannot be proven by one witness alone. The reason is that the day of Fitr is proven subordinately (dhimnan) through the proof of Ramadan. This is analogous to inheritance rights: the entitlement to inheritance depends on proven lineage, which may itself be established by the testimony of a midwife or a single witness. Just as lineage can be proven subordinately by one witness in certain cases, so too is the day of Fitr proven subordinately. This statement serves as the foundational principle for the more detailed discussion in the subsequent lesson about completing thirty days. It reflects Imam Muhammad's view that after thirty days have passed since the start of Ramadan (established by one witness), the next day is automatically Eid, even if the moon was not sighted on the previous night.

Key Terms
فطر (fitr): Breaking the fast; specifically the day of Eid al-Fitr.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony; here it refers to a single witness's report about the moon sighting.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or parentage; legal relationship through birth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this statement, on what basis is the day of Fitr (Eid) proven?
A) Direct testimony of two witnesses for Eid
B) The same single testimony that proved Ramadan, after completing 30 days
C) Astronomical calculation
D) The announcement of the judge

Key Takeaway
The day of Fitr is proven not independently, but as a subordinate consequence of the proof of Ramadan by one witness.

Moon Sighting: One Witness or Two? The Hanafi Position
Inter-madhhab dispute on number of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Ramadan moon sighting with one witness when cloudy, and explain the Hanafi distinction between khabar and shahada in refuting the opposing school.

Core Idea
Moon sighting is a religious report, not a court testimony — one reliable witness suffices when the sky is unclear.

This lesson examines the inter-madhhab dispute on the number of witnesses required for the sighting of the Ramadan moon. The Hanafi school holds that one reliable witness is sufficient when the sky is not clear, while Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i require two witnesses. We will explore the textual evidence and the key distinction between narration (khabar) and testimony (shahada).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State that the Hanafi school accepts one reliable witness ('adl) for Ramadan moon sighting when the sky is cloudy, and the witness can be male/female, free/slave. The only condition is 'adala.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Identify the opposing school and their argument
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i (in one opinion) require two witnesses because they consider moon sighting a shahada (judicial testimony).
Their dalil is that Quran and Sunnah require two witnesses for shahada in general.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: khabar vs shahada
The Hanafi school argues that moon sighting is a religious matter (amr dini) analogous to hadith narration, which is accepted from one person. The word 'shahada' in the relevant hadith is not literal but informational.
The hadith of the bedouin is cited as direct proof that the Prophet accepted one person's testimony.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, if one reliable witness reports the moon, the community must fast. Under Shafi'i/Maliki, they wait for two witnesses.
This affects millions of Muslims in cloudy regions.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on the hadith and analogy to khabar. The opposing view is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text
