توبہ کے بعد محدود فی القذف کا قول بھی رؤیت هلال میں قابل قبول اور معتبر ہوگا اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے کیونکہ چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی دینا در حقیقت خبر ہے نہ کہ شہادت اور توبہ کے بعد چونکہ محدود فی القذف عادل ہو گیا اس لئے رویت ہلال کی خبر دینے میں اس کا قول قبول ہوگا ۔ اور یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ ابو بکرۃ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ جو محدود فی القذف تھے تو بہ کر لینے کے بعد رؤیت ہلال میں صحابہ نے ان کے قول کو قبول کیا ہے۔ (الکفایہ) امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک رؤیت هلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول معتبر نہیں : امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ رؤیت هلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ رویت ہلال کی خبر من وجہ شہادت ہے بایں طور کہ اس خبر پر عمل کرنا قضاء قاضی کے بعد واجب ہوگا اور اس کا اختصاص بھی مجلس قضاء کے ساتھ ہے اور مخبر کے لئے عدالت کی شرط ہے یہ سب باتیں شہادت ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہیں اور محدود فی القذف کی شہادت تو بہ کے بعد بھی قبول نہیں کی جاتی چنانچہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ولا تُقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً اَبَدًا یعنی ان کی کوئی گواہی بھی نہ مانو یعنی نہ تو بہ سے پہلے اور نہ تو بہ کے بعد ۔ امام شافعی نے اپنے ایک قول میں جو یہ کہا ہے کہ رؤیت هلال دو آدمیوں کی شہادت سے ثابت ہوگی تو امام شافعی کے خلاف اولا تو وہ دلیل حجت ہے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے کہ یہ امر دینی ہے پس روایت احادیث کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے رمضان کے چاند کی رویت میں ایک آدمی کی شہادت کا قبول کرنا ثابت ہے چنانچہ حدیث ہے قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسِ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا جَاءَ أَعْرَابِيٌّ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ إِنِّي رَأَيْتُ الْهَلالَ يَعْنِي هَلالَ رَمَضَانَ فَقَالَ أَتَشْهَدُانْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ أَتَشْهَدَانُ مُحَمَّدًا رَّسُولُ اللهِ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ يَا بَلالُ اذِنْ فِي النَّاسِ فَلْيَصُومُوا غَدًا
Explanation of the issue: In general, if the sky is not clear but there is cloud, dust, smoke, etc., then the sighting of the Ramadan moon is established by the testimony of one reliable person, whether that person is male or female, free or slave. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i in one of his two opinions have stipulated two reliable persons. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i say: Testimony regarding the Ramadan moon is a shahada (judicial testimony), and for shahada the number (two persons) is required, so for seeing the Ramadan moon two persons are required. Our proof is that this is a religious matter: this person gave news that the fasts of Ramadan have become obligatory on people, and it is clear that the obligation of fasts is a religious matter. For establishing a religious matter, reliability is required but number, freedom, and masculinity are not required, just as narrating hadith is a religious work. In narrating hadith, number is not required, nor freedom, nor masculinity; rather, the narration of hadith is accepted from one person, from a slave, and from a woman. Since sighting the moon is a religious matter, the word 'shahada' (testimony) is not required to establish it, i.e., it is not necessary to say 'I testify' or 'I bear witness' that I have seen the Ramadan moon, as in worldly matters the word shahada is necessary for giving testimony. As for the requirement of reliability, the reason is that in religious matters, the statement of a sinful person (fasiq) is not accepted. Question: If someone asks: Why did the author of Hidayah say 'non-accepted'? Why didn't he say 'rejected'? In other words, why did he use the word 'ghair maqbul' instead of 'mardud'? Answer: The answer is that the statement of a fasiq is not absolutely rejected; rather it remains pending. If after investigation his statement is found to be true, it is accepted; if found to be false, it is rejected. As Allah says: 'O you who believe! If a sinful person comes to you with news, investigate.' (Surah al-Hujurat, verse 6). In any case, regarding the moon of Ramadan, the statement of a fasiq will not be accepted; the imams and scholars are agreed on this. However, it is narrated from Imam Tahawi that the statement of one person about the Ramadan moon is accepted whether he is reliable or not. From this it appears that according to Imam Tahawi the statement of an unreliable person (i.e., fasiq) would be accepted. Yet according to Imam Tahawi himself, the statement of a fasiq is not accepted. The author of Hidayah, interpreting this statement of Imam Tahawi, said that by 'reliable' (adil) Imam Tahawi means one whose reliability and piety are well-known among the people, and by 'unreliable' (ghair adil) he means one who is not well-known among the people, but his condition is concealed and hidden. So by 'unreliable' he means one whose condition is concealed (mastur al-hal), not a fasiq. The conclusion is that according to Imam Tahawi, in narrating the moon, the statement of a person whose reliability is well-known among the people is accepted, and also the statement of one whose reliability is concealed is accepted, but the statement of one whose fisq (sinfulness) is publicly known is not accepted even according to Imam Tahawi. By 'obstacle' (illat) is meant that there is cloud, dust, smoke, etc. in the sky. The author of Hidayah says that the absolute nature of al-Quduri's statement 'the imam accepted the testimony of one reliable person' indicates that after repentance, the statement of one flogged for qadhf is also acceptable and valid in moon sighting, and this is the zahir al-riwayah, because giving testimony of seeing the moon is in reality a narration (khabar), not a testimony (shahada), and after repentance, since the flogged for qadhf becomes reliable, his statement in narrating the moon sighting will be accepted. Another proof is that Abu Bakra (may Allah be pleased with him), who was flogged for qadhf, after repentance, the Companions accepted his statement regarding moon sighting. (al-Kifayah) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the statement of the flogged for qadhf is not reliable in moon sighting. There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the statement of the flogged for qadhf in moon sighting will not be accepted, and his proof is that the news of moon sighting is in one respect a testimony, in the sense that acting on this news becomes obligatory after the judgment of a judge, and it is also specific to the court session, and reliability is required for the informant; all these things indicate that it is a testimony. And the testimony of the flogged for qadhf is not accepted even after repentance, as the Quran says: 'And never accept their testimony forever' (Surah al-Nur, verse 4), i.e., their testimony is not to be accepted, neither before repentance nor after. Imam Shafi'i, in one of his opinions, said that the sighting of the moon is established by the testimony of two persons. Against Imam Shafi'i, firstly, the proof we have already mentioned is a valid argument, that this is a religious matter, so it resembles the narration of hadith. Secondly, it is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that the testimony of one person for the sighting of the Ramadan moon is accepted. Thus the hadith: Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: A bedouin came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'I have seen the moon, meaning the moon of Ramadan.' He said, 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast tomorrow.'
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of witnesses required for the sighting of the Ramadan moon. The Hanafi ruling is that when the sky is not clear (due to clouds, dust, smoke, etc.), the sighting of the Ramadan moon is established by the testimony of one reliable person ('adl). This person may be male or female, free or slave. The condition is only that the person be 'adl (just and reliable). The Hanafi school argues that this is a religious matter (amr dini), not a judicial testimony (shahada). The proof is that it is similar to the narration of hadith, where one person, a slave, or a woman is accepted. The opposing view from Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i (in one of his two opinions) is that two reliable witnesses are required because they consider it a form of shahada (testimony). The Hanafi response distinguishes between ikhbar (news) and shahada (testimony). The passage then discusses the condition of 'adala (reliability), clarifying that a fasiq (sinful person) is not accepted, but the author of Hidayah explains that the statement of a fasiq is not absolutely rejected but is suspended pending investigation (citing Quran 49:6). A dispute with Imam Tahawi is resolved by interpreting 'unreliable' as 'mastur al-hal' (unknown condition) rather than fasiq. The passage then addresses the specific case of a person flogged for qadhf (false accusation of adultery) after repentance. The majority Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) is that after repentance, such a person becomes 'adl and his testimony for moon sighting is accepted because it is a narration, not a testimony. This is supported by the practice of the Companions with Abu Bakra. However, there is an opposing narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that even after repentance, the testimony of a flogged person for moon sighting is not accepted because it is considered a testimony (shahada) in one respect, and the Quran (24:4) states that their testimony is never accepted. The passage concludes by returning to the inter-madhhab dispute, providing the hadith of the bedouin (Ibn Abbas) as direct proof that the Prophet accepted the testimony of one person for the Ramadan moon. This hadith is the strongest evidence for the Hanafi position. The overall message is that moon sighting is a religious matter where one reliable witness suffices when the sky is not clear.

Key Terms
رؤیت ہلال (ru'yat al-hilal): The visual sighting of the new crescent moon marking the beginning of a lunar month, specifically for Ramadan and Shawwal.
عادل (‘adl): A person who is just, reliable, and avoids major sins and does not persist in minor sins; their testimony or report is acceptable.
شہادت (shahada): Judicial testimony given in court with specific formalities (e.g., number, wording, freedom, gender requirements).
فاسق (fasiq): A person who sins openly and does not repent; such a person's testimony or news is not accepted in religious matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when the sky is cloudy, how many witnesses are needed to establish the sighting of the Ramadan moon?
A) Two witnesses, both male
B) One reliable witness, regardless of gender or status
C) Two witnesses, one male and one female
D) No witness; calendar calculation suffices

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts one reliable witness for Ramadan moon sighting when the sky is not clear, based on the nature of moon sighting as a religious report.

The Flogged Witness: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Moon Sighting
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahdud fi al-qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on the acceptance of a mahdud fi al-qadhf's report for moon sighting after repentance, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The flogged for qadhf becomes reliable after repentance — his report on moon sighting is accepted as a narration, not as testimony.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a person who has been flogged for false accusation of adultery (mahdud fi al-qadhf) can have his report on moon sighting accepted after repentance. The majority Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) accepts it, while there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa rejecting it. We will explore the evidence on both sides and the practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the conflicting positions
The majority (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) accept the report of a flogged person after repentance for moon sighting. Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration that it is not accepted.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the majority proof
Moon sighting is a khabar, not shahada. After repentance, the person becomes 'adl, so his narration is accepted. The practice of Companions with Abu Bakra supports this.
The author of Hidayah says this is the zahir al-riwayah.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's narration
He considers it a testimony (shahada) in one respect because it requires a judge's announcement, and the Quran says their testimony is never accepted.
This is a minority view.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If the flogged witness repents, the majority accepts his report for moon sighting; the other view rejects it.
This affects whether the community fasts based on his report.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is the majority view (zahir al-riwayah). Ibn Abidin etc. follow this.
Al-Marghinani explicitly states it is the zahir al-riwayah.

عادل ہو گیا اس لئے رویت ہلال کی خبر دینے میں اس کا قول قبول ہوگا ۔ اور یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ ابو بکرۃ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ جو محدود فی القذف تھے تو بہ کر لینے کے بعد رؤیت ہلال میں صحابہ نے ان کے قول کو قبول کیا ہے۔ (الکفایہ) امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک رؤیت هلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول معتبر نہیں : امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ رؤیت هلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ رویت ہلال کی خبر من وجہ شہادت ہے بایں طور کہ اس خبر پر عمل کرنا قضاء قاضی کے بعد واجب ہوگا اور اس کا اختصاص بھی مجلس قضاء کے ساتھ ہے اور مخبر کے لئے عدالت کی شرط ہے یہ سب باتیں شہادت ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہیں اور محدود فی القذف کی شہادت تو بہ کے بعد بھی قبول نہیں کی جاتی چنانچہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ولا تُقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً اَبَدًا یعنی ان کی کوئی گواہی بھی نہ مانو یعنی نہ تو بہ سے پہلے اور نہ تو بہ کے بعد ۔ امام شافعی نے اپنے ایک قول میں جو یہ کہا ہے کہ رؤیت هلال دو آدمیوں کی شہادت سے ثابت ہوگی تو امام شافعی کے خلاف اولا تو وہ دلیل حجت ہے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے کہ یہ امر دینی ہے پس روایت احادیث کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے رمضان کے چاند کی رویت میں ایک آدمی کی شہادت کا قبول کرنا ثابت ہے چنانچہ حدیث ہے قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسِ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا جَاءَ أَعْرَابِيٌّ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ إِنِّي رَأَيْتُ الْهَلالَ يَعْنِي هَلالَ رَمَضَانَ فَقَالَ أَتَشْهَدُانْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ أَتَشْهَدَانُ مُحَمَّدًا رَّسُولُ اللهِ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ يَا بَلالُ اذِنْ فِي النَّاسِ فَلْيَصُومُوا غَدًا
Explanation of the issue: In general, if the sky is not clear but there is cloud, dust, smoke, etc., then the sighting of the Ramadan moon is established by the testimony of one reliable person, whether that person is male or female, free or slave. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i in one of his two opinions have stipulated two reliable persons. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i say: Testimony regarding the Ramadan moon is a shahada (judicial testimony), and for shahada the number (two persons) is required, so for seeing the Ramadan moon two persons are required. Our proof is that this is a religious matter: this person gave news that the fasts of Ramadan have become obligatory on people, and it is clear that the obligation of fasts is a religious matter. For establishing a religious matter, reliability is required but number, freedom, and masculinity are not required, just as narrating hadith is a religious work. In narrating hadith, number is not required, nor freedom, nor masculinity; rather, the narration of hadith is accepted from one person, from a slave, and from a woman. Since sighting the moon is a religious matter, the word 'shahada' (testimony) is not required to establish it, i.e., it is not necessary to say 'I testify' or 'I bear witness' that I have seen the Ramadan moon, as in worldly matters the word shahada is necessary for giving testimony. As for the requirement of reliability, the reason is that in religious matters, the statement of a sinful person (fasiq) is not accepted. Question: If someone asks: Why did the author of Hidayah say 'non-accepted'? Why didn't he say 'rejected'? In other words, why did he use the word 'ghair maqbul' instead of 'mardud'? Answer: The answer is that the statement of a fasiq is not absolutely rejected; rather it remains pending. If after investigation his statement is found to be true, it is accepted; if found to be false, it is rejected. As Allah says: 'O you who believe! If a sinful person comes to you with news, investigate.' (Surah al-Hujurat, verse 6). In any case, regarding the moon of Ramadan, the statement of a fasiq will not be accepted; the imams and scholars are agreed on this. However, it is narrated from Imam Tahawi that the statement of one person about the Ramadan moon is accepted whether he is reliable or not. From this it appears that according to Imam Tahawi the statement of an unreliable person (i.e., fasiq) would be accepted. Yet according to Imam Tahawi himself, the statement of a fasiq is not accepted. The author of Hidayah, interpreting this statement of Imam Tahawi, said that by 'reliable' (adil) Imam Tahawi means one whose reliability and piety are well-known among the people, and by 'unreliable' (ghair adil) he means one who is not well-known among the people, but his condition is concealed and hidden. So by 'unreliable' he means one whose condition is concealed (mastur al-hal), not a fasiq. The conclusion is that according to Imam Tahawi, in narrating the moon, the statement of a person whose reliability is well-known among the people is accepted, and also the statement of one whose reliability is concealed is accepted, but the statement of one whose fisq (sinfulness) is publicly known is not accepted even according to Imam Tahawi. By 'obstacle' (illat) is meant that there is cloud, dust, smoke, etc. in the sky. The author of Hidayah says that the absolute nature of al-Quduri's statement 'the imam accepted the testimony of one reliable person' indicates that after repentance, the statement of one flogged for qadhf is also acceptable and valid in moon sighting, and this is the zahir al-riwayah, because giving testimony of seeing the moon is in reality a narration (khabar), not a testimony (shahada), and after repentance, since the flogged for qadhf becomes reliable, his statement in narrating the moon sighting will be accepted. Another proof is that Abu Bakra (may Allah be pleased with him), who was flogged for qadhf, after repentance, the Companions accepted his statement regarding moon sighting. (al-Kifayah) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the statement of the flogged for qadhf is not reliable in moon sighting. There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the statement of the flogged for qadhf in moon sighting will not be accepted, and his proof is that the news of moon sighting is in one respect a testimony, in the sense that acting on this news becomes obligatory after the judgment of a judge, and it is also specific to the court session, and reliability is required for the informant; all these things indicate that it is a testimony. And the testimony of the flogged for qadhf is not accepted even after repentance, as the Quran says: 'And never accept their testimony forever' (Surah al-Nur, verse 4), i.e., their testimony is not to be accepted, neither before repentance nor after. Imam Shafi'i, in one of his opinions, said that the sighting of the moon is established by the testimony of two persons. Against Imam Shafi'i, firstly, the proof we have already mentioned is a valid argument, that this is a religious matter, so it resembles the narration of hadith. Secondly, it is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that the testimony of one person for the sighting of the Ramadan moon is accepted. Thus the hadith: Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: A bedouin came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'I have seen the moon, meaning the moon of Ramadan.' He said, 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast tomorrow.'
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of witnesses required for the sighting of the Ramadan moon. The Hanafi ruling is that when the sky is not clear (due to clouds, dust, smoke, etc.), the sighting of the Ramadan moon is established by the testimony of one reliable person ('adl). This person may be male or female, free or slave. The condition is only that the person be 'adl (just and reliable). The Hanafi school argues that this is a religious matter (amr dini), not a judicial testimony (shahada). The proof is that it is similar to the narration of hadith, where one person, a slave, or a woman is accepted. The opposing view from Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i (in one of his two opinions) is that two reliable witnesses are required because they consider it a form of shahada (testimony). The Hanafi response distinguishes between ikhbar (news) and shahada (testimony). The passage then discusses the condition of 'adala (reliability), clarifying that a fasiq (sinful person) is not accepted, but the author of Hidayah explains that the statement of a fasiq is not absolutely rejected but is suspended pending investigation (citing Quran 49:6). A dispute with Imam Tahawi is resolved by interpreting 'unreliable' as 'mastur al-hal' (unknown condition) rather than fasiq. The passage then addresses the specific case of a person flogged for qadhf (false accusation of adultery) after repentance. The majority Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) is that after repentance, such a person becomes 'adl and his testimony for moon sighting is accepted because it is a narration, not a testimony. This is supported by the practice of the Companions with Abu Bakra. However, there is an opposing narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that even after repentance, the testimony of a flogged person for moon sighting is not accepted because it is considered a testimony (shahada) in one respect, and the Quran (24:4) states that their testimony is never accepted. The passage concludes by returning to the inter-madhhab dispute, providing the hadith of the bedouin (Ibn Abbas) as direct proof that the Prophet accepted the testimony of one person for the Ramadan moon. This hadith is the strongest evidence for the Hanafi position. The overall message is that moon sighting is a religious matter where one reliable witness suffices when the sky is not clear.

Key Terms
محدود فی القذف (mahdud fi al-qadhf): A person who has been flogged (hadd) for falsely accusing someone of adultery (qadhf). Such a person's testimony is generally rejected even after repentance.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or authoritative transmission in the Hanafi school, referring to the soundest narrations from Abu Hanifa and his disciples, contained in the six major works of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwayah, what is the ruling on accepting the moon sighting report of a person flogged for qadhf after sincere repentance?
A) It is accepted because moon sighting is a khabar
B) It is rejected based on Quran 24:4
C) It is accepted only if two witnesses are present
D) It is rejected unless the person was not actually guilty

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position accepts the moon sighting report of a flogged for qadhf after repentance, as moon sighting is a khabar, not a shahada.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Fasting the 31st Day: Precaution vs. Subordinate Establishment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fasting after 30 days with one witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on fasting the 31st day of Ramadan when the moon is not sighted and evaluate the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
After 30 days of Ramadan, the next day is Eid even without moon sighting — subordinately established.

The month of Ramadan may be established by the testimony of a single reliable witness if the sky is cloudy. But what happens when thirty fasts are completed and the Shawwal moon is not sighted on the 30th evening? Should the community fast one more day out of precaution, or is Eid already established? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi debate between Imam Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, each with a distinct legal principle and analogous reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the question
Understand the factual situation: Ramadan was started based on one witness; thirty days have passed; on the 30th evening, no moon is sighted for Shawwal. The question: should the people fast the next day (31st) or break fast for Eid?
This is not a case of cloudy sky on the 30th; the moon is simply not sighted.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its proof
According to the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad, Abu Hanifa holds that the people should fast the 31st day out of precaution (ihtiyat). His proof: breaking the fast (Eid) cannot be established by a single witness; it requires at least two witnesses. Since only one witness testified for the start, the same witness cannot establish the end.
This is a nawadir narration, not from the zahir al-riwayah.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and its proof
Imam Muhammad holds that after completing thirty days, the people should break fast, even if the moon is not sighted. His proof: the day of Fitr is established subordinately (dhimnan) through the establishment of Ramadan. He uses the analogy of selling a pregnant goat: selling the fetus alone is invalid, but it becomes valid as part of selling the mother.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position and forms the basis of fatwa.
4
Analyze the qiyas analogy
Break down the analogy: asl = sale of pregnant goat (fetus valid only subordinately); far' = establishing Eid by one witness; illa = subordinate establishment; hukm = Eid is validly established. Understand why Abu Hanifa rejects this analogy: he argues that Eid requires independent proof, unlike a subordinate component of a contract.
The qiyas is of the shabahah type, based on resemblance rather than a clear illa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical application
The relied-upon position is Imam Muhammad's: if Ramadan started with one witness and thirty days have passed, the next day is Eid and fasting is haram. The precautionary view of Abu Hanifa is not followed in practice because the lunar month cannot exceed thirty days and the month is complete.
This ruling applies when the start was based on one witness; if two witnesses testified, the same principle applies but with stronger proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال : اب سوال یہ ہے کہ امام المسلمین نے ایک آدمی کی شہادت قبول کر کے رمضان کے روزے رکھنے کا اعلان کراد یالوگوں نے شہادت کے دن سے تیسویں (۳۰) روزے پورے کر لئے میں روزے کی شام کو چاند نظر نہ آیا تو اب لوگ اگلے دن افطار کریں یا روزہ رکھیں ۔ جواب: سو اس بارے میں حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت یہ ہے کہ احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ لوگ اکتیسویں دن بھی افطار نہ کریں ، بلکہ روزہ رکھیں گویا افطار نہ کرنے کا مدار احتیاط پر ہے اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر تمہیں روزے پورے کر کے افطار کا حکم دیدیا جائے تو یہ افطار ایک آدمی کی شہادت سے ثابت ہو گا یعنی جس آدمی کی گواہی سے پہلا روزہ رکھا تھا گویا اسی کی گواہی سے افطار ہوا، حالانکہ افطار ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ کم از کم دو آدمیوں کی گواہی ضروری ہے۔ اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ تمہیں روزے پورا کرنے کے بعد لوگ افطار کریں اگر چہ تیسویں روزے کی شام کو چاند نظر نہ آیا ہو اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ بسا اوقات شئی ضمنا ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ ابتداء ثابت نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ بکری کے حمل کی بیع ابتداء جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ بکری کے ضمن میں حمل کی بیع بھی ثابت اور جائز ہو جاتی ہے پس اسی طرح یوم فطر اگر چہ ابتداء ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا لیکن ثبوت رمضان کے ضمن میں ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے بایں طور کہ جب ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے رمضان کا ثبوت ہو گیا اور لوگوں نے پورے میں روزے رکھ لئے تو اگلا دن خود بخود دفطر کا دن ہوگا کیونکہ
Question: Now the question is: The imam of the Muslims accepted the testimony of one person and announced the Ramadan fasts. The people completed thirty fasts from the day of testimony. In the evening of the thirtieth fast, the moon was not sighted. So should the people break their fast the next day or fast? Answer: Regarding this, from Imam Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad, the narration is that precaution is that people should not break the fast on the thirty-first day, but should fast. That is, the basis of not breaking fast is precaution. Another proof is that if you are ordered to break fast after completing the fasts, then this breaking would be established by the testimony of one person. That is, the same person by whose testimony the first fast was kept, apparently by his testimony the breaking occurs, although breaking fast is not established by the testimony of one person; rather, at least two witnesses are necessary. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that after you complete the fasts, people should break the fast, even if the moon was not sighted on the evening of the thirtieth fast. The proof is that sometimes a thing is established subordinately even if it is not established initially. For example, selling the fetus of a goat is not initially valid, but the sale of the fetus becomes valid and permissible within the sale of the goat. Similarly, the day of Fitr, although not initially established by the testimony of one person, is established by the testimony of one person as subordinate to the establishment of Ramadan. That is, when Ramadan is established by the testimony of one person and the people have completed the fasts (i.e., thirty days), then the next day automatically becomes the day of Fitr because...
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the situation where the start of Ramadan was established by the testimony of one reliable witness (due to cloudy sky), and the people have completed thirty fasts. However, on the evening of the thirtieth day, the moon for Shawwal is not sighted. The question is whether the people should fast the next day (the thirty-first) or break the fast for Eid. Two positions are reported: (1) From Imam Abu Hanifa through Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration: precaution requires that the people should not break the fast but should continue fasting. The reasoning is that breaking the fast (Eid) would be based solely on the testimony of the same one person who testified for Ramadan, and Eid cannot be established by one witness; it requires at least two witnesses. Therefore, to avoid potential error, they should fast the 31st day. (2) From Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: the people should break the fast after completing thirty days, even if the moon was not sighted. His reasoning is that the day of Fitr (Eid) is established subordinately (dhimnan) through the establishment of Ramadan. When Ramadan is established by one witness, the month is considered to have started. Since the lunar month is either 29 or 30 days, when thirty days have passed, the next day is automatically the first of Shawwal. This is analogous to selling a pregnant goat: the sale of the fetus is not valid independently, but it becomes valid as part of the sale of the goat. Similarly, the proof of Fitr is not valid independently from one witness, but it becomes valid as a consequence of the proof of Ramadan. The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the implication is that since the month of Ramadan is thirty days when completed, the next day must be Eid even if the moon is not sighted, because the month cannot exceed thirty days. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Imam Muhammad's view, as it aligns with the hadith 'The month is twenty-nine days' and the principle that if the moon is not sighted on the 30th night, the month is completed as 30 days and the next day is Eid. However, the precautionary view of Abu Hanifa is also noted.

Key Terms
لافطار (al-iftaar): Breaking the fast, specifically on the day of Eid al-Fitr, which requires proper proof of the new moon.
ضمنا ثابت (dhimnan thabit): Established subordinately or incidentally, as a consequence of something else being established.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Precaution; the legal principle of preferring the safer option to avoid potential error or sin.
حمل کی بیع (bay' al-haml): The sale of the fetus (young) of an animal. In Hanafi law, selling the fetus alone is invalid, but it is valid as part of selling the mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, what should be done after completing 30 fasts if the Shawwal moon is not sighted on the 30th evening?
A) Fast the 31st day due to precaution
B) Break the fast because the day of Fitr is established subordinately
C) Wait for another night to sight the moon
D) Follow the testimony of two witnesses to break the fast

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when Ramadan is established by one witness and thirty days are completed, the next day is Eid even without moon sighting, based on the principle of subordinate establishment.

Accepting the Report of a Repentant Qadhf Convict for Moon Sighting
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the acceptability of a repentant qadhf convict's report for moon sighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah) on accepting the report of a repentant maḥdūd fī al-qadhf for moon sighting and explain the distinction between khabar and shahadah that underlies the ruling.

Core Idea
A repentant qadhf convict's report for moon sighting is accepted as a khabar, not testimony — the distinction saves the ruling.

This lesson examines a nuanced point within Hanafi fiqh: can a person who was punished for false accusation (qadhf) serve as a witness for the sighting of the Ramadan moon? The answer depends on whether we treat the report as testimony (shahadah) or as a religious report (khabar). The relied-upon Hanafi position accepts it after repentance, but Imam Abu Hanifa himself dissented. We will walk through the reasoning, the proofs, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and the act
The person is a maḥdūd fī al-qadhf (convicted of false accusation) who has repented. The act is reporting the sighting of the Ramadan crescent.
2
State the two Hanafi views
The Zahir al-Riwayah view (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) accepts the report after repentance. Imam Abu Hanifa rejects it even after repentance, equating it to testimony.
3
Analyze the khabar vs shahadah distinction
The Zahir al-Riwayah treats moon sighting as a khabar (religious report) akin to hadith narration, not shahadah (court testimony). Hence, the strict rules of testimony do not apply.
Key principle: moon sighting is a religious matter (amr dīnī), not a judicial matter.
4
Examine the proofs
For acceptance: the practice of the Companions with Abu Bakrah (ra). For rejection: Imam Abu Hanifa's analogy to testimony and Quran 24:4 that permanently bars testimony.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi tradition (Al-Hidayah) adopts the acceptance position as the operative ruling for fatwa, due to the strength of the khabar distinction.
This is the relied-upon view for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الصوم
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم توبہ کے بعد محدود فی القذف کا قول بھی رؤیت ہلال میں قابل قبول اور معتبر ہوگا اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے کیونکہ چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی دینا در حقیقت خبر ہے نہ کہ شہادت اور توبہ کے بعد چونکہ محدود فی القذف عادل ہو گیا اس لئے رویت ہلال کی خبر دینے میں اس کا قول قبول ہوگا ۔ اور یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ ابو بکرۃ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ جو محدود فی القذف تھے توبہ کر لینے کے بعد رؤیت ہلال میں صحابہ نے ان کے قول کو قبول کیا ہے۔ (الکفایہ)
امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک رؤیت ہلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول معتبر نہیں : امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ رؤیت ہلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ رویت ہلال کی خبر من وجہ شہادت ہے بایں طور کہ اس خبر پر عمل کرنا قضاء قاضی کے بعد واجب ہوگا اور اس کا اختصاص بھی مجلس قضاء کے ساتھ ہے اور مخبر کے لئے عدالت کی شرط ہے یہ سب باتیں شہادت ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہیں اور محدود فی القذف کی شہادت توبہ کے بعد بھی قبول نہیں کی جاتی چنانچہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ولا تُقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً اَبَدًا یعنی ان کی کوئی گواہی بھی نہ مانو یعنی نہ توبہ سے پہلے اور نہ توبہ کے بعد ۔
امام شافعی نے اپنے ایک قول میں جو یہ کہا ہے کہ رؤیت ہلال دو آدمیوں کی شہادت سے ثابت ہوگی تو امام شافعی کے خلاف اولا تو وہ دلیل حجت ہے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے کہ یہ امر دینی ہے پس روایت احادیث کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے رمضان کے چاند کی رویت میں ایک آدمی کی شہادت کا قبول کرنا ثابت ہے چنانچہ حدیث ہے قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا جَاءَ أَعْرَابِيٌّ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ إِنِّي رَأَيْتُ الْهَلالَ يَعْنِي هَلالَ رَمَضَانَ فَقَالَ أَتَشْهَدُانْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ أَتَشْهَدَانُ مُحَمَّدًا رَّسُولُ اللهِ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ يَا بَلالُ اذِنْ فِي النَّاسِ فَلْيَصُومُوا غَدًا ابن عباس کہتے ہیں ایک اعرابی نے دربار رسالت میں آکر عرض کیا کہ میں نے رمضان کا چاند دیکھا ہے آپ نے پوچھا کہ تو اللہ کے ایک ہونے کی شہادت دیتا ہے اس نے کہا جی ہاں، آپ نے پوچھا تو محمد کے رسول خدا ہونے کی شہادت دیتا ہے اس نے کہا کہ ہاں آپ نے فرمایا کہ بلال تم لوگوں کو بتلا دو کہ وہ کل آئندہ روزہ رکھیں اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رؤیت ہلال رمضان کے سلسلہ میں ایک آدمی کی خبر قبول کر لی جاتی ہے۔
سوال : اب سوال یہ ہے کہ امام المسلمین نے ایک آدمی کی شہادت قبول کر کے رمضان کے روزے رکھنے کا اعلان کراد یا لوگوں نے شہادت کے دن سے تیسویں (۳۰) روزے پورے کر لئے اور روزے کی شام کو چاند نظر نہ آیا تو اب لوگ اگلے دن افطار کریں یا روزہ رکھیں ۔
جواب: سو اس بارے میں حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت یہ ہے کہ احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ لوگ اکتیسویں دن بھی افطار نہ کریں ، بلکہ روزہ رکھیں گویا افطار نہ کرنے کا مدار احتیاط پر ہے اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر تمہیں روزے پورے کر کے افطار کا حکم دیدیا جائے تو یہ افطار ایک آدمی کی شہادت سے ثابت ہو گا یعنی جس آدمی کی گواہی سے پہلا روزہ رکھا تھا گویا اسی کی گواہی سے افطار ہوا، حالانکہ افطار ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ کم از کم دو آدمیوں کی گواہی ضروری ہے۔ اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ تمہیں روزے پورا کرنے کے بعد لوگ افطار کریں اگر چہ تیسویں روزے کی شام کو چاند نظر نہ آیا ہو اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ بسا اوقات شئی ضمنا ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ ابتداء ثابت نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ بکری کے حمل کی بیع ابتداء جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ بکری کے ضمن میں حمل کی بیع بھی ثابت اور جائز ہو جاتی ہے پس اسی طرح یوم فطر اگر چہ ابتداء ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا لیکن ثبوت رمضان کے ضمن میں ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے بایں طور کہ جب ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے رمضان کا ثبوت ہو گیا اور لوگوں نے پورے تیس روزے رکھ لئے تو اگلا دن خود بخود فطر کا دن ہوگا کیونکہ شریعت میں کوئی مہینہ تیس دن سے زیادہ کا نہیں ہوتا اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ دایہ یعنی ایک عورت نے گواہی دی کہ یہ بچہ فلاں کا ہے تو اس ایک عورت کی گواہی سے اس بچہ کا اس فلاں سے نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا اور ثبوت نسب کے ضمن میں استحقاق وراثت بھی ثابت ہو جائے گا یعنی ان دونوں باپ بیٹے میں وراثت جاری ہوگی باپ اپنے اس بیٹے کا وارث ہوگا اور بیٹا اپنے اس باپ کا وارث ہوگا حالانکہ ابتداء اگر کوئی اپنے وارث ہونے پر ایک گواہ پیش کرے تو قبول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ دو گواہ نہ ہوں ۔
Book of Fasting. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 3. After repentance, the statement of one punished for qadhf is also acceptable and reliable in sighting the crescent, and this is the Zahir al-Riwayah, because giving testimony of seeing the moon is in reality a report (khabar), not a testimony (shahadah). After repentance, since the one punished for qadhf becomes just, his report about sighting the crescent is accepted. And there is also the proof that Abu Bakrah (may Allah be pleased with him), who was punished for qadhf, after he repented, the Companions accepted his statement regarding sighting the crescent. (Al-Kifayah). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the statement of one punished for qadhf is not reliable for sighting the crescent: There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the statement of one punished for qadhf will not be accepted for sighting the crescent. He gave as proof that the report of sighting the crescent is in some respects like testimony, in that acting upon this report becomes obligatory after the judge's decree, and it is specific to the court, and justice is a condition for the reporter. All these indicate that it is testimony. And the testimony of one punished for qadhf is not accepted even after repentance, as the Qur'an says: 'And never accept their testimony' (24:4), meaning do not accept any testimony from them, neither before repentance nor after. Imam al-Shafi'i said in one of his opinions that sighting the crescent is established by the testimony of two men. Against Imam Shafi'i, firstly that proof which we have mentioned is evidence, that this is a religious matter and thus resembles narrating hadith. Secondly, it is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he accepted the testimony of one person for sighting the Ramadan crescent. The hadith: Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: A bedouin came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'I saw the crescent', meaning the crescent of Ramadan. He said, 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast tomorrow.' From this hadith it is known that in the matter of sighting the Ramadan crescent, the report of one person is accepted. Question: Now the question is: If the leader of the Muslims accepted the testimony of one person and announced that they should fast, and the people completed thirty fasts from the day of testimony, and on the evening of the thirtieth day the moon was not seen, should the people break the fast the next day or fast? Answer: Regarding this, Hasan ibn Ziyad reports from Imam Abu Hanifa that caution is that the people should not break the fast on the thirty-first day, but should fast. The basis of not breaking the fast is caution. Another proof is that if you are ordered to break the fast after completing the fasts, this breaking would be established by the testimony of one person, i.e., the same person whose testimony started the fast would be the one whose testimony breaks it, while breaking the fast is not established by the testimony of one person; rather, the testimony of at least two persons is required. And Imam Muhammad reports that after completing the fasts, the people should break the fast even if the moon was not seen on the evening of the thirtieth day. His proof is that sometimes a thing is established indirectly even if not directly established at the beginning. For example, the sale of a goat's fetus is not valid initially, but it becomes valid and established when included in the sale of the goat. Similarly, the day of Fitr, though not initially established by the testimony of one person, becomes established indirectly through the establishment of Ramadan by the testimony of one person. That is, when Ramadan is established by one person's testimony and the people have completed thirty fasts, the next day automatically becomes the day of Fitr because no month in Shariah exceeds thirty days. And this is like a midwife who testifies that this child belongs to so-and-so; by her testimony, the child's lineage to that person is established, and through that lineage, inheritance rights are also established, i.e., the father inherits from the son and the son from the father, even though if someone tried to prove his own inheritance with one witness, it would not be accepted because two witnesses are required.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on accepting the statement of a person who was punished for false accusation of adultery (hadd al-qadhf) when he reports sighting the Ramadan moon. The commentator clarifies the Hanafi position, noting that the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) accepts his report after repentance, because reporting the moon is a khabar (news), not a shahadah (testimony). A khabar does not require the stringent conditions of testimony; it is more like narrating a hadith. The author supports this with the example of Abu Bakrah, who was punished for qadhf but after repentance, the Companions accepted his report. However, Imam Abu Hanifa dissented, equating this report to testimony and citing the Quranic verse that permanently rejects their testimony. The author then defends the Hanafi position against Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires two witnesses. The author argues that moon sighting is a religious matter akin to hadith transmission, and provides the hadith of the bedouin whose single statement was accepted by the Prophet. The passage ends with an important ikhtilaf regarding the completion of thirty days: if the thirtieth night is cloudy, Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) advises caution (fast the thirty-first day), while Imam Muhammad holds that since Ramadan is already established, the thirty-first day is automatically Eid and fasting is not required. The commentary here explains the underlying principles: caution versus automatic inference (dalalah bi al-tab'iyyah). The author compares this to the sale of a pregnant animal (where the fetus is sold automatically) and the testimony of a midwife (through which lineage is established indirectly). Both analogies illustrate that what cannot be proven directly may be proven indirectly when it follows from an established matter.

Key Terms
محدود فی القذف (maḥdūd fī al-qadhf): A person who has been legally punished (hadd) for falsely accusing someone of fornication/adultery (qadhf).
رؤیت ہلال (ru’yat al-hilāl): The act of sighting the new moon (crescent) to determine the beginning of a lunar month, especially Ramadan and Shawwal.
خبر (khabar): A report or narration, as opposed to formal testimony (shahādah). In the context of this passage, it refers to the communication of the sighting being treated like a hadith narration rather than courtroom testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah of the Hanafi school, when is the report of a person punished for qadhf accepted for moon sighting?
A) Never, because the Quran permanently rejects their testimony.
B) Only if he repents and becomes just (ʿadl).
C) Only if he brings two witnesses with him.
D) Only for the sighting of Shawwal, not Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, moon sighting reports are khabar (religious reports) not shahadah (testimony), so a repentant qadhf convict's report is accepted after repentance.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
10 min
Number of Witnesses for Moon Sighting and the Ruling on Completing Thirty Days
Inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes on moon sighting evidence and the 30-day completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi proof for accepting one witness for moon sighting and distinguish the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on completing thirty days.

Core Idea
One witness suffices for Ramadan moon sighting; if the 30th night is cloudy, scholars differ on fasting the 31st day — caution vs. indirect proof.

This lesson explores two related debates. First, the inter-madhhab dispute: Do we need one or two witnesses to confirm the Ramadan moon? The Hanafi school relies on a hadith where the Prophet accepted a single bedouin's report. Second, an internal Hanafi debate: If the moon is not seen on the 30th night, do we fast the 31st day or break? Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) says continue out of caution; Imam Muhammad says break because the 31st day is automatically Eid. We will examine the proofs and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the inter-madhhab issue
Identify the dispute: Hanafi says one witness suffices; Shafi'i says two witnesses are required. Note the key evidence: the hadith of the bedouin.
2
Examine the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafi argument: moon sighting is a religious matter (amr dīnī), akin to hadith narration, not judicial testimony. The Prophet's practice provides direct Sunnah.
3
Address the intra-Hanafi dispute on the 31st day
If the crescent is not sighted on the evening of the 30th day of Ramadan, what should be done? Two narrations: from Imam Abu Hanifa (caution: fast the 31st) and from Imam Muhammad (break: it is automatically Eid).
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's proof of indirect establishment
Imam Muhammad argues that the day of Fitr is established indirectly (bil-istirāk) when Ramadan is established by one witness and 30 days are completed. He gives analogies: sale of a pregnant goat, midwife testimony for lineage.
This is called dalālah bi al-tabʿiyyah (ancillary indication).
5
Determine the practical outcome
The text does not give a clear tarjih between the two views. In practice, many follow the caution view (continue fasting), while others follow Imam Muhammad's view. The student should understand both proofs.

امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک رؤیت ہلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول معتبر نہیں : امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ رؤیت ہلال میں محدود فی القذف کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ رویت ہلال کی خبر من وجہ شہادت ہے بایں طور کہ اس خبر پر عمل کرنا قضاء قاضی کے بعد واجب ہوگا اور اس کا اختصاص بھی مجلس قضاء کے ساتھ ہے اور مخبر کے لئے عدالت کی شرط ہے یہ سب باتیں شہادت ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہیں اور محدود فی القذف کی شہادت توبہ کے بعد بھی قبول نہیں کی جاتی چنانچہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ولا تُقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً اَبَدًا یعنی ان کی کوئی گواہی بھی نہ مانو یعنی نہ توبہ سے پہلے اور نہ توبہ کے بعد ۔
امام شافعی نے اپنے ایک قول میں جو یہ کہا ہے کہ رؤیت ہلال دو آدمیوں کی شہادت سے ثابت ہوگی تو امام شافعی کے خلاف اولا تو وہ دلیل حجت ہے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے کہ یہ امر دینی ہے پس روایت احادیث کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے رمضان کے چاند کی رویت میں ایک آدمی کی شہادت کا قبول کرنا ثابت ہے چنانچہ حدیث ہے قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا جَاءَ أَعْرَابِيٌّ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ إِنِّي رَأَيْتُ الْهَلالَ يَعْنِي هَلالَ رَمَضَانَ فَقَالَ أَتَشْهَدُانْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ أَتَشْهَدَانُ مُحَمَّدًا رَّسُولُ اللهِ قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ يَا بَلالُ اذِنْ فِي النَّاسِ فَلْيَصُومُوا غَدًا ابن عباس کہتے ہیں ایک اعرابی نے دربار رسالت میں آکر عرض کیا کہ میں نے رمضان کا چاند دیکھا ہے آپ نے پوچھا کہ تو اللہ کے ایک ہونے کی شہادت دیتا ہے اس نے کہا جی ہاں، آپ نے پوچھا تو محمد کے رسول خدا ہونے کی شہادت دیتا ہے اس نے کہا کہ ہاں آپ نے فرمایا کہ بلال تم لوگوں کو بتلا دو کہ وہ کل آئندہ روزہ رکھیں اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رؤیت ہلال رمضان کے سلسلہ میں ایک آدمی کی خبر قبول کر لی جاتی ہے۔
سوال : اب سوال یہ ہے کہ امام المسلمین نے ایک آدمی کی شہادت قبول کر کے رمضان کے روزے رکھنے کا اعلان کراد یا لوگوں نے شہادت کے دن سے تیسویں (۳۰) روزے پورے کر لئے اور روزے کی شام کو چاند نظر نہ آیا تو اب لوگ اگلے دن افطار کریں یا روزہ رکھیں ۔
جواب: سو اس بارے میں حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت یہ ہے کہ احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ لوگ اکتیسویں دن بھی افطار نہ کریں ، بلکہ روزہ رکھیں گویا افطار نہ کرنے کا مدار احتیاط پر ہے اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر تمہیں روزے پورے کر کے افطار کا حکم دیدیا جائے تو یہ افطار ایک آدمی کی شہادت سے ثابت ہو گا یعنی جس آدمی کی گواہی سے پہلا روزہ رکھا تھا گویا اسی کی گواہی سے افطار ہوا، حالانکہ افطار ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ کم از کم دو آدمیوں کی گواہی ضروری ہے۔ اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ تمہیں روزے پورا کرنے کے بعد لوگ افطار کریں اگر چہ تیسویں روزے کی شام کو چاند نظر نہ آیا ہو اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ بسا اوقات شئی ضمنا ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ ابتداء ثابت نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ بکری کے حمل کی بیع ابتداء جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ بکری کے ضمن میں حمل کی بیع بھی ثابت اور جائز ہو جاتی ہے پس اسی طرح یوم فطر اگر چہ ابتداء ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا لیکن ثبوت رمضان کے ضمن میں ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے بایں طور کہ جب ایک آدمی کی گواہی سے رمضان کا ثبوت ہو گیا اور لوگوں نے پورے تیس روزے رکھ لئے تو اگلا دن خود بخود فطر کا دن ہوگا کیونکہ شریعت میں کوئی مہینہ تیس دن سے زیادہ کا نہیں ہوتا اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ دایہ یعنی ایک عورت نے گواہی دی کہ یہ بچہ فلاں کا ہے تو اس ایک عورت کی گواہی سے اس بچہ کا اس فلاں سے نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا اور ثبوت نسب کے ضمن میں استحقاق وراثت بھی ثابت ہو جائے گا یعنی ان دونوں باپ بیٹے میں وراثت جاری ہوگی باپ اپنے اس بیٹے کا وارث ہوگا اور بیٹا اپنے اس باپ کا وارث ہوگا حالانکہ ابتداء اگر کوئی اپنے وارث ہونے پر ایک گواہ پیش کرے تو قبول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ دو گواہ نہ ہوں ۔
Book of Fasting. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 3. After repentance, the statement of one punished for qadhf is also acceptable and reliable in sighting the crescent, and this is the Zahir al-Riwayah, because giving testimony of seeing the moon is in reality a report (khabar), not a testimony (shahadah). After repentance, since the one punished for qadhf becomes just, his report about sighting the crescent is accepted. And there is also the proof that Abu Bakrah (may Allah be pleased with him), who was punished for qadhf, after he repented, the Companions accepted his statement regarding sighting the crescent. (Al-Kifayah). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the statement of one punished for qadhf is not reliable for sighting the crescent: There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the statement of one punished for qadhf will not be accepted for sighting the crescent. He gave as proof that the report of sighting the crescent is in some respects like testimony, in that acting upon this report becomes obligatory after the judge's decree, and it is specific to the court, and justice is a condition for the reporter. All these indicate that it is testimony. And the testimony of one punished for qadhf is not accepted even after repentance, as the Qur'an says: 'And never accept their testimony' (24:4), meaning do not accept any testimony from them, neither before repentance nor after. Imam al-Shafi'i said in one of his opinions that sighting the crescent is established by the testimony of two men. Against Imam Shafi'i, firstly that proof which we have mentioned is evidence, that this is a religious matter and thus resembles narrating hadith. Secondly, it is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he accepted the testimony of one person for sighting the Ramadan crescent. The hadith: Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: A bedouin came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'I saw the crescent', meaning the crescent of Ramadan. He said, 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said, 'Yes.' He said, 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast tomorrow.' From this hadith it is known that in the matter of sighting the Ramadan crescent, the report of one person is accepted. Question: Now the question is: If the leader of the Muslims accepted the testimony of one person and announced that they should fast, and the people completed thirty fasts from the day of testimony, and on the evening of the thirtieth day the moon was not seen, should the people break the fast the next day or fast? Answer: Regarding this, Hasan ibn Ziyad reports from Imam Abu Hanifa that caution is that the people should not break the fast on the thirty-first day, but should fast. The basis of not breaking the fast is caution. Another proof is that if you are ordered to break the fast after completing the fasts, this breaking would be established by the testimony of one person, i.e., the same person whose testimony started the fast would be the one whose testimony breaks it, while breaking the fast is not established by the testimony of one person; rather, the testimony of at least two persons is required. And Imam Muhammad reports that after completing the fasts, the people should break the fast even if the moon was not seen on the evening of the thirtieth day. His proof is that sometimes a thing is established indirectly even if not directly established at the beginning. For example, the sale of a goat's fetus is not valid initially, but it becomes valid and established when included in the sale of the goat. Similarly, the day of Fitr, though not initially established by the testimony of one person, becomes established indirectly through the establishment of Ramadan by the testimony of one person. That is, when Ramadan is established by one person's testimony and the people have completed thirty fasts, the next day automatically becomes the day of Fitr because no month in Shariah exceeds thirty days. And this is like a midwife who testifies that this child belongs to so-and-so; by her testimony, the child's lineage to that person is established, and through that lineage, inheritance rights are also established, i.e., the father inherits from the son and the son from the father, even though if someone tried to prove his own inheritance with one witness, it would not be accepted because two witnesses are required.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on accepting the statement of a person who was punished for false accusation of adultery (hadd al-qadhf) when he reports sighting the Ramadan moon. The commentator clarifies the Hanafi position, noting that the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) accepts his report after repentance, because reporting the moon is a khabar (news), not a shahadah (testimony). A khabar does not require the stringent conditions of testimony; it is more like narrating a hadith. The author supports this with the example of Abu Bakrah, who was punished for qadhf but after repentance, the Companions accepted his report. However, Imam Abu Hanifa dissented, equating this report to testimony and citing the Quranic verse that permanently rejects their testimony. The author then defends the Hanafi position against Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires two witnesses. The author argues that moon sighting is a religious matter akin to hadith transmission, and provides the hadith of the bedouin whose single statement was accepted by the Prophet. The passage ends with an important ikhtilaf regarding the completion of thirty days: if the thirtieth night is cloudy, Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) advises caution (fast the thirty-first day), while Imam Muhammad holds that since Ramadan is already established, the thirty-first day is automatically Eid and fasting is not required. The commentary here explains the underlying principles: caution versus automatic inference (dalalah bi al-tab'iyyah). The author compares this to the sale of a pregnant animal (where the fetus is sold automatically) and the testimony of a midwife (through which lineage is established indirectly). Both analogies illustrate that what cannot be proven directly may be proven indirectly when it follows from an established matter.

Key Terms
رؤیت ہلال (ru’yat al-hilāl): The act of sighting the new moon (crescent) to determine the beginning of a lunar month, especially Ramadan and Shawwal.
شہادت (shahādah): Formal testimony in a court of law, requiring specific conditions like two witnesses or cross-examination.
خبر (khabar): A report or narration; in fiqh, a communication that does not require the strict conditions of shahadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many witnesses are needed to confirm the sighting of the Ramadan crescent?
A) One reliable witness.
B) Two reliable witnesses.
C) One male and one female.
D) Four witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts one trustworthy report for Ramadan moon sighting based on the Prophet's practice, and if the 30th night is cloudy, scholars differ on continuing or breaking the fast.

Witnesses for Moon Sighting: Clear vs. Cloudy Sky
Determines the number of witnesses needed when sky is clear vs overcast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the required number of witnesses for moon sighting based on sky conditions and apply the principle of achieving certainty (yaqin) to distinguish between clear and obstructed skies.

Core Idea
Moon sighting witness count depends on certainty: a large multitude in clear sky, one or two in cloudy, to avoid error.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical issue in moon sighting: how many witnesses are needed to confirm the crescent? The Hanafi school differentiates based on sky conditions—a principle rooted in avoiding suspicion of error. As you read, note how the jurists balance the need for certainty (yaqin) with practical possibilities, and how they use analogy (qiyas) to define 'multitude'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Find the statement that gives the ruling for a clear sky vs. an obstructed sky. Determine the number of witnesses required in each case.
The key phrase is 'إذا لم تكن بالسماء علة' vs. 'إذا كان بالسماء علة'.
2
Understand the 'illah (legal cause)
Note the reason given for requiring a large multitude in clear sky: 'التفرد بالرؤية في مثل هذه الحالة يوهم الغلط' (singular sighting in such a case raises suspicion of error). Identify how the cause changes when the sky is obstructed.
The 'illah is the potential for mistake, which is plausible in clear sky but unlikely in cloudy conditions.
3
Examine the definition of 'multitude'
The text presents different opinions on the minimum number for 'jam' kathīr': some say all residents of the locality (ahl al-mahalla), Abu Yusuf says fifty by qiyas on qasamah. Consider why each definition aims to achieve certainty.
Abu Yusuf's qiyas links the number to the fifty oaths in qasamah, which also involve a locality and certainty.
4
Explore additional views
Note the opinions of al-Tahawi and Kitab al-Istihsan: a single witness from outside the city or on an elevated place is accepted. Understand the reasoning: fewer obstacles reduce suspicion of error.
This shows the Hanafi method of istihsan (juristic preference) to accommodate special circumstances.
5
Apply the principle to a scenario
Using the framework from this passage, determine the evidentiary requirement for a moon sighting report on a partly cloudy night from a group of 10 residents. Consider which view applies and whether certainty is achieved.
The judge must assess the situation and decide if the number yields yaqin.

مطلع صاف ہو تو جم غفیر کی رؤیت معتبر ہوگی ایک کی گواہی قابل قبول نہیں ہوگی
وَإِذَا لَمْ تَكُن بِالسَّمَاءِ عِلَّةً لَمْ تُقْبَلِ الشَّهَادَةُ حَتَّى يَرَاهُ جَمْعُ كَثِيرُ يَقَعُ الْعِلْمُ بِخَبَرِهِمْ لِأَنَّ التَّفَرُّدَ بِالرُّؤْيَةِ فِي مِثْلِ هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ يُوهِمُ الْغَلَطَ فَيَجِبُ التَّوَقُفْ فِيهِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ جَمْعًا كَثِيرًا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ بِالسَّمَاءِ عَلَّةً لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَنْشَقُ الْغَيْمُ عَنْ مَوْضِعِ الْقَمَرِ فَيَتَّفِقُ لِلْبَعْضِ النَّظَرُ ثُمَّ قِيلَ فِى حَدِ الْكَثِيرِ أَهْلُ الْمَحَلَّةِ وَعَن أَبِى يُوسُفَ خَمْسُونَ رَجُلًا اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْقَسَامَةِ وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ أَهْلِ الْمِصْرِ وَمَنْ وَرَدَ مِنْ خَارِجَ الْمِصْرِ وَذَكَرَ الصَّحَاوِيُّ أَنَّهُ تُقْبَلُ شَهَادَةَ الْوَاحِدِ إِذَا جَاءَ مِنْ خَارِجِ الْمِصْرِ لِقِلَّةِ الْمَوَانِعِ وَإِلَيْهِ الْإِشَارَةُ فِى كِتَابِ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ عَلَى مَكَانٍ مُرْتَفَع فِي الْمِصْرِ
ترجمہ اور جب آسمان میں کوئی علت نہ ہو تو گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی یہاں تک کہ اس کو ایسی جماعت کثیر ہ دیکھے جسکی خبر سے یقین حاصل ہو جائے کیونکہ اس جیسی حالت میں رویت ہلال میں منفرد و نا غلطی کا وہم پیدا کرتا ہے پس اس میں توقف واجب ہوگا یہاں تک کہ دیکھنے والی جماعت کثیرہ ہو برخلاف اس کے جبکہ آسمان میں کوئی علت ہو کیونکہ اب ابر چاند کی جگہ سے پھٹ جاتا ہے تو بعض کی نظر ( اس پر ) پڑ جاتی ہے پھر کثیر کی مقدار میں کہا گیا کہ اہل محلہ ہیں اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ پچاس آدمی ہیں قسامت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور کوئی فرق نہیں کہ وہ لوگ اہل مصر ہوں یا وہ ہوں جو باہر سے آئے ہیں۔ اور امام طحاوی نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ ایک ہی شخص کی گواہی قبول ہوگی جبکہ وہ باہر سے آیا ہو، کیونکہ وہاں موانع کم ہیں اور اسی کی طرف کتاب الاستحسان میں اشارہ ہے اور یونہی جب چاند دیکھنے والا شہر میں کسی بلند جگہ پر ہو ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر آسمان پر ابر ، غبار وغیرہ نہ ہو بلکہ مطلع بالکل صاف ہو تو رؤیت ہلال میں اتنی بڑی جماعت کی گواہی قبول ہوگی جن کی خبر سے چاند دیکھنے کا یقین حاصل ہو جائے کیونکہ مطلع صاف ہونے کی صورت میں فقط ایک دو آدمی کا چاند دیکھنا اور باقی کا نہ دیکھنا غلطی کا وہم پیدا کرتا ہے یعنی یہ وہم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر چاند ہوتا تو اوروں کو بھی نظر آتا پس ایسا معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ان ایک دو کو چاند کے دیکھنے میں غلطی واقع ہو گئی ہے ہاں اگر آسمان پر ابر ہو تو ایک دو کی گواہی بھی قبول کر لی جائے گی کیونکہ ابر کی صورت میں کبھی ایسا ہوتا ہے چاند کی جگہ سے ابر پھٹ گیا اور کسی ایک کی نظر چاند پر پڑ گئی اور ابر پھر باہم مل گیا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ کثیر کی مقدار کیا ہے تو بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ کثیر سے مراد محلہ کے تمام لوگ ہیں یعنی پورے محلہ کے لوگوں نے چاند دیکھا تو رؤیت ثابت ہو جائے گی اور امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ کثیر سے مراد پچاس آدمی ہیں امام ابو یوسف نے اس کو قسامت پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی محلہ میں اگر کوئی مقتول پایا گیا اور قاتل معلوم نہیں ہے تو محلہ کے پچاس افراد سے لاعلمی پر قسم کی جاتی ہے پس جس طرح
If the sky is clear, the sighting of a large multitude will be credible; the testimony of one will not be accepted. And when there is no obstruction (cloud) in the sky, the testimony is not accepted unless a large multitude sees it, from whose report certainty is obtained, because being singular in sighting in such a case creates suspicion of error, so it is necessary to stop (suspend judgment) until there is a large multitude. Unlike when there is an obstruction in the sky, because the cloud may split from the position of the moon and some happen to look at it. Then it was said regarding the limit of 'multitude': the residents of the locality. And from Abu Yusuf: fifty men, drawing analogy from qasamah (oath of compurgation). And there is no difference whether they are residents of the city or those who came from outside the city. Al-Tahawi mentioned that the testimony of one is accepted if he comes from outside the city due to fewer obstacles, and this is indicated in Kitab al-Istihsan. Likewise, if he is on an elevated place in the city. Translation: And when there is no obstruction in the sky, the testimony will not be accepted until he is seen by a large multitude from whose report certainty is attained, because in such a state, being singular in moon sighting creates suspicion of error, so stopping (judgment) is obligatory until the seeing multitude is large. Contrary to when there is an obstruction in the sky, because then the cloud splits from the moon's position and some happen to see it. Then regarding the quantity of 'multitude', it was said: it is the residents of the locality. And from Abu Yusuf: fifty men, measured by qasamah. And there is no difference whether they are residents of the city or those who come from outside. And Imam Tahawi mentioned that the testimony of a single person is accepted if he comes from outside the city due to fewer obstacles, and this is indicated in Kitab al-Istihsan. Similarly, if the seer is on an elevated place in the city. Explanation: The ruling is that if the sky is clear without clouds or dust, the testimony of such a large crowd is accepted that their report yields certainty of moon sighting. Because in a clear sky, only one or two persons seeing the moon while others do not creates suspicion of error, i.e., it seems likely that those one or two made a mistake. However, if there is cloud cover, then the testimony of one or two is accepted because in such a situation sometimes the cloud parts over the moon and one or two happen to see it, and then the cloud closes again. As for the definition of 'multitude', some scholars said it means all the residents of the locality: if all the people of the locality see the moon, the sighting is established. And Imam Abu Yusuf narrated that 'multitude' means fifty men, drawing analogy from qasamah, i.e., if a murdered person is found in a locality and the killer is unknown, fifty people from the locality take an oath of ignorance. So just as...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on the number of witnesses required for moon sighting, conditioned by the state of the sky. The commentator distinguishes between a clear sky and an overcast sky. If the sky is clear and without any obstruction, the testimony of one or two persons is not accepted because it raises suspicion of error; rather, a large multitude that brings certainty is required. If the sky is cloudy or otherwise obstructed, the testimony of one or two trustworthy persons is accepted because the obstruction explains why only a few saw it. The commentator then discusses the definition of 'multitude' (jamʿ kathīr). According to some scholars, it means all the residents of the locality (ahl al-mahalla). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, it means fifty men, by analogy with the qasamah (oath of compurgation) where fifty oaths are required from the locality in cases of found murder. The commentator notes that Imam Tahawi held a different opinion: if a person comes from outside the city (where there are fewer obstructions), his single testimony is accepted, and this is supported by Kitab al-Istihsan. Similarly, if the seer is in an elevated place within the city, his single testimony is accepted due to the clarity of view. The explanation further clarifies that the underlying reason (‘illah) is the suspicion of error: in a clear sky, if one person claims to see the moon while others do not, it is likely a mistake; thus, a large number yields certainty. In cloudy conditions, the possibility that only a few glimpsed the moon is plausible, so their testimony is accepted. The qiyas on qasamah shows that the number fifty is derived from a similar oath-based procedure in blood money cases.

Key Terms
جم غفیر (jamʿ ghafīr): A large multitude whose combined report yields certainty (yaqin) of the event.
علت (ʿillah): An obstruction in the sky (like clouds, dust, fog) that could prevent the moon from being visible to everyone.
قسامت (qasāmah): A legal procedure where fifty men from a locality take oaths denying knowledge of a murder, to avoid blood money liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on accepting a single person's testimony for moon sighting if the sky is completely clear?
A) It is accepted unconditionally.
B) It is not accepted unless there is an obstruction like clouds.
C) It is accepted only if the person is from outside the city.
D) It is accepted only if the person is a judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a large multitude for moon sighting in clear skies to eliminate suspicion of error, but accepts fewer witnesses when the sky is obstructed.

Moon Sighting Testimony: Number of Witnesses Required
Ruling on number requirements for moon sighting testimony based on sky condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of witnesses required for moon sighting testimony in clear vs. cloudy conditions according to the Hanafi school, and identify the intra-Hanafi differences in defining 'a large crowd'.

Core Idea
Moon sighting testimony requires a large crowd when the sky is clear; in clouds or from outside city, a single witness may suffice.

In the Hanafi school, accepting moon sighting testimony depends on whether the sky is clear or obstructed. This lesson unpacks the ruling from Al-Hidayah, explaining why a large crowd is needed for certainty and how scholars defined 'large crowd'. You will learn the general rule, the analogy to qasama, and the exceptional views of Imam al-Tahawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The text states that when the sky is clear (no cloud), testimony is not accepted until a large crowd sees the moon such that their report brings certainty.
This is the default rule.
2
Understand the reason
The reason (ta'lil) is that a single person or few people sighting the moon in a clear sky gives the impression of error (tawahhum al-ghalat), so we must pause until a large group reports.
Certainty (yaqeen) is the goal.
3
Distinguish the cloud condition
When there is a cloud ('illah), a single person's testimony may be accepted because the moon could become briefly visible through a gap, so the sighting is plausible.
This is the exception.
4
Examine definitions of kathir
The text discusses what constitutes a 'large crowd': some say all residents of the locality; Abu Yusuf says 50 men by analogy with qasama; al-Tahawi says a single witness from outside the city or on high ground is accepted due to fewer obstacles.
These are intra-madhhab differences.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
The mufta bihi (operative position) generally requires a large crowd in clear sky, but Tahawi's view provides a practical option in certain scenarios, allowing flexibility.
Reference to Kitab al-Istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا لَمْ تَكُن بِالسَّمَاءِ عِلَّةً لَمْ تُقْبَلِ الشَّهَادَةُ حَتَّى يَرَاهُ جَمْعُ كَثِيرُ يَقَعُ الْعِلْمُ بِخَبَرِهِمْ لِأَنَّ التَّفَرُّدَ بِالرُّؤْيَةِ فِي مِثْلِ هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ يُوهِمُ الْغَلَطَ فَيَجِبُ التَّوَقُفْ فِيهِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ جَمْعًا كَثِيرًا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ بِالسَّمَاءِ عَلَّةً لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَنْشَقُ الْغَيْمُ عَنْ مَوْضِعِ الْقَمَرِ فَيَتَّفِقُ لِلْبَعْضِ النَّظَرُ ثُمَّ قِيلَ فِى حَدِ الْكَثِيرِ أَهْلُ الْمَحَلَّةِ وَعَن أَبِى يُوسُفَ خَمْسُونَ رَجُلًا اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْقَسَامَةِ وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ أَهْلِ الْمِصْرِ وَمَنْ وَرَدَ مِنْ خَارِجَ الْمِصْرِ وَذَكَرَ الصَّحَاوِيُّ أَنَّهُ تُقْبَلُ شَهَادَةَ الْوَاحِدِ إِذَا جَاءَ مِنْ خَارِجِ الْمِصْرِ لِقِلَّةِ الْمَوَانِعِ وَإِلَيْهِ الْإِشَارَةُ فِى كِتَابِ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ عَلَى مَكَانٍ مُرْتَفَع فِي الْمِصْرِ
And when there is no cloud in the sky, the testimony is not accepted until a large crowd sees it such that knowledge is attained by their report, because being alone in sighting in such a situation gives the impression of error, so one must pause until it is a large crowd, contrary to when there is a cloud in the sky, because the cloud may split from the place of the moon and therefore sighting occurs for some individuals. Then it was said regarding the limit of 'kathir' that it is the people of the locality, and from Abu Yusuf it is fifty men by analogy with qasama. And there is no difference between the people of the city and those who come from outside the city. And al-Tahawi mentioned that the testimony of a single person is accepted if he comes from outside the city due to fewer obstacles, and there is indication of this in Kitab al-Istihsan. Similarly, if he is on an elevated place within the city.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal ruling on the admissibility of moon sighting testimony based on weather conditions. It states that when the sky is clear, a single or few individuals' testimony is not accepted because it raises the probability of error. Instead, a large gathering (jam' kathir) whose report brings certainty is required. This is because in such conditions, if the moon were present, many would see it. When there is a cloud cover, a single person's testimony may be accepted because the moon could be briefly visible through a gap in the clouds. The text then discusses the definition of 'kathir': some say it means all residents of the locality; Abu Yusuf analogizes it to the fifty men required for qasama (oath of innocence in blood money cases). Imam al-Tahawi holds that a single witness from outside the city is accepted due to fewer visual obstacles (like smoke and dust), and similarly if the witness is on a high place within the city. This view is referenced in Kitab al-Istihsan.

Key Terms
جماعة كثيرة (jamā‘ah kathīrah): A large group of people whose report brings certainty of knowledge regarding moon sighting
علة (‘illah): A cloud, dust, or any obstruction in the sky that prevents seeing the moon
قسامة (qasāmah): An oath taken by fifty men of a locality to deny involvement in a murder

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following correctly reflects the Hanafi ruling on moon sighting testimony?
A) In all cases, the testimony of two men is required.
B) In clear sky, a large crowd is needed; in cloudy sky, one person's testimony may suffice.
C) Only fifty men can testify.
D) No testimony is accepted unless confirmed by astronomy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a large crowd for moon sighting in clear skies to ensure certainty, but accepts individual testimony in obstructed conditions or from outside the city.

Sawm — Fasting

Ruling on One Who Alone Sees the Crescent of Eid al-Fitr
Ruling that a person who alone sees the Eid al-Fitr moon should not break fast out of caution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who alone sees the Eid al-Fitr crescent and explain the principle of ihtiyat (caution) that governs it.

Core Idea
One who alone sees the Eid moon must continue fasting until official confirmation.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a person sights the crescent of Shawwal on the 29th of Ramadan but no one else confirms it. Should he break his fast? The Hanafi school, emphasizing caution in acts of worship, rules that he must continue fasting. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate the importance of legal certainty (yaqīn) and the role of official testimony in establishing the end of Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the situation: a person alone sees the crescent of Eid al-Fitr (the moon that ends Ramadan).
The sighting is solitary, meaning no other witness corroborates it.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that he should not break his fast; he must continue fasting out of caution.
This is a wajib (obligatory) precaution, not a mere recommendation.
3
Understand the reasoning
The principle is 'ihtiyat' (caution) in matters of fasting: caution lies in upholding the obligation (wujub) until certainty is established through acceptable testimony.
His personal sighting does not constitute legal certainty for breaking the fast.
4
Note the consequence if violated
If he breaks his fast based on his own sighting, his fast is invalid and he must make it up (qada), but no kaffarah (expiation) is required because he acted on a valid personal belief.
Kaffarah is only due when fasting is deliberately broken without any valid excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ رَأَى هِلَالَ الْفِطْرِ وَحْدَهُ لَمْ يُفْطِرُ احْتِيَاطًا وَ فِي الصَّوْمِ الْاِحْتِيَاطُ فِي الْإِيجَابِ
And whoever sees the crescent of al-Fitr alone should not break his fast out of caution, and in the matter of fasting, caution lies in making it obligatory.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This is a concise legal ruling about a person who alone witnesses the crescent of Eid al-Fitr (at the end of Ramadan). The ruling is that he should not break his fast (i.e., should not consider Ramadan ended) but should continue fasting out of precaution. The reasoning is that in matters of fasting, the principle of caution (ihtiyat) is to uphold the obligation (wujub) of fasting until certainty of the new moon is established through acceptable testimony. If he does break the fast based on his own sighting, he must make up that day (qada) but no kaffarah is required because the sighting is not legally established for others. This rule applies regardless of whether the sky is clear or cloudy.

Key Terms
احتياطًا (iḥtiyāṭan): Acting cautiously to avoid violating the obligation of fasting

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he alone sees the crescent of Eid al-Fitr?
A) Break his fast immediately
B) Continue fasting out of caution
C) Tell others and all break fast
D) Break fast and give kaffarah

Key Takeaway
A solitary sighting of the Eid crescent does not permit breaking fast; caution requires continuing fasting until official confirmation.
